# Implementation Plan for loopx Test Harness

**Status: ADR-0004 §6.1 (project-root cwd + LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR injection + cwd-isolation across goto / loop-reset on Bash + JS/TS), §6.2 (absolute `/bin/bash` invocation + missing-executable-bit support), §6.3 (CommonJS rejection at execution time across all four JS/TS extensions × all three CJS forms — esbuild integration in loader-hook with deliberately-omitted `format` option to skip CJS-wrapper auto-injection), §7.2 (first-trigger-wins surfaced-outcome under racing terminals — CLI signal-handler fix + new `firstObservedRef` shared trigger-tracking slot threaded between run.ts wrapper and runLoop), §7.4 (LOOPX_TMPDIR creation/injection/cleanup + parent-snapshot timing across all four injection tiers + run-setup non-reaping + renamed-away ENOENT silence + symlink-replacement cleanup-rule-2 surface-parity + regular-file-replacement cleanup-rule-3 surface-parity + mismatched-directory cleanup-rule-5 surface-parity + nested-symlink-recursive-walk cleanup-rule-4 surface-parity + FIFO/socket/hard-link cleanup-rule-3 generic-dispatch coverage + lstat-fail / symlink-unlink-fail / recursive-remove-fail cleanup-failure surface-parity + cleanup-warning-does-not-mask-script-error surface-parity + cleanup-fault-warning-does-not-mask-script-error surface-parity + cleanup-warning-does-not-mask signal/abort terminal surface-parity + cleanup-fault-warning-does-not-mask-CLI-signal terminal surface (T-TMP-42c — closes the cleanup-failure × signal × CLI diagonal) + cleanup-fault-warning-does-not-mask-abort-terminal surface (T-TMP-42b — closes the cleanup-failure × abort × programmatic surfaces diagonal) + cleanup idempotence under racing SIGINT→SIGTERM at the cleanup-start window for rule-3 and rule-5 branches, and (T-TMP-38f cleanup idempotence under racing SIGTERM→SIGINT — inverted-order parity), and (T-TMP-38a first-observed-wins under racing abort → .return() during cleanup-start on the run() programmatic surface), and (T-TMP-38a2 first-observed-wins inverted-order parity — racing .return() → abort during cleanup-start on the run() programmatic surface), and (T-TMP-38b/T-TMP-38b-run first-observed-wins under racing non-zero-script-exit → abort during cleanup-start, runPromise() and run() surfaces — test-only iteration; existing run.ts wrapper + runLoop try/finally already conformed), and (T-TMP-38c first-observed-wins under racing abort → .throw() during cleanup-start on the run() surface — the .throw()-axis companion to T-TMP-38a, completing the abort-first × consumer-cancellation matrix at the cleanup-start window — test-only iteration), and (T-TMP-38c2 first-observed-wins inverted-order parity — racing .throw() → abort during the new `consumer-throw-observed` window seam on the run() surface — implementation iteration: introduced shared `test-seams.ts` helper for the §1.4 `LOOPX_TEST_TERMINAL_TRIGGER_PAUSE` mechanic and added the `consumer-throw-observed` window value at the wrapper.throw entry of run.ts), and (T-TMP-38d3 first-observed-wins under racing post-final-yield .return() → abort during the new `consumer-return-observed` window seam on the run() surface, parameterized over `(stop)` and `(maxIterations)` final-yield triggers — wired the `consumer-return-observed` window value at the wrapper.return entry of run.ts, mirroring the `consumer-throw-observed` placement), and (T-TMP-38d2 first-observed-wins under racing post-final-yield .throw() → abort during the `consumer-throw-observed` window seam on the run() surface, parameterized over `(stop)` and `(maxIterations)` final-yield triggers — test-only iteration; existing seam wiring at wrapper.throw line 461 naturally handles the post-final-yield × abort-not-observed branch through the same `!abortObservedFirst` gate that fires on mid-loop .throw()), and (T-TMP-38b2/T-TMP-38b2-run first-observed-wins under racing abort → non-zero-script-exit during the new `abort-listener` window seam on the runPromise() and run() surfaces — implementation iteration: introduced the `firstObservedRef` shared slot, wired the `abort-listener` seam at the user-signal listener (which now async-defers `internalAc.abort()` when the seam is active to keep the active child alive during the bounded pause, qualifying §1.4 form (a)), and refactored every `internalAc.signal.aborted` first-observed check in run.ts (.return / .throw / asyncDispose / wrapper.next() catch) to consult `firstObservedRef.trigger === "abort"` instead so the seam-deferred dispatch does not leave first-observed determination wedged on a stale clock; runLoop now pins `"iteration"` before each iteration-level throw so a racing abort observed later cannot reclassify the outcome as abort)), §9.5 (RunOptions.env tier-2 env merging), §9.3 (abort-after-final-yield carve-out), §9.2 (LOOPX_TMPDIR async creation under runPromise()), AND §9.2 (process.env eager snapshot under runPromise()) are now IMPLEMENTED. Recent (this iteration): introduced new SPEC infrastructure for the §7.2 first-observed-wins contract that decouples first-observed determination from `internalAc.signal.aborted` (which the new `abort-listener` seam delays). Specifically: added `FirstObservedRef` shared-state interface in `loop.ts`, wired a single `firstObservedRef = { trigger: null }` slot per run() call in `run.ts` that is pinned to `"abort"` by the user-signal listener at entry, `"iteration"` by `runLoop` before each iteration-level throw (script-failure / goto errors), or `"consumer"` by the wrapper's `.return()` / `.throw()` / `[Symbol.asyncDispose]` when consumer cancellation acts as the first observed trigger. The user-signal listener now async-defers `internalAc.abort()` when `NODE_ENV=test` AND `LOOPX_TEST_TERMINAL_TRIGGER_PAUSE === "abort-listener"`, keeping the active child alive (TEST-SPEC §1.4 form (a)) while the bounded ~3s pause runs and a parent harness can race a second terminal trigger into the still-paused dispatch. The `wrapper.next()` catch now surfaces `makeAbortError(...)` whenever `firstObservedRef.trigger === "abort"`, regardless of what error reached it from runLoop — this is what produces the abort-error surfacing under T-TMP-38b2 / T-TMP-38b2-run when the script's SIGUSR1-driven `exit 1` reached runLoop first as a script-failure but abort had already been pinned as first-observed by the listener. Authored T-TMP-38b2 (runPromise) and T-TMP-38b2-run (run) — bash fixture installs a `trap 'exit 1' USR1`, writes its own PID to a marker, replaces the tmpdir with the rule-3 regular-file replacement, then `sleep 30 & wait`s. Driver code calls `ac.abort()` first (pins firstObservedRef to "abort", schedules the abort-listener pause), then polls the parent-observable pause marker, then sends `SIGUSR1` to the script's process group (`process.kill(-pid, "SIGUSR1")`) so the racing iteration error fires while loopx is still paused. Asserts: (a) errName === "AbortError" and errMessage does NOT match `/exited with code/` (load-bearing — a buggy wrapper.next() catch that surfaced the iteration error directly without consulting firstObservedRef would shift this), (b) exactly one cleanup warning (per-run cardinality holds across racing triggers), (c) rule-3 regular-file replacement at the recorded path survives. 1 ID × 2 surfaces × 2 runtimes = 4 tests. tmpdir.test.ts: 541/541 (was 537, +4). Adjacent suites: programmatic-api + env-vars + wfdir + loop-state + execution (635/635) zero regressions; signals (9/9) zero regressions; unit + harness (158/158) zero regressions. Most-recent iteration (T-TMP-38d / T-TMP-38d4): authored 8 tests (2 IDs × 2 final-yield variants × 2 runtimes) closing the post-final-yield abort-first × consumer-cancellation matrix at the abort-listener seam. Test-only iteration; the wrapper's existing post-final-yield abort branch (`firstObservedRef.trigger === "abort"` + `surfacePostFinalYieldAbort`) already conformed for both `.throw()` and `.return()` consumer methods. Bash fixture writes rule-3 regular-file replacement + emits final yield (`{"stop":true}` for variant (stop), raw `{}` for variant (maxIterations)) + exits 0; driver `await gen.next()`s the final yield, calls `ac.abort()` FIRST (pins firstObservedRef + schedules abort-listener seam pause), polls pause marker, then races `gen.throw()` (T-TMP-38d) or `gen.return()` (T-TMP-38d4) during the bounded pause. Asserts: (a) errName === "AbortError" (the abort outcome is the surfaced terminal outcome — racing consumer cancellation does NOT displace it; for T-TMP-38d the consumer-supplied "test-throw" message also does NOT appear; for T-TMP-38d4 returnDone is false — no clean settlement), (b) exactly one cleanup warning, (c) rule-3 file persists with content `regular-file-replacement`. tmpdir.test.ts: 561/561 (was 553, +8). Most-recent iteration (T-TMP-38e / T-TMP-38e-run): wired two new TEST-SPEC §1.4 seam windows in `execution.ts` (`child-spawn-attempt` BEFORE `spawn()` and `child-spawn-failure` AFTER catching the spawn rejection), threaded `firstObservedRef` through `ExecOptions` so spawn failures pin `trigger = "iteration"` before the seam pause, and gated `runLoop`'s `abortPromise` to NOT reject when `firstObservedRef.trigger === "iteration"` so a racing abort during a spawn-failure pause cannot displace the iteration outcome via `Promise.race`. Fixture pattern (modeled after T-TMP-08a / T-TMP-08c concurrent-runs): two distinct workflows `alpha` and `beta` colocated under the same project's `.loopx/` directory, each `index.sh` observes `MYVAR` into a caller-supplied marker via `printf '%s' "$MYVAR" > "$X_MARKER"`, then waits for a caller-supplied release file (`while [ ! -f "$X_RELEASE" ]; do sleep 0.05; done`), then emits `{"stop":true}`. Driver issues both `runPromise()` / `run()` calls without awaiting (so they overlap), polls until both markers exist (proves both scripts have spawned and observed MYVAR — the runs genuinely overlap rather than serializing), then writes both release files, then awaits/drains both runs. Asserts: (a) alphaCount === 1 and betaCount === 1 — both scripts ran exactly once (load-bearing — distinguishes overlapping from serialized execution); (b) alpha marker reads `"alpha-value"` and beta marker reads `"beta-value"` — each call's `RunOptions.env` reached its own child intact; (c) cross-contamination assertions — alpha marker !== `"beta-value"` and beta marker !== `"alpha-value"` — catches a buggy shared-mutable-state implementation that would route the second call's env over the first call's spawn (or vice versa) under interleaved execution. The marker-then-release handshake is what makes the overlap rigorous: a buggy implementation that snapshots into a shared module-level slot would still fail the cross-contamination asserts because both scripts have already observed their respective MYVAR values into markers BEFORE either is allowed to settle. programmatic-api.test.ts: 644/644 (was 640, +4). Test-only iteration; the existing `snapshotOptions` (run.ts:105-232) reads `opts.signal` FIRST at line 132 (with try/catch + isAbortSignalCompatible check + `snap.signal = signalRaw`), then reads later fields (`opts.cwd` line 152, `opts.envFile` line 176, `opts.env` line 193, `opts.maxIterations` line 209) each wrapped in try/catch that captures throws into `snap.error` rather than escaping. A throwing `env` getter at line 195 sets `snap.error = e` AFTER `snap.signal` was already populated. Then in `runInternal` at line 623, `if (snap.signal?.aborted) throw makeAbortError(snap.signal);` runs BEFORE the `if (snap.error !== undefined) throw snap.error;` check at line 628. This is the load-bearing structural property: signal-first read order in `snapshotOptions` ensures `snap.signal` is populated even when a later field throws, and `runInternal`'s abort-precedence check fires before `snap.error` surfaces. A buggy implementation that read `options.env` (or any other later field) BEFORE `options.signal` would surface "env-getter-boom" instead of the AbortError and fail these tests — directly proving the "signal first" rule rather than merely inferring it from abort-vs-other-pre-iteration-failure precedence. Each test asserts (a) abort error surfaces (`name === "AbortError"` || `/abort/i.test(message)`) AND message does NOT match `/env-getter-boom/`, (b) no child was spawned (marker file absent), (c) no `loopx-*` tmpdir was created under the test-isolated TMPDIR parent. programmatic-api.test.ts: 942/942 (was 938, +4). Adjacent suites: zero regressions across tmpdir + env-vars + wfdir + loop-state + execution (904/904 across 5 e2e files), typecheck OK. Most-recent iteration (T-API-65a2 — Abort Precedence over Non-String Target Arguments): authored 12 tests (3 non-string target variants × 2 surfaces × 2 runtimes — Node 25.2.1 + Bun 1.3.11) extending the existing `SPEC: Abort Precedence over Pre-Iteration Failures` describe block in `apps/tests/tests/e2e/programmatic-api.test.ts` to pin the SPEC §9.3 abort-precedence contract on the **target-argument** (non-string) sub-branch — distinct from the target-syntax (`":bad"` invalid string) sub-branch covered by T-API-65a / T-API-65l. Closes both target-argument-validation sub-branches under SPEC §9.3's "target argument / target syntax validation" displacement. Variants are parameterized via a single `for` loop over three non-string target values (`undefined`, `null`, `42`) with each variant generating one `runPromise()` test and one `run()` test. Each test pre-aborts an `AbortController`, drives `runPromise(<variant> as any, opts)` or `run(<variant> as any, opts).next()`, and asserts (a) the surfaced error has `name === "AbortError"` OR matches `/abort/i` AND does NOT match `/target is required|must be a string|invalid.*target|target.*syntax/i` (anchored against the source-code error string `"target is required and must be a string"` at run.ts:691 — load-bearing for proving abort displaced the non-string-target rejection), (b) no child was spawned (the workflow's `child-ran.txt` marker is absent), (c) no `loopx-*` tmpdir was created under the test-isolated `TMPDIR` parent (per TEST-SPEC §4.7 isolation guidance, using `makeIsolatedTmpdirParent("api65a2-promise-${id}")` / `makeIsolatedTmpdirParent("api65a2-run-${id}")` per-variant parents). The fixture creates a valid `.loopx/ralph/index.sh` workflow that would write the marker if it ever ran — even though `undefined` / `null` / `42` can never resolve to "ralph", the marker check (b) is a belt-and-suspenders sanity net against an impl that somehow routes the call past target validation despite the non-string input. Test-only iteration; existing implementation in `packages/loop-extender/src/run.ts` already conformed: the abort-precedence check at line 623 (`if (snap.signal?.aborted) throw makeAbortError(snap.signal);`) runs FIRST inside `runInternal`, BEFORE the non-string target check at lines 686-692 (`if (target === undefined || target === null || typeof target !== "string") throw new Error("target is required and must be a string");`). The same code path serves both `run()` (lazy on first `.next()`) and `runPromise()` (eager via `runWithInternal` → `runInternal` async generator) surfaces — `runPromise` calls `runWithInternal` synchronously before its `await Promise.resolve()` microtask boundary, so abort dispatch fires at the call site for both surfaces, and the abort-error surfaces via the iterator's `.next()` rejection in both cases. A buggy implementation that routed target-syntax validation (`parseTarget` on a captured string) through the abort-precedence pathway but rejected non-string targets via a separate eager type-check (e.g., a synchronous `typeof target !== "string"` guard at the call site that escaped the captured-error path) would pass T-API-65a / T-API-65l yet fail this test. programmatic-api.test.ts: 954/954 (was 942, +12). Adjacent suites: zero regressions across tmpdir + env-vars + wfdir + loop-state + execution (904/904 across 5 e2e files), signals (9/9), unit + harness (158/158), typecheck OK. Most-recent iteration (T-API-65h / T-API-65i / T-API-65j / T-API-65o — Abort Precedence over Target-Resolution Failures): authored 12 tests (6 unique IDs × 2 runtimes — Node 25.2.1 + Bun 1.3.11) extending the existing `SPEC: Abort Precedence over Pre-Iteration Failures` describe block in `apps/tests/tests/e2e/programmatic-api.test.ts` to pin the SPEC §9.3 abort-precedence contract on the **target-resolution** sub-branch — distinct from the target-syntax (T-API-65a / 65l covering invalid target strings via `parseTarget`) and target-argument (T-API-65a2 covering non-string targets) sub-branches previously covered. SPEC §7.1 step 3 enumerates target resolution sub-paths: (a) missing workflow, (b) missing script in existing workflow, (c) missing default entry point — each is a distinct failure path INSIDE `runInternal` after `parseTarget` succeeds. T-API-65h covers (a) on runPromise (target `"nonexistent-workflow"`, fixture has `.loopx/ralph/index.sh`); T-API-65i covers (b) on runPromise (target `"ralph:check"`, fixture has only `index.sh`); T-API-65j covers (c) on runPromise (target `"ralph"`, fixture has only `check.sh`, no `index.*`); T-API-65o (a/b/c) covers all three on the run() generator surface via a single parameterized `for` loop. Each test pre-aborts an `AbortController`, drives `runPromise()` / `run().next()`, and asserts (a) `name === "AbortError"` OR `/abort/i.test(message)` AND the error message does NOT match the variant's target-resolution-specific regex (`/workflow.*not.*found|not.*found.*workflow|nonexistent-workflow/i` for missing-workflow, `/script.*not.*found|not.*found.*script|'check'/i` for missing-script, `/default entry|no.*index|index.*script/i` for missing-default-entry — anchored against the source error strings at run.ts:702-704 / 720-723 / 710-712), (b) the workflow's `child-ran.txt` marker is absent (no child was spawned), (c) no `loopx-*` tmpdir was created under the test-isolated `TMPDIR` parent (per TEST-SPEC §4.7 isolation guidance, using `makeIsolatedTmpdirParent("api65[h|i|j|o-X]")` per-variant parents). Test-only iteration; existing implementation in `packages/loop-extender/src/run.ts` already conformed: the abort-precedence check at run.ts:623 (`if (snap.signal?.aborted) throw makeAbortError(snap.signal);`) runs FIRST inside `runInternal`, BEFORE the workflow lookup at run.ts:700-705 (`Workflow 'X' not found in .loopx/`), the script lookup at run.ts:719-724 (`Script 'X' not found in workflow 'Y'`), and the index-presence check at run.ts:708-713 (`Workflow 'X' has no default entry point ('index' script)`). The same code path serves both `run()` (lazy on first `.next()`) and `runPromise()` (eager — `runPromise` calls `runWithInternal` synchronously before its `await Promise.resolve()` microtask boundary), so abort dispatch fires at the call site for both surfaces and the abort error surfaces via the iterator's `.next()` rejection in both cases. A buggy implementation that routed pre-aborted-signal precedence through env-file / discovery / target-syntax checks but bypassed abort-precedence on the workflow-lookup / script-lookup / index-presence paths would fail (a) on the corresponding variant. programmatic-api.test.ts: 966/966 (was 954, +12). Adjacent suites: zero regressions across tmpdir + env-vars + wfdir + loop-state + execution (904/904 across 5 e2e files), signals (9/9), unit + harness (158/158), typecheck OK.**

## P0/P1 — RESOLVED

### ADR-0004 §9.3 / §9.5 / §9.1 / §5.1 / §5.3 / §5.4 (T-API-65t — Abort Precedence over Discovery Name-Restriction Failure) — RESOLVED

SPEC §9.3 enumerates `.loopx/` discovery failures as one of the displaced pre-iteration failure modes. T-API-65s closes the SPEC §5.2 same-base-name collision sub-path; this iteration closes the SPEC §5.3 name-restriction sub-path (workflow / script names that violate `[a-zA-Z0-9_][a-zA-Z0-9_-]*`). Both sub-paths share the SPEC §5.4 "fatal in run mode" classification, but the validation code path and the surfaced error class are distinct (collision vs. name-pattern), and a buggy implementation that routed the collision sub-path through abort-precedence but emitted the name-restriction error directly (bypassing abort) would pass T-API-65s yet surface the name-restriction error here.

This iteration authors **8 tests** (2 fixtures × 2 surfaces × 2 runtimes — Node 25.2.1 + Bun 1.3.11):
- **T-API-65t-promise (a/b)**: `runPromise()` surface, parameterized over (a) `.loopx/-bad-workflow/index.sh` invalid workflow name and (b) `.loopx/broken/-bad.sh` invalid script name. Each fixture also includes the valid target workflow `.loopx/ralph/index.sh`. Drive `const c = new AbortController(); c.abort(); runPromise("ralph", { cwd, signal: c.signal, maxIterations: 1 })`. Asserts: (a) the promise rejects with the **abort error** (`name === "AbortError"` OR `/abort/i.test(message)`) AND the message does NOT match `/-bad(-workflow)?|invalid|must match|\[a-zA-Z0-9_\]/i` (proving abort displaced the name-restriction error, not vice-versa); (b) no child was spawned (no `child-ran.txt` marker written by `ralph/index.sh`); (c) no `loopx-*` tmpdir was created under the test-isolated `TMPDIR` parent.
- **T-API-65t-generator (a/b)**: `run()` generator-surface counterpart. Same fixtures; first `gen.next()` throws the abort error rather than the name-restriction error. Same three assertions.

**Test-only iteration**; existing implementation in `packages/loop-extender/src/run.ts` already conformed: `snapshotOptions` captures `options.signal` first and the snap-aborted check short-circuits before `discoverScripts` runs, so the SPEC §5.3 name-restriction validation at discovery time is never reached when a usable signal was pre-aborted at call time.

programmatic-api.test.ts: 1052/1052 tests (was 1044, +8). Adjacent suites: zero regressions.

### ADR-0004 §9.3 / §9.5 / §9.1 / §5.1 / §5.2 / §5.4 (T-API-65s-promise / T-API-65s-generator — Abort Precedence over Sibling-Validation Discovery Failure) — RESOLVED

SPEC §9.3 enumerates `.loopx/` discovery failures as one of the displaced pre-iteration failure modes. There are two SPEC §5.1 / §5.4 discovery-failure sub-paths: (1) the missing-`.loopx/` existence sub-path (covered by T-API-65b / 65m on the abort-precedence surface, T-TMP-12-programmatic-discovery-missing-loopx on the no-abort surface, and T-SIG-24 on the CLI signal-wins surface) and (2) the sibling-validation sub-path (a same-base-name collision in any sibling workflow under `.loopx/` — fatal in run mode per SPEC §5.4 regardless of whether the target workflow is the broken one). Sub-path (2) had counterparts on the no-abort surface (T-TMP-12-programmatic-discovery-validation) and the CLI signal-wins surface (T-SIG-25), but the programmatic abort-precedence surface was uncovered. Without this case, an implementation could route the missing-`.loopx/` failure through abort-precedence while emitting the collision error directly (bypassing abort precedence) for the validation sub-path, surfacing the collision error and possibly creating a tmpdir before the abort was observed.

This iteration authors **4 tests** (2 unique IDs × 2 runtimes — Node 25.2.1 + Bun 1.3.11):
- **T-API-65s-promise**: `runPromise()` surface. Fixture pairs a valid target workflow `.loopx/ralph/index.sh` with a sibling `.loopx/broken/` containing a `check.sh` + `check.ts` base-name collision. Drive `const c = new AbortController(); c.abort(); runPromise("ralph", { cwd, signal: c.signal, maxIterations: 1 })`. Asserts: (a) the promise rejects with the **abort error** (`name === "AbortError"` OR `/abort/i.test(message)`) AND the message does NOT match `/collision|broken|check\.(sh|ts)|multiple files/i` (proving the abort displaced the sibling-validation collision error, not vice-versa); (b) no child was spawned (no `child-ran.txt` marker written by `ralph/index.sh`); (c) no `loopx-*` tmpdir was created under the test-isolated `TMPDIR` parent (assertion scoped per TEST-SPEC §4.7 preface).
- **T-API-65s-generator**: `run()` generator-surface counterpart. Same fixture; first `gen.next()` throws the abort error rather than the collision error. Same three assertions.

**Test-only iteration**; existing implementation in `packages/loop-extender/src/run.ts` already conformed: `snapshotOptions` captures `options.signal` first and the snap-aborted check short-circuits before discovery runs, so the SPEC §5.4 sibling-validation pass at discovery time is never reached when a usable signal was pre-aborted at call time.

programmatic-api.test.ts: 1044/1044 tests (was 1040, +4). Adjacent suites: zero regressions.

### ADR-0004 §9.1 / §9.2 / §9.3 / §9.5 (T-API-65p / T-API-65q — Abort Precedence over Option-Snapshot Failures: 16-Variant Matrix) — RESOLVED

SPEC §9.3 abort-precedence rule states that a usable signal captured at call time displaces "captured option-snapshot errors" alongside the other pre-iteration failure modes. T-API-65f / T-API-65g already pin one representative option-snapshot variant on each surface (throwing later-option getter on `env`); this iteration extends the option-snapshot coverage by parameterizing **exhaustively** over every invalid `maxIterations` value (i)–(vi) and **representatively** over the remaining option-snapshot families (vii)–(xvi). Per SPEC §9.3 carve-out (ii), invalid `options.signal` is excluded because it captures no usable signal — that path is covered separately by T-API-65e.

This iteration authors **64 tests** (16 unique variants × 2 surfaces × 2 runtimes — Node 25.2.1 + Bun 1.3.11):
- **T-API-65p (i)–(xvi)**: `runPromise()` surface. Each variant constructs a pre-aborted `AbortController` plus an `opts` object that triggers a specific option-snapshot failure mode, then asserts: (a) the promise rejects with the **abort error** (`name === "AbortError"` OR `/abort/i.test(message)`) AND the message does NOT match a per-variant negative pattern that would be present if the option-snapshot error were surfaced instead; (b) no child was spawned (no `child-ran.txt` marker); (c) no `loopx-*` tmpdir was created under the test-isolated `TMPDIR` parent.
- **T-API-65q (i)–(xvi)**: `run()` generator-surface counterpart. Same 16 variants, same per-variant assertions but driven by `gen.next()` rejection.

**Variants covered.** (i) `maxIterations: -1`; (ii) `maxIterations: 1.5`; (iii) `maxIterations: NaN`; (iv) `maxIterations: Infinity`; (v) `maxIterations: null as any`; (vi) `maxIterations: "1" as any`; (vii) non-string `cwd: 42 as any`; (viii) throwing `cwd` getter (`Object.defineProperty(opts, "cwd", { enumerable: true, get() { throw new Error("cwd-getter-boom"); } })`); (ix) non-string `envFile: 42 as any`; (x) throwing `envFile` getter; (xi) invalid `env` shape `[] as any`; (xii) non-string env entry value `{ KEY: 42 as any }`; (xiii) throwing enumerable getter inside `env` (`Object.defineProperty(env, "KEY", { enumerable: true, get() { throw new Error("env-entry-getter-boom"); } })`); (xiv) throwing `env` `Proxy` `ownKeys` trap; (xv) throwing `env` `Proxy` `get` trap on an included key (descriptor returns full data form `{ enumerable: true, configurable: true, value: undefined, writable: true }` for engine-validity); (xvi) throwing `options.maxIterations` getter.

**Construction-rule compliance.** Per TEST-SPEC §1.3 "test-construction sanity for getter / proxy variants", getter / proxy variants (viii, x, xiii, xiv, xv, xvi) install the throwing accessor / proxy directly on the object passed to `runPromise()` / `run()` via `Object.defineProperty` or field-by-field construction — never via object-spread of an accessor-bearing object — so the throwing accessor / trap fires inside loopx's snapshot pass rather than being short-circuited by harness-side enumeration before the call.

**Test-only iteration**; existing implementation in `packages/loop-extender/src/run.ts` already conformed: `snapshotOptions` reads `options.signal` first per SPEC §9.1 / §9.5, captures the aborted state, and `runInternal` short-circuits to `throw makeAbortError(snap.signal)` at the top of the function before the option-snapshot error check (run.ts:623–630). A buggy implementation that read other option fields before `options.signal`, that surfaced the option-snapshot error before checking `snap.signal?.aborted`, or that special-cased any of the 16 specific failure modes outside the abort-precedence pathway would fail one or more variants.

programmatic-api.test.ts: 1040/1040 (was 976, +64). Adjacent suites: zero regressions.

### ADR-0004 §9.3 / §9.5 / §9.1 / §8.1 / §7.1 (T-API-65r-promise / T-API-65r-generator — Abort Precedence over Unreadable Global Env File Load Failure) — RESOLVED

SPEC §9.3 enumerates "env-file loading" as one of the displaced pre-iteration failure modes. SPEC §7.1 step 2 covers BOTH local `-e` and global env files in that loading step. T-API-65 / T-API-65k cover **missing local** env file across both API surfaces; T-API-65c covers **unreadable local** env file (mode 000) on `runPromise()`; the **unreadable global** env file sub-path (the same fixture pattern as T-TMP-12-global-env-unreadable on the no-abort surface, and T-SIG-30 on the CLI signal-wins surface) was uncovered at the abort-precedence intersection on **both** API surfaces. Per SPEC §8.1, `XDG_CONFIG_HOME` is read from the inherited environment (NOT from `RunOptions.env`), so the harness injects it through the driver process's inherited env — same channel that delivers `TMPDIR` to driver-based tests.

This iteration authors **4 tests** (2 unique IDs × 2 runtimes — Node 25.2.1 + Bun 1.3.11):
- **T-API-65r-promise**: `runPromise()` × `const c = new AbortController(); c.abort(); runPromise("ralph", { cwd, signal: c.signal, maxIterations: 1 })` where `$XDG_CONFIG_HOME/loopx/env` exists at mode `0o000` and `XDG_CONFIG_HOME` is passed via the driver's inherited env. Asserts: (a) the promise rejects with the **abort error** (`name === "AbortError"` OR `/abort/i.test(message)`) AND the message does NOT match `/xdg|global.*env|loopx\/env|EACCES|permission/i` (proving the abort displaced the global-env-file-load failure, not vice-versa); (b) no child was spawned (no `child-ran.txt` marker); (c) no `loopx-*` tmpdir was created under the test-isolated `TMPDIR` parent.
- **T-API-65r-generator**: `run()` × same construction. Generator-surface counterpart. Asserts: (a) first `next()` throws the abort error — **NOT** the global-env-file error; (b)/(c) same as r-promise.

Both gated `it.skipIf(IS_ROOT)` — root bypasses POSIX permission checks. Cleanup restores `chmod 0o644` so `project.cleanup()`'s `rm` succeeds.

**Test-only iteration**; existing implementation in `packages/loop-extender/src/run.ts` already conformed: the abort-precedence pathway short-circuits before the global env-file load step (which would otherwise surface an `EACCES` read error). A buggy implementation that loaded the global env file before snapshotting `options.signal` (or before checking `signal.aborted` after the snapshot) would surface the `EACCES` error and fail (a). Together with T-API-65 / T-API-65k (missing local), T-API-65c (unreadable local), and T-TMP-12-global-env-unreadable / T-SIG-30 (no-abort and CLI signal-wins surfaces), this closes the global-env-unreadable failure mode across all three precedence-relevant surfaces (CLI signal-wins, programmatic abort-precedence, no-abort tmpdir-non-creation).

programmatic-api.test.ts: 976/976 (was 972, +4). Adjacent suites: zero regressions.

### ADR-0004 §9.3 / §9.5 / §8.2 (T-API-65c — Abort Precedence over Unreadable Local Env File Load Failure) — RESOLVED

SPEC §9.3 enumerates "env-file loading" as one of the displaced pre-iteration failure modes. SPEC §8.2 distinguishes two fatal env-file paths: (i) **missing** env file (covered by T-API-65 / T-API-65k for both API surfaces), and (ii) **unreadable** env file. The unreadable-local-env sub-path was uncovered at the abort-precedence intersection on the `runPromise()` surface. SPEC §8.1 separately classifies malformed lines as parser warnings (non-fatal), so this test specifically exercises the **unreadable** branch via `chmod 0o000` rather than malformed content.

This iteration authors **2 tests** (1 unique ID × 2 runtimes — Node 25.2.1 + Bun 1.3.11):
- **T-API-65c**: `runPromise()` × `const c = new AbortController(); c.abort(); runPromise("ralph", { signal: c.signal, envFile: "unreadable.env", maxIterations: 1 })` where `unreadable.env` exists in the project dir at mode `0o000`. Asserts: (a) the promise rejects with the **abort error** (`name === "AbortError"` OR `/abort/i.test(message)`) AND the message does NOT match `/unreadable\.env|envFile|env file|EACCES|permission/i` (proving the abort displaced the env-file-load failure, not vice-versa); (b) no child was spawned (no `child-ran.txt` marker); (c) no `loopx-*` tmpdir was created under the test-isolated `TMPDIR` parent. Conditional on `process.getuid() !== 0` via `it.skipIf(IS_ROOT)` — root bypasses POSIX permission checks. Cleanup restores `chmod 0o644` to ensure `project.cleanup()`'s `rm` succeeds.

**Test-only iteration**; existing implementation in `packages/loop-extender/src/run.ts` already conformed: the abort-precedence pathway in `runInternal` short-circuits before the env-file-load step (which would otherwise surface an `EACCES` read error per SPEC §8.2). A buggy implementation that read the env file before snapshotting `options.signal` (or before checking `signal.aborted` after the snapshot) would surface the `EACCES` error and fail (a). Together with T-API-65 (missing-env-file, `runPromise()`) and T-API-65k (missing-env-file, `run()`), this closes SPEC §8.2's two fatal env-file paths × abort-precedence on the `runPromise()` surface; the `run()` counterpart for the unreadable branch is not separately enumerated by TEST-SPEC §4.9 but the same code path is exercised on the generator surface by T-API-65k's missing-env-file test (env-file-load is a single SPEC §8.2 step regardless of failure-mode-class on the `run()` surface).

programmatic-api.test.ts: 972/972 (was 970, +2). Adjacent suites: zero regressions.

### ADR-0004 §9.1 / §9.2 / §9.3 / §9.5 (T-API-65v / T-API-65w — Invalid Options Wrapper Carrying Aborted Signal Does NOT Enter Abort Pathway) — RESOLVED

SPEC §9.3 enumerates **two** distinct "no usable signal" carve-outs from abort precedence: (i) "An invalid `options` value … captures no signal and does not enter this pathway", and (ii) "non-`AbortSignal`-compatible `options.signal` captures no signal and does not enter this pathway." The carve-out (ii) — invalid `signal` shape on a valid options object — is covered by T-API-65e (`run()` surface only). The carve-out (i) — invalid options **wrapper** (e.g., array per SPEC §9.5 "non-array" violation) carrying an aborted signal as an own property — was uncovered at the abort-precedence intersection on **both** API surfaces.

This iteration authors **4 tests** (2 unique IDs × 2 runtimes — Node 25.2.1 + Bun 1.3.11):
- **T-API-65v**: `runPromise()` × `const opts: any = []; opts.signal = c.signal; runPromise("ralph", opts)`. The wrapper is an array (SPEC §9.5 "non-array" violation — same `[]` wrapper exercised by T-API-61e), and an aborted `AbortController.signal` is attached as an own property. Asserts: (a) the promise rejects with the **invalid-options error class** matching T-API-61e (`message.toMatch(/options|RunOptions/i)`) — **NOT** an abort error (`looksLikeAbort === false`, predicate identical to T-API-65e's anchored `\babort(ed)?\b` word-match); (b) no child was spawned (no `child-ran.txt` marker); (c) no `loopx-*` tmpdir was created under the test-isolated `TMPDIR` parent.
- **T-API-65w**: `run()` × same construction. Generator-surface counterpart. Asserts: (a) first `next()` throws the invalid-options error class matching T-API-61a — **NOT** an abort error; (b)/(c) same as 65v.

**Test-only iteration**; existing implementation in `packages/loop-extender/src/run.ts` already conformed: the option-snapshot validator detects the array-wrapper SPEC §9.5 violation BEFORE inspecting `opts.signal` for usability, surfacing the invalid-options error per the `runPromise()` and `run()` validation paths exercised by T-API-61e / T-API-61a. A buggy implementation that read `opts.signal` first, observed the aborted state, and routed through abort precedence (effectively bypassing wrapper validation when an aborted signal was attached) would fail (a) on both variants. Together T-API-65v + T-API-65w close SPEC §9.3 carve-out (i) ("invalid options value … captures no signal") across both API surfaces, complementing T-API-65e for carve-out (ii) on `run()`.

programmatic-api.test.ts: 970/970 (was 966, +4). Adjacent suites: zero regressions across tmpdir + env-vars + wfdir + loop-state + execution (904/904 across 5 e2e files), typecheck OK.

### ADR-0004 §9.1 / §9.3 / §9.5 / §7.1 (T-API-65h / T-API-65i / T-API-65j / T-API-65o — Abort Precedence over Target-Resolution Failures) — RESOLVED

SPEC §9.3 enumerates "target resolution" as one of the displaced pre-iteration failure modes. SPEC §7.1 step 3 enumerates target resolution sub-paths: missing workflow, missing script in existing workflow, and missing default entry point. The earlier T-API-65a / T-API-65l covered the target-syntax branch (invalid target string `":bad"` via `parseTarget`); T-API-65a2 covered the non-string target-argument branch. T-API-65h / 65i / 65j / 65o close the **target-resolution** branch — distinct from target-argument / target-syntax: the target string is well-formed and routes through `parseTarget`, then fails at the workflow / script / index-presence checks INSIDE `runInternal`.

This iteration authors **12 tests** (6 unique IDs × 2 runtimes — Node 25.2.1 + Bun 1.3.11):
- **T-API-65h**: `runPromise()` × pre-aborted × target `"nonexistent-workflow"` (workflow lookup fails at run.ts:700-705).
- **T-API-65i**: `runPromise()` × pre-aborted × target `"ralph:check"` (script lookup fails at run.ts:719-724; fixture has only `index.sh`).
- **T-API-65j**: `runPromise()` × pre-aborted × target `"ralph"` (index-presence check fails at run.ts:708-713; fixture has only `check.sh`).
- **T-API-65o (a/b/c)**: `run()` generator-surface counterpart, parameterized over the same three target-resolution sub-paths via a single `for` loop.

Each test asserts (a) `name === "AbortError"` OR `/abort/i.test(message)` AND the error message does NOT match the variant's target-resolution-specific regex (`/workflow.*not.*found|not.*found.*workflow|nonexistent-workflow/i` for missing-workflow, `/script.*not.*found|not.*found.*script|'check'/i` for missing-script, `/default entry|no.*index|index.*script/i` for missing-default-entry), (b) the workflow's `child-ran.txt` marker is absent (no child was spawned), (c) no `loopx-*` tmpdir was created under the test-isolated `TMPDIR` parent (per TEST-SPEC §4.7 isolation guidance, using `makeIsolatedTmpdirParent("api65X-...")` per-variant parents).

**Test-only iteration**; existing implementation in `packages/loop-extender/src/run.ts` already conformed: `runInternal` at run.ts:623 checks `if (snap.signal?.aborted) throw makeAbortError(snap.signal);` BEFORE workflow lookup at run.ts:700, script lookup at run.ts:719, and index-presence check at run.ts:708. The same code path serves both `run()` (lazy on first `.next()`) and `runPromise()` (eager — `runPromise` calls `runWithInternal` synchronously before its `await Promise.resolve()` microtask boundary), so abort dispatch fires at the call site for both surfaces and the abort error surfaces via the iterator's `.next()` rejection in both cases. A buggy implementation that routed pre-aborted-signal precedence through env-file / discovery / target-syntax checks but bypassed abort-precedence on the workflow-lookup / script-lookup / index-presence paths would fail (a) on the corresponding variant.

Together T-API-65h/65i/65j (runPromise) and T-API-65o (run) pin abort-precedence across all three SPEC §7.1 step 3 target-resolution sub-paths × both API surfaces. programmatic-api.test.ts: 966/966 (was 954, +12). Adjacent suites: zero regressions across tmpdir + env-vars + wfdir + loop-state + execution (904/904 across 5 e2e files), signals (9/9), unit + harness (158/158), typecheck OK.

### ADR-0004 §9.1 / §9.2 / §9.3 / §9.5 (T-API-65a2 — Abort Precedence over Non-String Target Arguments) — RESOLVED

SPEC §9.3 enumerates the pre-iteration failure modes that an aborted signal displaces: captured option-snapshot errors, **target argument / target syntax validation**, `.loopx/` discovery, env-file loading, target resolution, and tmpdir creation. The "target argument / target syntax validation" displacement is itself two sub-branches per SPEC §9.1:

- **Target syntax**: invalid string targets (e.g., `":bad"`) — covered by T-API-65a (runPromise) / T-API-65l (run) using `parseTarget` on the captured string.
- **Target argument**: non-string `target` values (e.g., `undefined`, `null`, `42`) — covered here by T-API-65a2.

Existing T-API-65a / T-API-65l proved abort displaces target-syntax errors; T-API-65a2 closes the target-argument sub-branch. Together both fully close the SPEC §9.3 "target argument / target syntax validation" displacement clause.

T-API-65a2 authors **12 tests** (3 non-string target variants × 2 surfaces × 2 runtimes — Node 25.2.1 + Bun 1.3.11) parameterized via a single `for` loop in the existing `SPEC: Abort Precedence over Pre-Iteration Failures` describe block. Variants: `undefined` (i), `null` (ii), `42` (iii). Each variant runs both `runPromise()` and `run()` surface tests.

Each test:
- Pre-aborts an `AbortController` synchronously before the `runPromise()` / `run()` call.
- Calls the function with the non-string target as `<variant> as any` (TypeScript escape hatch for the loose type).
- Asserts the rejection / first-`next()` throw has `name === "AbortError"` OR matches `/abort/i`.
- Asserts the error message does NOT match `/target is required|must be a string|invalid.*target|target.*syntax/i` — anchored against the source error string `"target is required and must be a string"` at `run.ts:691`. **This is the load-bearing assertion**: a buggy implementation that routed target-syntax validation through abort-precedence but rejected non-string targets via a separate eager type-check (escaping the captured-error path) would surface the non-string-target message instead.
- Asserts the workflow's `child-ran.txt` marker is absent (no child was spawned).
- Asserts no `loopx-*` tmpdir was created under the test-isolated `TMPDIR` parent (per TEST-SPEC §4.7 isolation guidance).

**Test-only iteration**; existing implementation in `packages/loop-extender/src/run.ts` already conformed:
- `snapshotOptions` (run.ts:105-232) reads `opts.signal` first; the user-signal listener (run.ts:307-322) registers `addEventListener("abort", ...)` and propagates pre-aborted state to `internalAc`.
- The pre-aborted check at run.ts:346-362 synchronously dispatches `internalAc.abort(reason)` when `usableSignal.aborted === true`.
- `runInternal` at run.ts:623 checks `if (snap.signal?.aborted) throw makeAbortError(snap.signal);` BEFORE the non-string target check at run.ts:686-692. This is the load-bearing structural property: abort precedence runs first, before target-argument validation.
- Same code path serves both `run()` (lazy on first `.next()`) and `runPromise()` (eager — `runPromise` calls `runWithInternal` synchronously before its `await Promise.resolve()` microtask boundary), so abort dispatch fires at the call site for both surfaces and the abort error surfaces via the iterator's `.next()` rejection in both cases.

programmatic-api.test.ts: 954/954 (was 942, +12). Adjacent suites: zero regressions across tmpdir + env-vars + wfdir + loop-state + execution (904/904 across 5 e2e files), signals (9/9), unit + harness (158/158), typecheck OK.

### ADR-0004 §9.1 / §9.2 / §9.3 / §9.5 (T-API-65f / T-API-65g — Abort Precedence over Throwing Later-Option Getter) — RESOLVED

SPEC §9.3 enumerates the pre-iteration failure modes that an aborted signal displaces: **captured option-snapshot errors**, target argument / target syntax validation, `.loopx/` discovery, env-file loading, target resolution, and tmpdir creation. The earlier T-API-65 series (T-API-65 / 65a / 65b / 65d on `runPromise()`; T-API-65k / 65l / 65m / 65n on `run()`) closed items 2–6, but did NOT cover item 1 (captured option-snapshot errors) — the FIRST item in the SPEC §9.3 enumeration. T-API-65f / T-API-65g close that gap by pairing a pre-aborted signal with a throwing later-option getter (`get env() { throw new Error("env-getter-boom"); }`).

The structural property the tests pin is the SPEC §9.1 / §9.2 "signal first" read-order rule: per SPEC §9.1 wording "Option-snapshot timing — `options.signal` is read first before any other field, so an already-aborted signal is captured before any subsequent option-field read can produce a snapshot exception" and SPEC §9.2 "Identical to `run()`: each option field read at most once, `options.signal` first." Without this rule, an aborted signal could be defeated by a throwing later-option getter that fires BEFORE the signal is captured. The implementation in `packages/loop-extender/src/run.ts` ALREADY conformed; this iteration is test-only and ships 4 tests (2 IDs × 2 runtimes — Node 25.2.1 + Bun 1.3.11) appended to the existing `SPEC: Abort Precedence over Pre-Iteration Failures` describe block.

**Implementation property pinned (test-only iteration).** In `snapshotOptions` (run.ts:105-232), the read order is: signal (line 132) → cwd (line 152) → envFile (line 176) → env (line 193) → maxIterations (line 209). Each later field is wrapped in try/catch that captures throws into `snap.error` rather than escaping. When the `env` getter throws at line 195, `snap.error` is populated AFTER `snap.signal` is already set at line 146. Then in `runInternal` (run.ts:608+), the line-623 check `if (snap.signal?.aborted) throw makeAbortError(snap.signal);` runs BEFORE the line-628 check `if (snap.error !== undefined) throw snap.error;`. The `runWithInternal` body wires the user signal listener at line 332-363 immediately after `snapshotOptions` returns, so the `addEventListener` registration happens at the call site and the `usableSignal.aborted` synchronous-dispatch path at line 346-362 propagates abort to `internalAc` before the wrapper is returned. A buggy implementation that (a) read `options.env` before `options.signal` would surface "env-getter-boom" before the signal was captured, (b) ran `if (snap.error !== undefined) throw snap.error;` before `if (snap.signal?.aborted) throw makeAbortError(snap.signal);` in `runInternal` would surface "env-getter-boom" instead of AbortError, or (c) skipped `addEventListener` registration when `snap.error` was set (guarding the registration only on `snap.error === undefined && snap.signal`) would still leave the abort-precedence path open via the `aborted: true` synchronous-dispatch branch at line 346 — but the line-332 guard `if (snap.error === undefined && snap.signal)` would skip the entire registration block when `snap.error` is set, and a buggy implementation that EAGERLY surfaced `snap.error` BEFORE the user-signal listener registered could leave a real AbortSignal's `aborted: true` un-noticed. The current implementation correctly registers the listener BEFORE `snap.error` is consulted (at line 332, where `snap.error` is checked but only because the env getter has not yet fired — the env getter only fires inside `snapshotOptions` if the user supplies a throwing-getter `env`, and `snap.signal` is already populated at that point because signal-first read order ran first).

**Test surface (T-API-65f — `run()` × pre-aborted + throwing env getter).** Driver pre-aborts an `AbortController`, builds an options object with `signal`, `cwd`, `maxIterations: 1`, AND a throwing `get env()` accessor that raises `new Error("env-getter-boom")` on read. Calls `run("ralph", throwingOpts)`, then awaits `gen.next()` and catches the rejection. Asserts: (a) `name === "AbortError"` OR `/abort/i.test(message)` is true, AND `message` does NOT match `/env-getter-boom/` (load-bearing — proves the abort error displaced the option-snapshot error rather than the option-snapshot error escaping); (b) no child was spawned (marker file absent — pre-iteration failure fires before any spawn); (c) no `loopx-*` tmpdir was created under the test-isolated `TMPDIR` parent (per TEST-SPEC §4.7 isolation guidance — uses `mkdtemp(loopx-test-api65f-)` parent).

**Test surface (T-API-65g — `runPromise()` × pre-aborted + throwing env getter).** Promise-surface counterpart to T-API-65f. Same throwing-getter options object; calls `await runPromise("ralph", throwingOpts)` and catches the rejection. Asserts the same three properties: (a) abort error surfaces, NOT the env-getter-boom error; (b) no child was spawned; (c) no `loopx-*` tmpdir was created. The promise-surface version is structurally distinct because `runPromise()`'s async body runs synchronously up to its first `await`, calling `runWithInternal` BEFORE the first `await Promise.resolve()` boundary — so the snapshot pass + signal capture + abort-listener registration fire at the call site, but the option-shape error is captured into `snap.error` and surfaces via promise rejection AFTER the microtask boundary. This preserves the "always returns a promise" contract per SPEC §9.2 even under throwing-getter inputs.

Now-passing tests (this iteration):
- **programmatic-api.test.ts: 942/942 PASS** (was 938, +4)
- Adjacent suites: zero regressions across tmpdir (569/569) + env-vars + wfdir + loop-state + execution (904/904 across 5 e2e files); typecheck OK.

### ADR-0004 §9.3 / §9.5 / §9.1 / §9.2 (T-API-65 / 65a / 65b / 65d / 65e / 65k / 65l / 65m / 65n — Foundational Abort Precedence over Pre-Iteration Failures) — RESOLVED

SPEC §9.3 specifies the abort-precedence contract: when `options.signal` is an AbortSignal-compatible object that is aborted (either at call-time capture or via subsequent abort dispatch before the first script spawn), the abort outcome displaces all OTHER pre-iteration failures — missing env-file, invalid-target syntax, missing `.loopx/` discovery, tmpdir-creation failure — and surfaces an `AbortError` rather than the displaced failure mode's signature. SPEC §9.3 carves out a critical exception: a non-AbortSignal-compatible `signal` (one that fails the §9.5 shape contract) does NOT enter this pathway — it surfaces as an option-snapshot shape error instead, and any *other* pre-iteration error may still surface in implementation-defined order. The T-API-65 foundational series pins the load-bearing structural property of abort-precedence on both `run()` and `runPromise()` surfaces against each of the four canonical pre-iteration displaced-failure-mode arms, plus the §9.3 carve-out arm — completing the foundational rows of the T-API-65* abort-precedence matrix that earlier iterations referenced as "still need authoring."

The implementation in `packages/loop-extender/src/run.ts` ALREADY conformed; this iteration is test-only and ships 18 tests (9 unique IDs × 2 runtimes — Node 25.2.1 + Bun 1.3.11) under a new `SPEC: Abort Precedence over Pre-Iteration Failures` describe block at the bottom of `apps/tests/tests/e2e/programmatic-api.test.ts`. The structural property the tests pin: in `runInternal` (run.ts:608+), the `if (snap.signal?.aborted) throw makeAbortError(snap.signal);` check at line 623 runs FIRST — BEFORE `snap.error` (628), discovery (640), envFile loading (660-668), target validation (686-692), workflow lookup (700), and tmpdir creation (in `runLoop`). This is the load-bearing structural property: abort precedence runs first. Symmetrically, `snapshotOptions` (run.ts:105-232) reads `signal` first (so the call-site capture for `signal` is decoupled from later option fields' read order); the user-signal listener (run.ts:307-322) registers `addEventListener("abort", ...)` and propagates to `internalAc`; the pre-aborted check (run.ts:346-362) synchronously dispatches `internalAc.abort(reason)` when `usableSignal.aborted === true`. For the §9.3 carve-out arm: `snapshotOptions` for invalid signal shape sets `snap.error = TypeError` and never assigns `snap.signal`, so `snap.signal?.aborted` is `undefined` and the abort-precedence path is structurally skipped — `snap.error` (or another pre-iteration error like missing env-file) surfaces instead in implementation-defined order. The carve-out is honored structurally rather than via an explicit conditional.

**Test surface (T-API-65 / 65a / 65b / 65d / 65k / 65l / 65m / 65n — pre-aborted signal beats each canonical pre-iteration displaced-failure mode × both surfaces).** Eight unique-ID arms parameterize over four displaced-failure modes × two API surfaces, closing the abort-precedence × pre-iteration-failure-axis × surface matrix on the runPromise-surface (T-API-65 / 65a / 65b / 65d) and the run-surface (T-API-65k / 65l / 65m / 65n). The four displaced-failure modes:
- **Missing env-file** (T-API-65 runPromise / T-API-65k run): driver passes `envFile: "/nonexistent/path/to/env"` alongside a pre-aborted AbortController. Without abort precedence, an env-file-not-found error would surface during the discovery + env-load phase. With correct abort precedence, the AbortError surfaces first.
- **Invalid target `:bad`** (T-API-65a runPromise / T-API-65l run): driver passes the syntactically invalid target `":bad"` (parseTarget would reject) alongside a pre-aborted controller. Without abort precedence, an invalid-target error would surface from `parseTarget`. With correct precedence, AbortError wins.
- **Missing `.loopx/` discovery** (T-API-65b runPromise / T-API-65m run): driver passes a `cwd` that does not contain a `.loopx/` directory alongside a pre-aborted controller. Without abort precedence, a discovery error would surface (no workflows found). With correct precedence, AbortError wins.
- **Tmpdir-creation failure** (T-API-65d runPromise / T-API-65n run): driver sets `TMPDIR` to a non-writable parent (e.g., `/proc/1`) alongside a pre-aborted controller. Without abort precedence, an EACCES `mkdtemp` error would surface from `runLoop`'s tmpdir setup. With correct precedence, AbortError wins. Skipped under root (root has write access to `/proc/1`-like parents and the test cannot induce the displaced failure mode).

Each abort-path test asserts (a) abort error surfaces (`name === "AbortError"` || `/abort/i.test(message)`), AND the message does NOT match the displaced failure mode's signature (e.g., does NOT match `/ENOENT/`, `/parseTarget|invalid target|:bad/`, `/discovery|no workflows/i`, `/EACCES|mkdtemp/`); (b) no child was spawned (marker file absent — load-bearing: distinguishes pre-iteration abort precedence from a buggy implementation that spawned the child first then aborted); (c) no `loopx-*` tmpdir was created under the test-isolated `TMPDIR` parent (per TEST-SPEC §4.7 isolation guidance — uses `mkdtemp(loopx-test-api65*-)` parents). The marker-absent + tmpdir-absent assertions are what make the abort-precedence claim rigorous: a buggy `runInternal` that ran `if (snap.error) throw snap.error` BEFORE `if (snap.signal?.aborted) throw makeAbortError(...)` would surface the displaced error's signature in (a) AND fail (b)/(c) when the displaced error fires after a child has already started or after tmpdir-create has already taken effect.

**Test surface (T-API-65e — invalid signal shape `"not-a-signal"` + missing envFile carve-out per SPEC §9.3).** Single ID × 2 runtimes = 2 tests. Driver passes `signal: "not-a-signal"` (a non-object that fails the §9.5 compatibility shape contract) alongside `envFile: "/nonexistent/path"`. Per SPEC §9.3 carve-out, the non-compatible signal does NOT enter the abort-precedence pathway — the implementation captures the shape error into `snap.error` and clears `snap.signal`. Without an aborted `snap.signal` to displace `snap.error`, the surfaced error is implementation-defined: it may be the shape error itself (reading `RunOptions.signal must be an AbortSignal-compatible object`) OR the env-file-not-found error (per SPEC §9.5 the read order between option fields is implementation-defined; per the structural property in `runInternal`, `snap.error` runs before envFile loading at line 628, so in practice the shape error wins — but the test does not pin that ordering since the SPEC explicitly leaves it implementation-defined). Asserts: `name === "AbortError"` is `false` AND the error message does NOT match the anchored regex `/\babort(ed)?\b/i` — confirming the abort pathway was structurally skipped. The anchored regex (`\b...\b`) is the load-bearing detail: the SPEC-mandated shape error message contains the substring `"AbortSignal-compatible"` (which contains the substring `"Abort"`), and a naive `/abort/i.test(message)` would falsely match the shape error and report "abort path was entered." The anchored `/\babort(ed)?\b/i` only matches `abort` or `aborted` as standalone words, not as substrings of `AbortSignal`/`AbortController`/etc. — correctly distinguishing abort errors from shape errors that mention AbortSignal in the message text. The test allows the surfaced error to reference signal-shape OR missing env-file (impl-defined ordering between those two per SPEC §9.5) while structurally pinning the abort-pathway-not-entered claim. This is the load-bearing test for the SPEC §9.3 carve-out: a buggy implementation that surfaced an abort error whenever `snap.signal` was supplied (regardless of compatibility) would fail.

Now-passing tests (this iteration):
- **programmatic-api.test.ts: 938/938 PASS** (was 920, +18)
- Adjacent suites: zero regressions across tmpdir (569/569) + env-vars + wfdir + loop-state + execution (335/335 across 4 e2e files) + signals (9/9) + unit + harness (158/158); typecheck OK.

### ADR-0004 §9.1 / §9.2 / §9.3 / §9.5 (T-API-64m / T-API-64m2 / T-API-64n / T-API-64n2 / T-API-64o / T-API-64o2 / T-API-64p / T-API-64p2 / T-API-64p3 / T-API-64q / T-API-64q2 — Throwing-AEL-getter / Prototype-Inherited / No-removeEventListener / aborted:true × non-compatible-shape × maxIter:0 carve-out / Non-undefined-AEL-return) — RESOLVED

This iteration closes the remaining T-API-64 sub-IDs that round out the SPEC §9.5 duck-typed-signal compatibility contract on both API surfaces (52 tests across 11 unique it() bodies × parameterized variants × 2 runtimes), AND ships an implementation fix in `run.ts` to honor the SPEC §9.3 / §9.5 / T-API-64p contract that **a signal failing the §9.5 compatibility check (including a throwing `addEventListener`) does NOT enter the abort-precedence pathway regardless of `aborted`'s value**.

**Implementation fix (run.ts).** Two coupled changes that together honor the SPEC §9.3 + §9.5 contract for `aborted: true` × non-compatible-shape:
- **Always invoke `addEventListener` at call-site capture, regardless of `aborted` value.** Previously `runWithInternal` short-circuited on `snap.signal.aborted === true` and skipped the `addEventListener` registration entirely — meaning a duck signal with `{ aborted: true, addEventListener() { throw } }` would route through the abort-precedence pathway in `runInternal` (surfacing an AbortError) instead of being caught as a non-compatible signal (surfacing an option-snapshot error). The fix removes the if/else branching and unconditionally invokes `addEventListener` inside try/catch FIRST, then performs the `aborted` check after a clean registration. This matches SPEC §9.5 wording "must be callable and returns without throwing when loopx invokes it" — loopx must invoke it to verify the contract, and per T-API-64p that verification must happen even when `aborted: true`.
- **Clear `snap.signal` when `addEventListener` registration throws.** SPEC §9.3 specifies that "an invalid `options` value or non-`AbortSignal`-compatible `options.signal` captures no signal and does not enter this pathway" — i.e., a non-compatible signal must NOT enter the abort-precedence pathway. The natural way to express "no usable signal was captured" is to clear `snap.signal`. The downstream `snap.signal?.aborted` check in `runInternal` then naturally returns `undefined` and the abort-precedence path is skipped, allowing the captured `snap.error` (the `addEventListener` throw) to surface as an option-snapshot error.

A buggy implementation that gated abort-vs-option-snapshot dispatch on `aborted` alone (without first verifying the full §9.5 contract via `addEventListener` invocation) would surface an AbortError on T-API-64p / T-API-64p2 / T-API-64p3 (variant c, throwing-AEL) and fail. A buggy implementation that always entered the abort-precedence pathway whenever `snap.signal.aborted === true` (regardless of whether `snap.error` was also set from a downstream registration failure) would also fail those tests — the explicit `snap.signal = undefined` clear catches that failure mode by making the abort-precedence check structurally unreachable when the contract failed. The reordering of the existing `if (snap.signal.aborted)` and `if (snap.error)` checks in `runInternal` is intentionally NOT done, because SPEC §9.3 requires that an aborted USABLE signal displaces other pre-iteration option errors (e.g., a throwing cwd getter); the `snap.signal = undefined` mechanism preserves that semantic by distinguishing "non-compatible signal" (snap.signal cleared, no abort precedence) from "compatible signal + other option error" (snap.signal preserved, abort precedence wins).

**Test surface (T-API-64m / T-API-64m2 — Throwing addEventListener getter).** SPEC §9.5 requires `addEventListener` to be "callable and returns without throwing when loopx invokes it" — but the contract is also violated when the property *read itself* throws, before loopx can ever attempt to invoke the result. T-API-64f covers `addEventListener` that is a function that throws when called (the property read returns a function, the call throws); T-API-64m covers the structurally different case where the property's *getter* throws on read (loopx never observes any value because the read raises). The test uses `Object.defineProperty(duck, "addEventListener", { enumerable: true, get() { throw new Error("ae-getter-boom"); } });` — the `Object.defineProperty` form on a fresh object guards against the test harness or JS engine invoking the getter before `run()` is called and surfacing the exception at the test call site. The implementation already conformed via the try/catch wrapper around the `addEventListener` property read in `isAbortSignalCompatible` (run.ts:64) — the throwing getter falls through to `return false`, which sets snap.error and (after the implementation fix) clears snap.signal. (1 ID × 2 surfaces × 2 runtimes = 4 tests.)

**Test surface (T-API-64n / T-API-64n2 — Prototype-inherited duck signal).** SPEC §9.5 uses "expose", not "has own", for the AbortSignal-compatibility contract — a duck signal whose `aborted` and `addEventListener` are inherited from a custom prototype (e.g., a class instance) must be accepted. Tests construct `class DuckSignal { addEventListener(...) {...} _fire() {...} } DuckSignal.prototype.aborted = false; const duck = new DuckSignal();` — `duck.aborted` and `duck.addEventListener` resolve via prototype walk (`Object.hasOwn` returns false until `_fire()` writes the own `aborted` property). Asserts: (a) `ownHasAborted === false` AND `ownHasAEL === false` (sanity — proves the test genuinely exercises the prototype-walk path), (b) abort surfaced (the inherited contract was honored), (c) NO option-snapshot error appears. A buggy implementation that probed via `Object.hasOwn(duck, "aborted")` / `Object.hasOwn(duck, "addEventListener")` would fail (a) AND surface an option-shape error rather than entering the abort path. Implementation already conformed: `isAbortSignalCompatible` uses ordinary `[[Get]]` semantics (`(signal as ...).aborted` and `(signal as ...).addEventListener`) which walk the prototype chain. (1 ID × 2 surfaces × 2 runtimes = 4 tests.)

**Test surface (T-API-64o / T-API-64o2 — No removeEventListener × normal completion).** SPEC §9.5 explicitly states `removeEventListener` is NOT part of the AbortSignal-compatibility contract: "loopx does not require its presence, and whether loopx invokes it on settlement is implementation-defined." A duck signal that exposes only `aborted` and `addEventListener` (no `removeEventListener` own or inherited) must be accepted, and a normal-completion run that never aborts must settle without throwing. T-API-64a / T-API-64a2 cover the abort-path acceptance (the abort fires); T-API-64o / T-API-64o2 closes the normal-completion-path cell (the script emits `{"stop":true}` and exits 0; the run drains cleanly to `{ done: true }`). The test asserts: (a) `hasRemove === false` (sanity — `"removeEventListener" in duck` excludes both own and inherited), (b) settled cleanly without throwing (no TypeError from a `signal.removeEventListener` call), (c) script ran exactly once and emitted `stop: true` (proves the loop body was entered, not a pre-iteration short-circuit), (d) no warning / error mentioning `removeEventListener` or TypeError on stderr. A buggy implementation that called `signal.removeEventListener(...)` unguarded on settlement would TypeError on the duck, failing (b) or (d). Implementation already conformed: the `internalAc.signal` (a real AbortSignal) is what `execution.ts` calls `removeEventListener` on; the user-supplied `snap.signal` is registered with `{ once: true }` which auto-removes the listener on fire, and loopx never explicitly calls `snap.signal.removeEventListener(...)` on the user signal. (1 ID × 2 surfaces × 2 runtimes = 4 tests.)

**Test surface (T-API-64p / T-API-64p2 / T-API-64p3 — `aborted: true` × non-compatible-shape × maxIterations:0 carve-out).** SPEC §9.3 specifies: "An invalid `options` value or non-`AbortSignal`-compatible `options.signal` captures no signal and does not enter this pathway." The cardinal contract is that `aborted: true` ALONE is not sufficient to enter the abort pathway — the signal must ALSO satisfy the §9.5 compatibility contract (including `addEventListener` being callable and returning without throwing). T-API-64f / T-API-64i / T-API-64i3 cover the three `addEventListener`-half violations (throws-on-call / non-callable / missing) with `aborted: false`; their assertions ("option-snapshot error, not an abort error") would also pass on a buggy implementation that read `aborted` first, observed `false`, and routed through the option-snapshot path before noticing the `addEventListener` violation — so the existing tests cannot distinguish between "shape was checked first" and "aborted was checked first and happened to be false." T-API-64p inverts that failure mode: it pairs each contract-violating shape with `aborted: true`, ensuring a buggy implementation that read `aborted` first and routed through abort precedence on the truthy reading would surface an abort error and fail. Parameterized over 3 variants — (a) missing `addEventListener` property, (b) non-callable `addEventListener` (number 123), (c) throwing `addEventListener`. T-API-64p2 is the runPromise() counterpart. T-API-64p3 closes the maxIterations:0 diagonal: option-shape validation is iteration-count-independent, and the abort-precedence carve-out applies regardless of iteration count — same 3 shape variants under `maxIterations: 0` × both surfaces. The implementation fix in `run.ts` (described above) is what makes these tests pass for variant (c) — variants (a) and (b) were already handled correctly by `isAbortSignalCompatible`'s `typeof !== "function"` rejection. (3 IDs × 3 variants × 2 surfaces × 2 runtimes = 36 tests for T-API-64p / 64p2 / 64p3 cumulative.)

**Test surface (T-API-64q / T-API-64q2 — `addEventListener` returns non-undefined value accepted).** SPEC §9.5 requires `addEventListener` to be "callable and returns without throwing"; it does NOT require the return value to be `undefined`. A buggy implementation that asserted `result === undefined` after invoking `addEventListener` would reject perfectly conforming duck signals whose `addEventListener` happens to return a value (a string, number, the listener itself, or any other non-undefined result), violating the SPEC contract. Parameterized over 4 non-undefined return variants — (a) string `"registered"`, (b) number `123`, (c) the listener function itself (`return fn;` — mirroring some event-emitter libraries), (d) object `{ ok: true }`. The fixture is the long-lived `touch ready.txt; while true; do sleep 1; done` pattern — driver awaits the ready marker, then calls `duck._fire()` to trigger the abort. Asserts: (a) NO synchronous throw (duck signal accepted at call site), (b) script reached "ready" (the loop body was entered — the duck was usable), (c) abort error surfaced (NOT an option-shape / signal-validation error), (d) `RunOptions.signal` does not appear in the error message. A buggy implementation that asserted return-value-undefined would surface an option-shape error instead of letting the run proceed to the abort path, failing (b)/(c)/(d). Implementation already conformed: `isAbortSignalCompatible` only checks `typeof ael !== "function"` — the return value is not consulted. (1 ID × 4 variants × 2 surfaces × 2 runtimes = 16 tests.)

Now-passing tests (this iteration):
- **programmatic-api.test.ts: 920/920 PASS** (was 868, +52)
- Adjacent suites: zero regressions across tmpdir + env-vars + wfdir + loop-state + execution + signals + version-check + unit + harness; typecheck OK.

### ADR-0004 §9.1 / §9.2 / §9.3 / §9.5 (T-API-64 series — Duck-Typed Signal Acceptance and Contract Violations) — RESOLVED

SPEC §9.5 defines AbortSignal-compatibility as a duck-typed contract: any object with a readable boolean `aborted` property AND a callable `addEventListener('abort', listener)` method qualifies as a usable signal. SPEC §9.5 also specifies reentrancy semantics: if `addEventListener` synchronously invokes the registered listener during registration, OR if `aborted` is observed as `true` at any point during call-time capture, loopx treats the signal as aborted. SPEC §9.3 further specifies that an invalid `options.signal` (one that fails the SPEC §9.5 contract) is an option-snapshot error, NOT an abort error, and does NOT enter the abort-precedence pathway. The T-API-64 series pins down the foundational duck-signal contract pieces across the {run() / runPromise()} surface matrix.

The implementation in `packages/loop-extender/src/run.ts` ALREADY conformed: `isAbortSignalCompatible` (lines 51-70) checks the contract via try/catch reads — both `aborted` and `addEventListener` are read inside try/catch so throwing getters return false; `typeof aborted !== "boolean"` rejects missing/non-boolean variants (no coercion); `typeof ael !== "function"` rejects non-callable. `snapshotOptions` (lines 132-147) captures the signal-shape error into `snap.error` when the contract fails, surfacing it as an option-snapshot error rather than an abort error. The reentrant `addEventListener` pathway (lines 339-347) wraps `signal.addEventListener("abort", onUserSignalAbort, { once: true })` in a try/catch, and the listener `onUserSignalAbort` (lines 307-322) pins `firstObservedRef.trigger = "abort"` and calls `internalAc.abort()` — when the duck signal's `addEventListener` synchronously invokes the listener during registration (whether or not it also mutates `aborted`), the abort path runs reentrantly. The `aborted: true` at capture-time pathway (lines 327-338) checks `snap.signal.aborted` BEFORE `addEventListener` so an already-aborted duck signal pins the abort outcome regardless of whether `addEventListener` is well-formed (but only after `isAbortSignalCompatible` confirms the shape — T-API-64p ensures `aborted: true` × non-compatible-shape still routes through the option-snapshot error path).

A buggy implementation that surfaced an invalid-signal-shape as an abort error (e.g., by routing through the abort-precedence pathway whenever `aborted === true` was observed without first verifying full contract compatibility) would fail T-API-64 / T-API-64j / T-API-64j2. A buggy implementation that recognized reentrant `addEventListener` only on `runPromise()` (and registered the listener but did not enter the abort pathway on `run()`) would fail T-API-64b / T-API-64b2 on the run() surface. A buggy implementation that gated abort treatment on a post-`addEventListener` re-read of `aborted` (rather than honoring the listener-firing event itself as a SPEC §9.5 abort signal) would fail T-API-64b2 (the isolated reentrancy variant where `aborted` stays false). A buggy implementation that coerced missing/null/0/undefined `aborted` to `false` via falsy-checks (or coerced 1 to `true` via truthy-checks) would fail T-API-64j / T-API-64j2 across the no-coercion variant matrix. A buggy implementation that let a throwing `aborted` getter or throwing `addEventListener` escape past the snapshot-capture boundary would fail T-API-64h / T-API-64h2 / T-API-64f / T-API-64g on the call-site never-throws assertion.

Now-passing tests (this iteration):
- **programmatic-api.test.ts: 848/848 PASS** (was 782, +66) — added 66 tests (33 unique it() bodies × 2 runtimes) under a new `SPEC: Duck-Typed Signal — Acceptance and Contract Violations` describe block at the bottom of programmatic-api.test.ts:
  - **T-API-64**: `run()` — invalid `options.signal` (string `"not-a-signal"`) surfaces as option-snapshot error on first `next()`, NOT an abort error. Asserts (a) the error message references the invalid signal shape, (b) `looksLikeAbort` is false (no AbortError name, no /aborted|abortError/i pattern in message), (c) no child spawned. (1 ID × 2 runtimes = 2 tests.)
  - **T-API-64a / T-API-64a2**: Duck-typed signal acceptance under abort firing — `runPromise()` (T-API-64a) and `run()` (T-API-64a2) accept own-property duck signal `{ aborted: false, addEventListener(t, fn) { if (t === "abort") this._listener = fn; }, _fire() { this.aborted = true; this._listener?.(); } }` and surface the abort error correctly when `_fire()` is called mid-iteration. Long-lived bash fixture (`touch ready.txt; while true; do sleep 1; done`); driver code polls for the ready marker before firing the duck. T-API-64a2 swallows the next() promise rejection synchronously to avoid an unhandled rejection during the polling wait. (2 IDs × 2 runtimes = 4 tests.)
  - **T-API-64b**: Reentrant `addEventListener` (conjunction case — listener fires synchronously during registration AND `aborted` transitions to `true`) treated as aborted on both surfaces. Parameterized over `runPromise()` / `run()`. Asserts (a) abort surfaced, (b) no child spawned (no marker file written), (c) no `loopx-*` directory created under the test-isolated `TMPDIR` parent. (1 ID × 2 surfaces × 2 runtimes = 4 tests.)
  - **T-API-64b2**: Isolated reentrant `addEventListener` (FIRST disjunct — listener fires synchronously during registration, but `aborted` remains false) treated as aborted on both surfaces. Catches a buggy implementation that gated abort treatment on a post-registration re-read of `aborted` rather than honoring the listener-firing event itself. (1 ID × 2 surfaces × 2 runtimes = 4 tests.)
  - **T-API-64c**: Duck signal with `aborted: true` at capture time (SECOND disjunct — `aborted` observed as true; listener never fires) treated as aborted on both surfaces. (1 ID × 2 surfaces × 2 runtimes = 4 tests.)
  - **T-API-64d**: Real pre-aborted `AbortSignal` instance rejects `runPromise()` with abort error, no child spawned, no tmpdir created — pins the contract for real `AbortSignal` instances passed already-aborted. (1 ID × 2 runtimes = 2 tests.)
  - **T-API-64e**: `run()` reads `options.signal` BEFORE `options.env`. Constructs an opts object with both `signal` and `env` exposed via enumerable getters that push to a shared `order` array; asserts `order[0] === "signal"`. (1 ID × 2 runtimes = 2 tests.)
  - **T-API-64f / T-API-64g**: Throwing `addEventListener` (`function() { throw new Error("listener-register-failed"); }`) surfaces as option-snapshot error on first `next()` (T-API-64f, run()) or promise rejection (T-API-64g, runPromise()). Asserts (a) NO synchronous throw at call site (load-bearing — captures the SPEC §9.1 / §9.2 never-throws contract), (b) error references invalid signal or wraps `listener-register-failed`, (c) NOT an abort error, (d) no child spawned, (e) no tmpdir created. (2 IDs × 2 runtimes = 4 tests.)
  - **T-API-64h / T-API-64h2**: Throwing `aborted` getter (`Object.defineProperty(duck, "aborted", { get() { throw new Error("aborted-getter-failed"); } })`) surfaces as option-snapshot error on both surfaces — pins the SPEC §9.5 "readable `aborted` property" contract (a getter that throws is not "readable"). Asserts the error wraps the getter exception or references the invalid signal, NOT an abort error. (2 IDs × 2 runtimes = 4 tests.)
  - **T-API-64i / T-API-64i2**: Non-callable `addEventListener` (string `"not-a-function"` stored on the property) surfaces as option-snapshot error on both surfaces. (2 IDs × 2 runtimes = 4 tests.)
  - **T-API-64i3 / T-API-64i4**: Missing `addEventListener` property (`{ aborted: false }` only) surfaces as option-snapshot error on both surfaces — distinguishes from T-API-64i (non-callable but present) by exercising the `prop in obj` / `obj.prop !== undefined` lookup path. (2 IDs × 2 runtimes = 4 tests.)
  - **T-API-64j / T-API-64j2**: Missing or non-boolean `aborted` parameterized over 7 variants — (a) missing own property, (b) explicit `undefined`, (c) string `"false"`, (d) number `0`, (e) `null`, (f) truthy number `1`, (g) object `{}` — surfaces as option-snapshot error on both surfaces. The expanded variant matrix hardens the no-coercion rule across primitive-vs-object × falsy-vs-truthy × undefined-vs-null axes — a buggy implementation that defaulted missing `aborted` to `false` (or coerced any non-boolean via `!aborted` / `aborted == false` / `aborted == true`) would silently treat the duck signal as either "not yet aborted, proceed" or "already aborted, route through abort pathway" and fail at least one variant. Each variant is a separate `it()` block so failure attribution is clear. (2 IDs × 7 variants × 2 runtimes = 28 tests.)
- Test infrastructure added inline: `makeIsolatedTmpdirParent(label)` and `listLoopxEntries(parent)` — same pattern used in T-API-57 / T-API-58 series for tmpdir-creation absence assertions.
