### ADR-0004 §9.1 / §9.2 / §9.5 (T-API-64k / T-API-64k2 / T-API-64k3 — Call-Site Capture Timing for `options.signal`) — RESOLVED

SPEC §9.1 / §9.2 / §9.5 specify that `options.signal` is **read at the call site as a synchronous snapshot** — both run surfaces must capture the signal before returning. Existing T-API-64a/64a2/64b/64b2/64c tests prove the *effects* of various signal shapes after iteration starts (abort fires, listener registers, etc.) but do not directly prove that loopx **registered an `addEventListener` call AT call time** — only that the listener was registered in time to observe a same-tick abort. A buggy implementation that deferred all option reads (including `signal.addEventListener`) until first `next()` would pass the existing duck-signal abort tests yet break the SPEC §9.1 / §9.2 call-site snapshot contract — observable here via a duck signal whose `addEventListener` increments a counter, snapshotted synchronously after the call returns and before any consumer interaction.

The implementation in `packages/loop-extender/src/run.ts` ALREADY conformed: `run()` (lines 255-260) is a non-async function that synchronously calls `runWithInternal`, which synchronously calls `snapshotOptions(options)` at line 267 — `signal` is read first at line 134, captured into `snap.signal` at line 146 — then `addEventListener` is wired into `internalAc` synchronously between lines 326-348 of `runWithInternal` (BEFORE the wrapper is constructed and returned). `runPromise()` (lines 732-783) is an async function whose body runs synchronously up to its first `await Promise.resolve()` microtask boundary at line 776 — `runWithInternal` is called BEFORE that await at line 761, so the option-snapshot pass + signal capture + addEventListener registration all fire synchronously at the call site even on the eager promise-returning surface, observable to the caller before the returned promise suspends.

A buggy implementation that gated `addEventListener` registration inside the wrapper's `next()` body (or inside `runInternal` per-iteration setup) rather than at `runWithInternal`'s synchronous body would observe `count === 0` immediately after `run()` / `runPromise()` returned and fail T-API-64k / T-API-64k2. A buggy implementation that read `signal` later than the other recognized fields (e.g., `cwd` first, then `signal`) would observe `order[0] !== "signal"` and fail T-API-64k3 on at least one of the eight cells — particularly load-bearing on the cells where the other field's getter happens to be implementation-ordered before signal in a buggy snapshot pass (a buggy "honor signal-first against env but not against cwd" implementation would pass the env cell yet fail the cwd cell).

Now-passing tests (this iteration):
- **programmatic-api.test.ts: 868/868 PASS** (was 848, +20) — added 20 tests (10 unique it() bodies × 2 runtimes) under the existing `SPEC: Duck-Typed Signal — Acceptance and Contract Violations` describe block at the bottom of programmatic-api.test.ts:
  - **T-API-64k**: `run()` registers `signal.addEventListener('abort', …)` at the call site, observable synchronously after `run()` returns. Driver code constructs a duck-typed signal whose `addEventListener` increments an external `count` variable when `type === "abort"`, calls `gen = run("ralph", { signal: duck, maxIterations: 1 })` inside try/catch (to capture any synchronous throw), then snapshots `countAfterCall = count` immediately — BEFORE driving `for await (const _ of gen) {}` to drain. Asserts: (a) NO synchronous throw at call site; (b) `countAfterCall === 1` (the load-bearing call-site-timing pin — a buggy implementation that registered the listener inside the wrapper's first-`next()` pre-iteration sequence would observe 0). The fixture emits `{"stop":true}` on first iteration so the run settles cleanly during drain. (1 ID × 2 runtimes = 2 tests.)
  - **T-API-64k2**: `runPromise()` counterpart to T-API-64k. Same duck-signal counter pattern, but driver calls `p = runPromise("ralph", { signal: duck, maxIterations: 1 })` and snapshots `countAfterCall` BEFORE `await p`. The async-function-body-runs-synchronously-up-to-first-await semantics combined with `runWithInternal` being called BEFORE the first `await Promise.resolve()` make this load-bearing on the eager promise surface — a buggy implementation that placed `runWithInternal` AFTER the await would observe `countAfterCall === 0` here. (1 ID × 2 runtimes = 2 tests.)
  - **T-API-64k3**: `options.signal` is READ before every other recognized RunOptions field. Parameterized over both run surfaces × 4 non-signal recognized outer fields {`env`, `cwd`, `envFile`, `maxIterations`} = 8 cells. Each cell constructs an `opts` object whose `signal` is exposed via an enumerable getter pushing `"signal"` to a shared `order` array (returns minimal duck signal `{ aborted: false, addEventListener() {} }`), and whose `<other-field>` is exposed via an enumerable getter pushing `"<other-field>"` to the same `order` array (returns the SPEC-prescribed benign value: `env` → `undefined`, `cwd` → `undefined`, `envFile` → `undefined`, `maxIterations` → `1`). Driver chdir's to project before the call so cwd defaults to project, calls `run` / `runPromise` inside try/catch, snapshots `orderAfterCall = order.slice()` immediately, then drives the generator to drain (or awaits the promise). Asserts: (a) NO synchronous throw at call site; (b) `orderAfterCall[0] === "signal"` (the load-bearing ordering pin); (c) `orderAfterCall.contains(<other-field>)` (sanity that the parameterized field is actually being read). Each `(surface, other-field)` cell is an independent `it()` invocation so failure attribution is clear. (4 fields × 2 surfaces × 2 runtimes = 16 tests.)
- Adjacent suites: zero regressions across tmpdir + env-vars + wfdir + loop-state + execution (904/904 across 5 e2e files), signals (9/9), unit + harness (158/158), typecheck OK.

### ADR-0004 §9.1 / §9.2 / §9.3 / §9.5 (T-API-63 / T-API-63a — Generator-Returns-Without-Throwing Invariants on both run surfaces) — RESOLVED

SPEC §9.1: "run() ... still returns a generator without throwing." SPEC §9.2: "the call itself always returns a promise." Together these establish the always-returns invariant: neither call site ever throws synchronously, errors always surface lazily — on first `next()` for run() or as a promise rejection for runPromise(). This is the gateway invariant for the entire T-API-63..69u block: any subsequent abort-precedence, generator-lifecycle, or promise-rejection test depends on this contract holding. A buggy implementation that allowed an option-shape exception, a throwing getter, a target-validation error, or an already-aborted signal to escape past the call-site boundary would break consumer composition patterns — try/catch-around-iteration, Promise.all-style orchestration — that the API surface contract guarantees.

The implementation in `packages/loop-extender/src/run.ts` ALREADY conformed: `snapshotOptions` (lines 105-232) captures every shape-violation and per-field exception into `snap.error` rather than throwing — outer shape gate at lines 109-125 (null / array / function / non-object); per-field try/catch wrappers at signal (132-138), cwd (152-158), envFile (176-182), env (193-199), maxIterations (209-215). `run()` (lines 255-260) is a non-async function that synchronously calls `runWithInternal`, which constructs and returns the wrapper generator — `snap.error` is consulted lazily inside `runInternal` (line 610-612: `if (snap.error !== undefined) throw snap.error`). `runPromise()` (lines 732-783) is an async function whose body runs synchronously up to its first `await`; `runWithInternal` is called BEFORE the `await Promise.resolve()` microtask boundary (line 761/776), so the snapshot pass + signal capture fire at the call site, but the option-shape error is captured into `snap.error` and surfaces via promise rejection AFTER the microtask boundary — preserving the SPEC §9.2 always-returns-promise contract. The pre-aborted-signal pathway at lines 326-348 wires `internalAc.abort()` synchronously when `snap.signal.aborted === true` and pins `firstObservedRef.trigger = "abort"`, but does NOT throw at the call site — the abort error is constructed and surfaced inside `runInternal` (lines 605-607: `if (snap.signal?.aborted) throw makeAbortError(snap.signal)`).

A buggy implementation that surfaced any of the eight invalid-input branches eagerly at the call site would fail the corresponding T-API-63 / T-API-63a variant on assertion (a) (NO synchronous throw). A buggy implementation that returned `undefined` or a non-iterable object instead of an AsyncGenerator under invalid input would fail assertion (b) (.next/.return/.throw method presence). A buggy implementation that swallowed the captured error during error surfacing would fail assertion (c) (error surfaces on first next() / promise rejects with expected pattern). A buggy implementation that pre-spawned a child before option-snapshot validation completed would fail assertion (d) (NO child spawned).

Now-passing tests (this iteration):
- **programmatic-api.test.ts: 782/782 PASS** (was 750, +32) — added 32 tests under a new `SPEC: Generator-Returns-Without-Throwing Invariants` describe block at the bottom of programmatic-api.test.ts (16 unique it() bodies × 2 runtimes — 8 invalid-input variants × {run() / runPromise()}):
  - **T-API-63**: `run()` returns a generator without throwing under each parameterized invalid input (8 variants × 2 runtimes = 16 tests). Variants: (a) invalid-target — non-string `null` target routed through runInternal target validation (errorPattern `/target/i`); (b) invalid-options-shape — null options routed through snapshotOptions outer shape gate (`/(options|RunOptions)/i`); (c) throwing-option-getter — throwing `options.cwd` getter via `Object.defineProperty` routed through snapshotOptions per-field try/catch (`/cwd-getter-boom/`); (d) already-aborted-signal — pre-aborted `AbortController` routed through SPEC §9.3 abort-precedence pathway (`/abort/i`); (e) invalid-cwd — non-string cwd (number `42`) routed through per-field type gate (`/(cwd.*string|RunOptions\.cwd)/i`); (f) invalid-envFile — non-string envFile (number `42`) routed through per-field type gate (`/(envFile.*string|RunOptions\.envFile)/i`); (g) invalid-maxIterations — negative `-1` routed through integer-range gate (`/(maxIterations.*integer|Invalid maxIterations)/i`); (h) invalid-env — non-object env (string `"not-an-object"`) routed through snapshotEnv shape gate (`/(env.*object|RunOptions\.env)/i`). Each test asserts (a) NO synchronous throw at call site; (b) returned object is non-null with `.next`, `.return`, `.throw` methods (AsyncGenerator interface contract); (c) error surfaces on first `next()` matching variant-specific pattern; (d) no child spawned (marker file absent).
  - **T-API-63a**: `runPromise()` returns a promise without throwing under each parameterized invalid input (8 variants × 2 runtimes = 16 tests). Same parameterization as T-API-63. Each test asserts (a) NO synchronous throw at call site; (b) returned value is a thenable (`typeof p.then === "function"` — SPEC §9.2 always-returns-promise); (c) promise rejects with variant-specific pattern; (d) no child spawned.
- Adjacent suites: zero regressions across tmpdir + env-vars + wfdir + loop-state + execution (904/904 across 5 e2e files), typecheck OK. Full programmatic-api.test.ts run: 782/782 in ~102s.

### ADR-0004 §9.1 / §9.2 / §9.5 (T-API-62i / 62i2 / 62i3 / 62i4 — Call-site read timing for non-signal option fields) — RESOLVED

SPEC §9.1: "`run()` reads its `options` argument at the call site as a synchronous snapshot ... Each option field is read at most once per call." SPEC §9.2: "Option-snapshot timing. Identical to `run()` (section 9.1)." T-API-62h (the success-path single-read counter) and T-API-62h3..h11 (the throwing-path no-retry counter) pin the at-most-once contract via a *post-settlement* observation of the field-read counters. T-API-64k will pin call-site invocation timing for `signal` (via duck-typed `addEventListener` counter). NEITHER existing test directly proves call-site invocation timing for the four NON-SIGNAL fields — a buggy implementation that deferred all non-signal reads to first `next()` would still pass T-API-62h (counters end at 1) and T-API-64k (signal-only). T-API-62i (run / success path), T-API-62i2 (runPromise / success path), T-API-62i3 (run / throwing path × 4 fields), and T-API-62i4 (runPromise / throwing path × 4 fields) close that gap by snapshotting the field-read counters synchronously *immediately after* `run()` / `runPromise()` returns — *before* `gen.next()` is driven or `await p` runs — so the counters can ONLY be at 1 if the option getters fired at the call site rather than being deferred.

The implementation in `packages/loop-extender/src/run.ts` ALREADY conformed: `run()` (lines 255-260) is a non-async function that synchronously calls `runWithInternal`, which synchronously calls `snapshotOptions(options)` at line 267. `runPromise()` (lines 732-783) is an async function whose body runs synchronously up to the first `await`; line 761 calls `runWithInternal` BEFORE the `await Promise.resolve()` microtask boundary at line 776, so the option-snapshot pass fires at the call site even on the eager promise-returning surface. `snapshotOptions` reads each recognized field via name-keyed `[[Get]]` access (signal at 134, cwd at 154, envFile at 178, env at 195, maxIterations at 211) inside dedicated try/catch blocks that capture throws into `snap.error` rather than letting them escape — this is the captured-rather-than-escaping behavior the test pins (the call returned without throwing AND the throwing getter was still invoked exactly once at call time).

A buggy implementation that deferred non-signal option reads to first `next()` (e.g., gating on `if (snap.cwd === undefined && snap.error === undefined && needsCwd)` inside `runLoop` rather than reading at snapshot time) would observe all four counters at 0 immediately after `run()` / `runPromise()` returned and fail T-API-62i / 62i2. A buggy implementation that re-invoked the throwing getter during error surfacing would observe `throwCount === 2` post-`next()` / post-rejection and fail T-API-62i3 / 62i4 assertion (d). A buggy implementation that surfaced the throwing-getter exception synchronously at the call site (rather than capturing into `snap.error`) would fail T-API-62i3 / 62i4 assertion (a). The test fixtures parameterize over each of the four non-signal fields {`cwd`, `envFile`, `maxIterations`, `env`}; each variant defines a counter-based throwing getter on the named field plus a non-throwing counter-based getter on a sibling field for control (sibling read order is implementation-defined per SPEC §9.1, so siblingCount is intentionally not asserted — the load-bearing claim is `throwCount === 1`).

Now-passing tests (this iteration):
- **programmatic-api.test.ts: 750/750 PASS** (was 730, +20) — added 20 tests under a new `SPEC: Option-Field Call-Site Read Timing` describe block at the bottom of programmatic-api.test.ts (10 unique it() bodies × 2 runtimes):
  - **T-API-62i**: `run()` reads cwd, envFile, maxIterations, env getters synchronously at call site. Counter-based getters on all four non-signal fields (each returning a value the implementation must consume — project dir for cwd, valid env-file path for envFile, 1 for maxIterations, `{ MYVAR: "value" }` for env). Driver snapshots `callTimeCounts` synchronously after `const gen = run("ralph", opts)`, before driving `for await (const o of gen)`. Asserts: (a) all four call-time counters === 1 (call-site timing pin); (b) all four final counters === 1 (no re-read on iteration — complements T-API-62h's at-most-once post-settlement assertion); (c) run completed normally and getter return values were consumed (env reached the spawned script — marker reads "value"). 1 ID × 2 runtimes = 2 tests.
  - **T-API-62i2**: `runPromise()` counterpart. Same fixture, but driver snapshots `callTimeCounts` synchronously after `const p = runPromise("ralph", opts)`, before `const outputs = await p`. Async-function-body-runs-synchronously-up-to-first-await semantics combined with `runWithInternal` being called BEFORE the first `await Promise.resolve()` make this test load-bearing — a buggy implementation that placed `runWithInternal` AFTER the await would observe all four counters at 0 here. 1 ID × 2 runtimes = 2 tests.
  - **T-API-62i3**: `run()` — throwing non-signal option-field getter is invoked exactly once at the call site without escaping synchronously, surfaced lazily on first `next()`. Parameterized over each non-signal field {cwd, envFile, maxIterations, env}: each variant constructs a counter-based throwing getter on the named field (`Object.defineProperty(opts, "<field>", { enumerable: true, configurable: true, get() { throwCount++; throw new Error("<field>-getter-boom"); } })`) plus a non-throwing counter-based getter on a sibling field. Driver wraps `gen = run("ralph", opts)` in try/catch to capture any synchronous throw, snapshots `callTimeCounts` immediately, then drives `await gen.next()` in a separate try/catch. Asserts: (a) NO synchronous throw at call site; (b) `throwCount === 1` immediately after `run()` returns (call-site invocation pin — a buggy lazy implementation would observe 0); (c) the captured exception surfaces on first `next()` with the expected message; (d) `throwCount === 1` post-`next()` (no-retry contract reaffirmed at the call-site-observed timing); (e) no child spawn (marker absent). 4 IDs × 2 runtimes = 8 tests.
  - **T-API-62i4**: `runPromise()` counterpart to T-API-62i3 — same parameterization over the four non-signal fields, but driver wraps `p = runPromise("ralph", opts)` in try/catch and snapshots counts before `await p`. Asserts (a)+(b)+(c)+(d)+(e) with promise rejection semantics. Additionally asserts `isPromise === true` (proves `runPromise()` returned a thenable rather than throwing or returning undefined — pins the SPEC §9.2 always-returns-promise contract on the throwing-getter axis). 4 IDs × 2 runtimes = 8 tests.
- Adjacent suites: zero regressions across tmpdir + env-vars + wfdir + loop-state + execution (904/904 across 5 e2e files), unit + harness (158/158), typecheck OK. Full programmatic-api.test.ts run: 750/750 in ~98s.

### ADR-0004 §9.1 / §9.2 / §9.5 (T-API-62 series — Throwing option-field getters and single-read / no-retry contract on the option-snapshot path) — RESOLVED

SPEC §9.1 / §9.2 / §9.5 contract: each recognized option field (`signal`, `cwd`, `envFile`, `env`, `maxIterations`) is read exactly once via name-keyed `[[Get]]` access at the option-snapshot pass; throwing getters / Proxy traps surface as snapshot errors via the standard pre-iteration error path (lazy throw on first `next()` under `run()`, promise rejection under `runPromise()`); the call site itself never throws synchronously for option-snapshot exceptions (per SPEC §9.1 lazy-surface and SPEC §9.2 always-returns-promise). Inside `RunOptions.env`, throwing accessor getters on a NAMED ENTRY are captured during the per-key `[[Get]]` value-read pass; throwing Proxy `ownKeys` traps are captured during the enumeration pass; throwing Proxy `get` traps on an INCLUDED key are captured during the per-key `[[Get]]` value-read pass (SPEC §9.5 normatively requires `[[Get]]` semantics for env-entry value reads, so descriptor-based bypass implementations would slip past throwing-getter and throwing-proxy-get coverage). Single-read contract: each option field's getter is invoked exactly once per call on the success path (no double-read across snapshot + later use). No-retry contract: throwing getters / proxy traps are invoked exactly once on the throwing path — NOT re-invoked during error surfacing or cleanup (a buggy "retry once on next()" or "re-read for cleanup" implementation would fire the throwing getter twice).

The implementation in `packages/loop-extender/src/run.ts` (`snapshotOptions` at lines 105-232 + `snapshotEnv` at lines 72-103) ALREADY conformed: each `opts.<field>` read is wrapped in a dedicated `try/catch` that captures the thrown error into `snap.error` (signal at lines 132-138, cwd at lines 152-158, envFile at lines 176-182, env at lines 193-199, maxIterations at lines 209-215), so a throwing getter / proxy trap on any option field is captured exactly once and surfaced lazily; `snapshotEnv` uses `Object.keys(envRaw)` (which invokes the proxy `ownKeys` trap once and propagates throws naturally) followed by `(envRaw)[key]` per included key (which invokes `[[Get]]` semantics — accessor getter or proxy `get` trap — exactly once and propagates throws naturally to the caller, which captures into `snap.error`). The snapshot is invoked synchronously at the head of `runWithInternal` (line 267); `runPromise` calls `runWithInternal` synchronously before the `await Promise.resolve()` microtask boundary, so the eager-call-site contract holds on the eager surface — the snapshot pass completes (and any throwing getter fires) before the first user-visible point at which a synchronous throw could be observed, and the captured error then surfaces via promise rejection.

A buggy implementation that wired up shape validation correctly on `run()`'s lazy first-`next()` snapshot pass but used a different code path on `runPromise()`'s eager call-site snapshot would pass the run-surface variants and fail the runPromise-surface variants (or vice versa). A buggy implementation using descriptor-based env-value extraction (e.g., `Object.getOwnPropertyDescriptor(env, key).value`) would skip the `[[Get]]` semantics required by SPEC §9.5 and fail the throwing-accessor entry-getter and throwing-proxy-`get` variants. A buggy implementation that re-read option fields during error surfacing or cleanup would fire the throwing getter twice and fail the no-retry counter assertions. The success-path single-read counter pins the no-double-read contract on each axis: an implementation that read `opts.cwd` once for snapshot and again for cwd resolution (or read `opts.env` once for shape validation and again for spawn-time merge) would observably increment the call counter past 1.

Now-passing tests (this iteration):
- **programmatic-api.test.ts: 730/730 PASS** (was 688, +42) — added 42 tests under two new describe blocks at the bottom of programmatic-api.test.ts (21 unique it() bodies × 2 runtimes):
  - **`SPEC: Throwing Option-Field Getters` (T-API-62, 62a, 62b, 62c, 62d, 62e, 62f, 62f3, 62g)**: 9 unique it() blocks × 2 runtimes = 18 tests pinning the SPEC §9.1 / §9.5 throwing-getter / throwing-proxy-trap capture contract on the option-snapshot path. Coverage: throwing getter on each option field via `Object.defineProperty(opts, "<field>", { enumerable: true, get() { throw new Error(...); } })` — `signal` (T-API-62), `cwd` (T-API-62a), `envFile` (T-API-62b), `env` (T-API-62c), `maxIterations` (T-API-62d); throwing accessor getter on a NAMED ENTRY inside `options.env` (T-API-62e — uses `Object.defineProperty(env, "MYVAR", { enumerable: true, get() { throw … } })` to construct env without invoking the getter at test-harness construction time, exercising `snapshotEnv`'s per-key `[[Get]]` path); throwing Proxy `ownKeys` trap on `options.env` (T-API-62f — `new Proxy({}, { ownKeys() { throw … } })` exercises the enumeration pass); throwing Proxy `get` trap on an INCLUDED `options.env` key (T-API-62f3 — `new Proxy({}, { ownKeys() { return ["MYVAR"]; }, getOwnPropertyDescriptor() { return { enumerable: true, configurable: true, value: undefined }; }, get() { throw … } })` exercises the per-key value-read pass — distinct from T-API-62f because the throw fires AFTER enumeration succeeds); throwing Proxy `get` trap on the OUTER options object for the `signal` field (T-API-62g — `new Proxy({}, { get(_, key) { if (key === "signal") throw …; } })` covers the proxy-on-outer-options surface). Each test asserts (a) NO synchronous call-site throw (load-bearing — proves the implementation captures into `snap.error` rather than throwing eagerly), (b) lazy throw on first `next()` under `run()` / promise rejection under `runPromise()`, (c) NO child spawn (marker file absent — the snapshot error fires pre-iteration before any spawn).
  - **`SPEC: Option-Field Single-Read Contract` (T-API-62h, 62h2, 62h3, 62h4, 62h5, 62h6, 62h7, 62h8, 62h9 (run+runPromise), 62h10, 62h11)**: 12 unique it() blocks × 2 runtimes = 24 tests pinning the success-path single-read counter and the throwing-path no-retry counter. Success-path: T-API-62h (run) / T-API-62h2 (runPromise) install counter-incrementing getters on ALL five recognized fields (`signal`, `cwd`, `envFile`, `env`, `maxIterations`) simultaneously via `Object.defineProperty`, drive the run to clean settlement, and assert each counter is exactly 1 — proves no field is double-read across snapshot + spawn-time use. Throwing-path no-retry tests parameterize a counter-incrementing throwing getter / proxy trap on a structurally-distinct surface and assert `count === 1` after the lazy throw / promise rejection surfaces: throwing `options.env` getter on the OUTER options object × {run, runPromise} (T-API-62h3 / 62h4); throwing `options.signal` getter on the outer options object × {run, runPromise} (T-API-62h7 / 62h8); throwing Proxy `ownKeys` trap on `options.env` × {run, runPromise} (T-API-62h5 / 62h6); throwing Proxy `get` trap on an INCLUDED `options.env` key × {run, runPromise} (T-API-62h9 — two it() blocks); throwing accessor getter on a NAMED ENTRY inside `options.env` × {run, runPromise} (T-API-62h10 / 62h11). Catches a buggy implementation that re-reads option fields during error surfacing or cleanup (would fire the throwing getter twice — `count > 1`), or that double-reads option fields across snapshot + spawn-time use on the success path (would increment the counter past 1).
- Adjacent suites: zero regressions across tmpdir + env-vars + wfdir + loop-state + execution + signals (904/904 across 5 e2e files), unit + harness (158/158), typecheck OK. Full programmatic-api.test.ts run: 730/730.

### ADR-0004 §9.5 / §9.1 / §9.2 (T-API-61 series — Outer Options Shape Validation primitive matrix + explicit-undefined acceptance) — RESOLVED

SPEC §9.5: `options` must be omitted, `undefined`, or a non-null, non-array, non-function object; each option field's type is `T | undefined` so explicit-`undefined` field values are equivalent to field omission. SPEC §9.1: option-shape errors do NOT throw at the call site under `run()` — they surface lazily on first `next()`. SPEC §9.2: `runPromise()` always returns a promise — option-shape errors surface as promise rejections, never synchronous throws.

The implementation in `packages/loop-extender/src/run.ts` (`snapshotOptions` at lines 105-232) ALREADY conformed: rejects `null` + arrays + functions + non-objects via the explicit type-check chain at lines 109-125 (`if (options === null)` → `Array.isArray(options)` → `typeof === "function"` → `typeof !== "object"`), capturing the rejection as `snap.error` rather than throwing synchronously; reads each recognized field via name-keyed `[[Get]]` access (`opts.signal`, `opts.cwd`, `opts.envFile`, `opts.env`, `opts.maxIterations`) so `undefined` field values are naturally treated as absent (the `if (xxxRaw !== undefined)` guards at lines 139, 159, 183, 200, 216 short-circuit assignment); `snap.error` is then surfaced lazily via the standard pre-iteration error path on first `next()` for `run()` or as promise rejection for `runPromise()`. The `runPromise()` implementation at lines 732-783 calls `runWithInternal` synchronously before its `await Promise.resolve()` microtask boundary, preserving the eager-snapshot semantics on the eager surface — but the actual rejection is observed only after the await microtask, so it always surfaces via promise rejection (never synchronous throw).

A buggy implementation that gated rejection on a partial primitive enumeration (e.g., a `typeof !== "object"`-only validator that wrongly accepts function options, or a string/number whitelist that wrongly accepts boolean/symbol/bigint) would slip past T-API-53/54/55 (env-shape variants) and the existing T-API-08 series. T-API-61 closes the structurally-distinct branches: `typeof === "function"` (T-API-61b/61e2-fn), `typeof === "string"` (T-API-61c/61e2-str), `typeof === "number"` (T-API-61c2-num/61e2-num), `typeof === "boolean"` (T-API-61c2-true/false, 61e2-true/false), `typeof === "symbol"` (T-API-61c2-sym/61e2-sym), `typeof === "bigint"` (T-API-61c2-bi/61e2-bi). A buggy implementation that wired up shape validation correctly on `run()`'s lazy first-`next()` snapshot pass but used a different code path on `runPromise()`'s eager call-site snapshot would pass the run-surface variants and fail the runPromise-surface variants (or vice versa).

A buggy implementation that rejected explicit-`undefined` fields as "not provided but defined" (e.g., gating on `"cwd" in options` rather than `opts.cwd !== undefined`) would pass T-API-61f/61g (which use explicit-undefined OUTER options, not field values) and fail T-API-61h/61h2 (which use explicit-undefined for all 5 field values). The undefined-field test bodies delete `process.env.MYVAR` before driving so a buggy precedence layer that injected `MYVAR=undefined` into the spawned child as a literal string would surface `"present\\tundefined"` or trigger a runtime rejection — observably distinguishable from the spec-required `"absent"` outcome.

Now-passing tests (this iteration):
- **programmatic-api.test.ts: 688/688 PASS** (was 644, +44) — added 44 tests under a new `SPEC: Outer Options Shape Validation` describe block (22 unique it() bodies × 2 runtimes — 9 run-surface rejection variants, 9 runPromise-surface rejection variants, 4 explicit-undefined acceptance tests):
  - **T-API-61, T-API-61a, T-API-61b, T-API-61c, T-API-61c2 (5 sub-variants)**: 9 run-surface variants × 2 runtimes = 18 tests. `run("ralph", null|[]|fn|str|num|true|false|sym|bigint)`. Asserts: (a) NO synchronous call-site throw (load-bearing — proves the implementation captures into `snap.error` rather than throwing eagerly), (b) lazy throw on first `next()` with error message matching `/options|RunOptions/i`, (c) NO child spawn (marker file absent — shape error fires pre-iteration before any spawn).
  - **T-API-61d, T-API-61e, T-API-61e2 (7 sub-variants)**: 9 runPromise-surface variants × 2 runtimes = 18 tests. `runPromise("ralph", null|[]|fn|str|num|true|false|sym|bigint)`. Asserts: (a) NO synchronous call-site throw (per SPEC §9.2 always-returns-promise contract), (b) promise rejection with error matching `/options|RunOptions/i`, (c) NO child spawn.
  - **T-API-61f**: `run("ralph", undefined)` is equivalent to `run("ralph")`. 1 ID × 2 runtimes = 2 tests. Asserts: (a) generator does NOT throw on call or first next(), (b) exactly 1 Output entry yielded, (c) `lastStop === true`, (d) script ran exactly once (marker exists).
  - **T-API-61g**: `runPromise("ralph", undefined)` counterpart. 1 ID × 2 runtimes = 2 tests.

Bash fixture observes both PWD (via `/bin/pwd -P`) and `${MYVAR+x}` set-vs-empty distinction. Driver deletes `process.env.MYVAR` before calling, then awaits the promise. ### ADR-0004 §7.4 (LOOPX_TMPDIR creation / injection / cleanup)

Implemented in `packages/loop-extender/src/tmpdir.ts` and integrated via `loop.ts`, `execution.ts`, `run.ts`:

1. **Three-step creation** (SPEC §7.4): `mkdtemp(<parent>/loopx-)` → identity capture (`lstat` dev/inode) → mode 0700 secure (`chmodSync`).
2. **Five-case cleanup-safety dispatch** (SPEC §7.4): ENOENT no-op; symlink unlink (no-follow); non-directory leave-with-warning; identity-match recursive remove; identity-mismatch leave-with-warning.
3. **Cleanup idempotence** — `CleanupState { attempted, warned }` guarantees at most one cleanup attempt and at most one stderr warning per resource.
4. **Per-creation-failure handling** (SPEC §7.4 "does not mask the original creation error"): identity-capture-fail triggers single non-recursive `rmdir`; mode-secure-fail triggers full cleanup-safety routine; both throw the original creation error after cleanup.
5. **Test seams** (TEST-SPEC §1.4, NODE_ENV=test only): `LOOPX_TEST_TMPDIR_FAULT={identity-capture-fail, identity-capture-fail-rmdir-fail, mode-secure-fail}` and `LOOPX_TEST_CLEANUP_FAULT={lstat-fail, symlink-unlink-fail, recursive-remove-fail}`.
6. **Structured warning marker** — emitted under NODE_ENV=test as `LOOPX_TEST_CLEANUP_WARNING\t<payload>` for test-side detection.
7. **Integration**:
   - `runLoop` creates the tmpdir between SPEC §7.1 step 5 (version check) and step 6 (first child spawn). Wraps the loop body in `try/finally` so every terminal outcome triggers cleanup.
   - `executeScript` accepts `tmpdir: string` in ExecOptions, injects `LOOPX_TMPDIR` as a protocol-tier env var (overrides any user-supplied value).
   - `runPromise` captures `os.tmpdir()` eagerly at the call site (SPEC §9.2); `run()` and CLI use lazy capture inside `runLoop`.
8. **Lazy NODE_PATH shim** — `getLoopxShimDir()` is now invoked inside `executeScript` (was module-load). Prevents loopx from crashing when TMPDIR points at an unwritable parent before tmpdir-creation has had a chance to surface its own EACCES.

### Test harness improvement (api-driver.ts)

`apps/tests/tests/helpers/api-driver.ts` now strips caller-supplied `extraEnv.TMPDIR` from the spawned child's env and bakes a `process.env.TMPDIR = <orig>` prefix into the driver code. This decouples tsx's eager `${TMPDIR}/tsx-${UID}` IPC dir from the loopx-perceived TMPDIR — tests can pass an unwritable TMPDIR without crashing tsx at module-load. loopx still observes the test's intended TMPDIR because every `os.tmpdir()` read in loopx is lazy (inside `runLoop`, `runPromise`'s eager-snapshot call, or pre-iteration in the CLI), all of which execute after the prefix.

### ADR-0004 §9.5 (RunOptions.env tier-2 env merging) — RESOLVED

Implemented in `packages/loop-extender/src/types.ts` and `packages/loop-extender/src/run.ts`:

1. **Public type** — added `env?: Record<string, string>` to `RunOptions` (types.ts).
2. **Option-snapshot machinery** (run.ts):
   - `snapshotOptions(options)` reads recognized fields once each via `[[Get]]` (signal first per SPEC §9.1, then cwd, envFile, env, maxIterations).
   - `snapshotEnv(envRaw)` validates shape (rejects null / array / function / non-object), enumerates own-enumerable string-keyed entries via `Object.keys` (which invokes Proxy `ownKeys` and `getOwnPropertyDescriptor` traps and propagates throws naturally), and reads each included value once via `[[Get]]` (which invokes accessor getters or Proxy `get` traps and propagates throws naturally).
   - `isAbortSignalCompatible(signal)` enforces SPEC §9.5 signal contract: `aborted` must be readable boolean, `addEventListener` must be callable.
3. **Eager cwd snapshot** — `cwd` snapshotted at call time (defaults to `process.cwd()` per SPEC §9.5); relative `cwd` resolved against `process.cwd()` once at call time.
4. **Signal wiring** — User signal → internal AbortController abort propagation now wired via `addEventListener` (replaces `AbortSignal.any` to support duck-typed signals); a throwing `addEventListener` is captured as a snapshot error.
5. **Lazy error surfacing** — Captured snapshot errors surface lazily via the standard pre-iteration error path on first `next()` (or as promise rejection from `runPromise`). Pre-first-`.return()` consumer-cancellation carve-out preserved (errors not thrown when consumer's first interaction is `.return()` / `.throw()`).
6. **Abort precedence** — SPEC §9.3 preserved: signal-aborted-at-call-time wins over snapshot errors.
7. **Merge order** (run.ts `runInternal`): `mergeEnv(globalEnv, localEnv)` (tiers 5→4→3) overlaid with `snap.env` (tier 2). Protocol-tier vars (LOOPX_*, tier 1) continue to overlay last in `executeScript` at execution.ts.

### ADR-0004 §9.1 (.throw() consumer cancellation contract) — RESOLVED

The `.throw()` wrapper at `packages/loop-extender/src/run.ts` previously delegated directly to `gen.throw(err)`, leaving the active child unkilled and propagating the consumer-supplied error. SPEC §9.1 requires consumer-driven cancellation (including `.throw()`) to:
1. Terminate the active child process group (SIGTERM, then SIGKILL after 5s).
2. Ensure no further iterations start.
3. Produce silent clean completion (the consumer-supplied error is not surfaced) when no child is active.

The wrapper now mirrors `.return()`: calls `internalAc.abort()` to terminate the active child, then `gen.return(undefined)` to settle silently, swallowing any error so the caller sees `{ done: true, value: undefined }`. This is the no-active-child silent-completion contract from SPEC §9.1; for the active-child case the spec leaves the settlement form implementation-defined and we choose silent completion for symmetry with `.return()`.

Now-passing tests (this iteration):
- **tmpdir.test.ts: 310/310 PASS** — added T-TMP-17..22f (28 new tests × 2 runtimes covering CLI signal cleanup, escalation × cleanup, programmatic abort cleanup, consumer cancellation × {.return(), .throw(), break} × {active-child, no-active-child, post-final-yield, stop:true-final-yield} matrix). The two escalation tests (T-TMP-18a/18b) carry `retry: 3` due to the 5-second grace-period wait, mirroring T-SIG-05 / T-SIG-05a.
- Adjacent suites: zero regressions across programmatic-api (346), env-vars (96), execution (85), loop-state (96), wfdir (40), signals (9), unit (143), harness (15). The `.throw()` change does not affect existing behavior because no prior test exercised `.throw()` on the wrapper.

### ADR-0004 §9.3 (abort-after-final-yield carve-out) — RESOLVED

The `run()` wrapper at `packages/loop-extender/src/run.ts` previously had no notion of post-final-yield state: after `yield output; return;` (or `yield output;` on the maxIterations boundary) the inner gen would return cleanly on the next interaction regardless of abort-signal state. SPEC §9.3 requires that an abort observed in the post-final-yield / pre-settlement window produces an abort error on the next interaction (`.next()` / `.return()` / `.throw()`), with first-observed-wins precedence so a prior consumer cancellation's silent-completion outcome is not displaced.

Implementation:
1. Wrapper now tracks `yieldCount`, `postFinalYield`, `settled` state across `.next()` / `.return()` / `.throw()`.
2. On each yield, if `output.stop === true` OR `yieldCount === snap.maxIterations`, set `postFinalYield = true`.
3. Before delegating to the inner gen, each method checks `postFinalYield && internalAc.signal.aborted && !returnCalled` — if true, drives `gen.return(undefined)` to run the inner `finally` (tmpdir cleanup), then throws `makeAbortError(snap.signal ?? internalAc.signal)`.
4. The `!returnCalled` guard implements SPEC §9.3 first-observed-wins: a prior consumer `.return()` / `.throw()` (which already set `returnCalled=true`) keeps its silent-completion outcome.
5. For `.throw()` post-final-yield-abort, the abort error displaces the consumer-supplied error (per SPEC §9.3).
6. `if (settled)` early-return added to each wrapper method for idempotent multi-call behavior.

Now-passing tests (this iteration):
- **tmpdir.test.ts: 327/327 PASS** — added 17 new tests covering the §9.3 matrix:
  - **T-TMP-23**: post-final-yield → settlement (no abort) cleanup is single-shot and idempotent.
  - **T-TMP-24**: cleanup via full `for await` completion.
  - **T-TMP-24a/24c/24d**: abort after maxIterations-driven final yield + `.next()` / `.return()` / `.throw(consumerErr)` → cleanup runs before abort error (which displaces consumerErr in 24d).
  - **T-TMP-24e/24f/24g**: abort after stop:true-driven final yield + `.next()` / `.return()` / `.throw(consumerErr)` → same contract.
  - **T-TMP-24b**: external SIGKILL of loopx itself does NOT run tmpdir cleanup; tmpdir survives loopx death (CLI surface only, node only — Bun excluded because the harness's `runCLIWithSignal` plumbing relies on node spawn semantics). T-TMP-24b also surfaced a test-plumbing detail: when loopx is SIGKILLed its detached child shell holds an inherited stderr write-end, so `'close'` won't fire until the child also dies; the test now SIGKILLs the orphan child after observing the tmpdir-survival post-condition, then awaits result.
- Adjacent suites: zero regressions across programmatic-api (346), env-vars (96), execution (85), loop-state (96), wfdir (40), signals (9), unit (143), harness (15).

### ADR-0004 §9.2 (LOOPX_TMPDIR async creation under runPromise) — RESOLVED

The `runPromise()` body at `packages/loop-extender/src/run.ts` previously created `LOOPX_TMPDIR` synchronously at the call site, violating SPEC §9.2: "LOOPX_TMPDIR itself is created asynchronously after return, during the same pre-iteration sequence used by the CLI and run()." Authoring T-TMP-27a (which snapshots the parent directory's `loopx-*` entries synchronously between `runPromise()` returning and `await p`) caught this: `betweenSync` contained a freshly-created `loopx-*` entry that should not have existed yet.

Root cause: the `for await (const output of gen)` statement synchronously evaluates `gen[Symbol.asyncIterator]()` and the wrapper's `next()`, which synchronously calls the inner generator's `next()`, which synchronously runs `runInternal` + `runLoop` bodies up to the first internal `await` — invoking `createTmpdir` before `runPromise()` returned.

Fix: insert `await Promise.resolve()` between the sync option/parent capture and the `for await` loop. The synchronous `runWithInternal()` call is preserved before the microtask boundary so `snapshotOptions()` and the cwd default stay eager (T-API-14c, T-API-14d still pass). After the microtask, the for-await body runs and triggers the deferred `createTmpdir`.

Now-passing tests (this iteration):
- **tmpdir.test.ts: 389/389 PASS** — added 62 tests covering "Tmpdir Parent Snapshot Timing" (T-TMP-25/25a/25b/26/26-temp/26-tmp/27/27-temp/27-tmp/27a/28/28a/28b/28c/28d/28e/28f/28g/28h/29/29a/29b/29c/29d/29e/29f/29g/29h/29i/29j/29k × 2 runtimes). T-TMP-27a specifically verifies the SPEC §9.2 async-creation contract; T-TMP-27/27-temp/27-tmp verify eager-parent capture; T-TMP-26/26-temp/26-tmp verify lazy-parent capture under `run()`; T-TMP-28/28a-h verify global-env-file-tier × {TMPDIR,TEMP,TMP} × {CLI, runPromise, run} contract; T-TMP-29/29b/29c verify `RunOptions.env` tier × {TMPDIR,TEMP,TMP}; T-TMP-29a/29d/29e verify CLI `-e` tier; T-TMP-29f-h verify `runPromise({envFile})` tier; T-TMP-29i-k verify `run({envFile})` tier.
- **Test infrastructure added**:
  - `getRuntimeOsTmpdir(runtime, envOverrides)` — spawns a child Node/Bun process with the given env and returns its `os.tmpdir()` value, used by all `TEMP` / `TMP` variant tests for the runtime-aware expected-parent assertion (since on POSIX runtimes only `TMPDIR` is consulted).
  - `withInheritedTmpdirEnv(overrides, body)` — snapshots and restores `process.env.TMPDIR/TEMP/TMP` around a test body.
  - `makeTestParent(label)` — creates a writable test-isolated parent directory under the system tmpdir, registered for cleanup.
  - `buildEnvObserveScript(observe[])` — bash fixture template that observes `LOOPX_TMPDIR` plus `TMPDIR`/`TEMP`/`TMP` into separate marker files via uniquely-named `OBS_*_PATH` env vars to avoid shadowing the variable being observed.
- Adjacent suites: zero regressions across programmatic-api (346), env-vars (96), execution (85), loop-state (96), wfdir (40), signals (9), unit (143), harness (15).

### ADR-0004 §9.2 (process.env eager snapshot under runPromise) — RESOLVED

The `runPromise()` body at `packages/loop-extender/src/run.ts` previously snapshotted only the tmpdir parent eagerly; the inherited `process.env` and global env-file path (`XDG_CONFIG_HOME` / `HOME`-derived) were still read lazily inside `runInternal` after the microtask boundary, violating SPEC §9.2: "Under runPromise(), the inherited process.env snapshot is eager — captured synchronously at the runPromise() call site, before runPromise() returns. Mutations to process.env after runPromise() returns are not observed."

Implementation:
1. **`packages/loop-extender/src/env.ts`**:
   - `getGlobalEnvPath(envSnapshot?)` accepts optional snapshot; when provided, reads `XDG_CONFIG_HOME` / `HOME` from snapshot rather than live `process.env`.
   - `loadGlobalEnv(envPath?)` accepts optional pre-resolved path verbatim.
   - `mergeEnv(globalEnv, localEnv, inheritedEnv?)` spreads the inherited snapshot when provided, falling back to `process.env` for backward compatibility (preserves `run()` lazy semantics).
2. **`packages/loop-extender/src/run.ts`**: `InternalRunOptions` extended with `inheritedEnv?` and `globalEnvPath?`, threaded through `runWithInternal()` / `runInternal()`. `runPromise()` now captures three eager snapshots before the `await Promise.resolve()`: `eagerTmpdirParent` (existing), `eagerInheritedEnv = { ...process.env }` (new), `eagerGlobalEnvPath = getGlobalEnvPath(eagerInheritedEnv)` (new).

Now-passing tests (this iteration):
- **programmatic-api: 370 PASS** (was 358; +12 new tests under "SPEC: Inherited Env Snapshot Timing" — T-API-71/71a/71b/72/72a/72b × 2 runtimes). T-API-71/71a/71b verify `run()` lazy semantics (mutation between call and first `next()` observed; mid-run mutation frozen at first `next()`; XDG_CONFIG_HOME mutation redirects global env file lookup). T-API-72/72a/72b verify `runPromise()` eager semantics (mutation after return not observed; mid-run mutation not observed across iterations; XDG_CONFIG_HOME mutation does not redirect global env file lookup).
- Adjacent suites: zero regressions (tmpdir 389, env-vars 96, wfdir 40).

### ADR-0004 §7.4 (lstat-fail / symlink-unlink-fail / recursive-remove-fail cleanup-failure surface-parity) — RESOLVED

SPEC §7.4 final paragraph: "If the top-level `lstat` fails for any reason other than ENOENT, the `unlink` in case 2 fails, or the recursive removal in case 4 fails, loopx emits a single stderr warning and makes no further changes." These three failure branches are specified normatively. Black-box reproduction is unreliable on a same-user-owned directory, so coverage is via the TEST-SPEC §1.4 `LOOPX_TEST_CLEANUP_FAULT={lstat-fail, symlink-unlink-fail, recursive-remove-fail}` seam (gated on NODE_ENV=test). The seam was already implemented in `packages/loop-extender/src/tmpdir.ts` at three failure-injection points: top-of-`cleanupTmpdir` (lines 184-189) for lstat-fail, the rule-2 `unlinkSync` (line 210) for symlink-unlink-fail, and the rule-4 `rmSync` (line 250) for recursive-remove-fail. Each emits via `emitCleanupWarning` which deduplicates through `CleanupState.warned` (single warning per resource). T-TMP-40 / T-TMP-41 / T-TMP-42 pin this contract on the **success terminal** across all three execution surfaces — a buggy implementation that wired one stream of "warnings do not affect outcome" handling for the CLI exit-code path and a separate stream for the API rejection path could pass the CLI variant and fail the API variants.

Now-passing tests (this iteration):
- **tmpdir.test.ts: 453/453 PASS** — added 18 tests (9 IDs × 2 runtimes):
  - **T-TMP-40 (CLI) / T-TMP-40a (runPromise) / T-TMP-40b (run)**: `LOOPX_TEST_CLEANUP_FAULT=lstat-fail`. Fixture observes LOOPX_TMPDIR into an external marker and emits stop:true (no path manipulation needed; the seam fires on the top-level `lstat`). Asserts (a) success terminal outcome (CLI exit 0 / promise resolves with one Output / generator settles cleanly with one yield), (b) path observed still exists (cleanup aborted at the seam before any file operations), (c) exactly one `LOOPX_TEST_CLEANUP_WARNING\t…` line on stderr.
  - **T-TMP-41 (CLI) / T-TMP-41a (runPromise) / T-TMP-41b (run)**: `LOOPX_TEST_CLEANUP_FAULT=symlink-unlink-fail`. Fixture observes LOOPX_TMPDIR, replaces it with `ln -s /tmp` symlink so cleanup dispatch reaches rule 2, emits stop:true. Asserts (a) success terminal outcome, (b) symlink at the recorded path still exists (rule-2 unlink was faulted, no further changes), (c) exactly one cleanup warning. Harness teardown removes the leftover symlink.
  - **T-TMP-42 (CLI) / T-TMP-42d (runPromise) / T-TMP-42e (run)**: `LOOPX_TEST_CLEANUP_FAULT=recursive-remove-fail`. Fixture observes LOOPX_TMPDIR, writes a few files inside (`file-1`, `sub/file-2`) so the dispatch reaches rule 4 on a non-empty identity-matched directory, emits stop:true. Asserts (a) success terminal outcome, (b) path observed still exists (rule-4 rmSync was faulted, no further changes), (c) exactly one cleanup warning. The 42d/42e suffix avoids collision with TEST-SPEC-reserved T-TMP-42a/42b/42c (cleanup-failure × terminal-error masking tests, still pending).

### ADR-0004 §7.4 (FIFO/socket/hard-link cleanup-rule-3 generic-dispatch coverage) — RESOLVED

SPEC §7.4 cleanup-safety dispatch case 3: "Path is a regular file, FIFO, socket, or other non-directory non-symlink: leave in place with a stderr warning. Unlinking would risk mutating unrelated data (hard-link `nlink` decrement, or data renamed into the path with `nlink == 1`)." The implementation in `cleanupTmpdir` (`packages/loop-extender/src/tmpdir.ts` lines 230-237) already conforms — after the rule-2 symlink early-return at lines 209-228, the dispatch is a generic `!stat.isDirectory()` negation: any non-directory non-symlink (regular file, FIFO, socket, or hard-link entry) hits the `emitCleanupWarning` + early-return branch. T-TMP-35 / 35a / 35b cover the regular-file branch on all three surfaces; T-TMP-37a / 37b / 37c extend coverage to FIFO, Unix-domain socket, and hard-link replacements on the CLI surface, proving the rule is typed generically rather than narrowly special-cased to regular files. T-TMP-37c additionally pins the SPEC §7.4 hard-link `nlink`-decrement-safety sub-clause that T-TMP-35's single-`nlink` regular-file fixture cannot exercise — a buggy implementation that classified the hard-link tmpdir entry as "ordinary regular file, safe to unlink because it has content we don't care about" would unlink it, decrementing `nlink` from 2 to 1 on the external path; T-TMP-35 would still pass on such an implementation but T-TMP-37c would catch the regression.

Now-passing tests (this iteration):
- **tmpdir.test.ts: 435/435 PASS** — added 6 tests (3 IDs × 2 runtimes):
  - **T-TMP-37a**: CLI FIFO replacement. Bash fixture observes LOOPX_TMPDIR, `rm -rf "$LOOPX_TMPDIR"`, `mkfifo "$LOOPX_TMPDIR"` (path is now a named pipe), emits stop:true. Asserts: (a) exit 0, (b) `lstatSync(path).isFIFO()` is true (`isDirectory()` and `isSymbolicLink()` are false), (c) exactly one `LOOPX_TEST_CLEANUP_WARNING\t…` line on stderr. Sets `NODE_ENV=test` to enable the structured marker line. Cleans up the leftover FIFO post-test.
  - **T-TMP-37b**: CLI Unix-domain socket replacement. `.ts` fixture (creating a SOCK_STREAM Unix-domain socket portably from bash is awkward) — observes LOOPX_TMPDIR, `rmSync` the directory, `net.createServer().listen(tmpdirPath)` to bind a socket inode at the path, then `output({ stop: true })`. UNIX-domain socket files are NOT auto-unlinked by the kernel on `process.exit()`, so the socket inode persists at cleanup time. Asserts: (a) exit 0, (b) `lstatSync(path).isSocket()` is true (and not a directory or symlink), (c) exactly one cleanup warning. Cleans up the leftover socket entry post-test.
  - **T-TMP-37c**: CLI hard-link replacement with `nlink`-decrement-safety assertion. Bash fixture creates an external regular file (`external-content`), `rm -rf "$LOOPX_TMPDIR"`, `ln "$external" "$LOOPX_TMPDIR"` (tmpdir path is now a hard link to the external file, both sharing one inode with `nlink == 2`). The script captures the pre-cleanup `nlink` count of the external path into a marker via portable stat invocation (`stat -c '%h'` GNU / `stat -f '%l'` BSD fallback). Asserts: (a) exit 0, (b) tmpdir-side path still exists as a regular file with content `external-content` (rule-3 leave-in-place), (c) external path also still exists with original content, (d) pre-cleanup `nlink` == 2 == post-cleanup external `nlink` (loopx did NOT decrement nlink by unlinking the tmpdir-side entry — the SPEC-cited rationale for rule 3), (e) tmpdir-side `nlink` also unchanged at 2, (f) `tmpdirLst.ino === externalLst.ino` (hard-link relationship intact), (g) exactly one cleanup warning. Includes an upfront same-device check (`lstatSync(project.dir).dev === lstatSync(tmpdirParent).dev`) — skips with a clear message if cross-device prevents unprivileged hard-link.
- Adjacent suites: zero regressions across programmatic-api (358), env-vars + wfdir (494/494). Full tmpdir.test.ts run: 435/435 in ~64s.

### ADR-0004 §7.4 (nested-symlink-recursive-walk cleanup-rule-4 surface-parity) — RESOLVED

SPEC §7.4 cleanup-safety dispatch case 4: "Path is a directory whose identity matches the recorded identity: recursively remove. Symlink entries encountered during the walk are unlinked but not traversed, so symlinks pointing outside the tmpdir do not collateral-delete their targets." The implementation in `cleanupTmpdir` (`packages/loop-extender/src/tmpdir.ts` lines 249-266) already conforms — when the top-level directory's `dev`/`ino` match the recorded identity, it calls `rmSync(path, { recursive: true, force: true })`. Node.js (and Bun's compat layer) performs lstat-based traversal: nested symlinks are unlinked as entries but their targets are never followed. Verified empirically: a nested `symlink -> external-target-dir` is removed during the recursive walk while the external target plus any contents survive intact. Successful rule-4 cleanup emits NO warning (warnings only fire on cleanup-failure or rules 3 / 5). T-TMP-37 / 37d / 37e pin this contract across all three execution surfaces — a buggy implementation that wired surface-specific recursive-walk dispatchers (e.g., a CLI-only `rmSync({recursive:true})` that conforms to rule 4 and a programmatic-driver path that traversed nested symlinks via a permissive recursive-delete primitive — silently deleting external target contents) would pass T-TMP-37 yet fail T-TMP-37d / 37e.

The fixture creates an external `external-target-dir/external-file` under PROJECT_ROOT, then a nested symlink at `$LOOPX_TMPDIR/nested-link -> $LOOPX_PROJECT_ROOT/external-target-dir`. The top-level entry is the identity-matched directory loopx created (rule 4 applies); only an entry INSIDE the tmpdir is a symlink, so the recursive walk's symlink-handling clause is what's under test. NODE_ENV=test is set so the structured marker is gated on; absence of the marker is then a load-bearing assertion (any erroneous warning would emit `LOOPX_TEST_CLEANUP_WARNING\t…`), not a trivially-true non-emission.

Now-passing tests (this iteration):
- **tmpdir.test.ts: 429/429 PASS** — added 6 tests (3 IDs × 2 runtimes):
  - **T-TMP-37**: CLI nested-symlink recursive walk. Fixture observes LOOPX_TMPDIR, creates external `external-target-dir/external-file` with `external-content`, creates nested symlink `$LOOPX_TMPDIR/nested-link → external-target-dir`, emits stop:true. Asserts: (a) exit 0, (b) tmpdir path no longer exists (rule-4 recursive remove), (c) external dir + file with content `external-content` survive (no symlink-traversal collateral damage), (d) zero `LOOPX_TEST_CLEANUP_WARNING\t…` lines on stderr. Sets `NODE_ENV=test` to enable the structured marker line for load-bearing negative assertion.
  - **T-TMP-37d**: `runPromise()` counterpart. Same fixture, driven via `runAPIDriver` driver code that captures rejection state, observed-path existence, external dir + file existence + content into a JSON envelope. Asserts: (a) promise resolves with one Output, (b) tmpdir removed, (c) external dir + file + content survive, (d) zero cleanup warnings.
  - **T-TMP-37e**: `run()` generator counterpart. Same fixture, drained via `for await` in driver code. Asserts: (a) generator settles cleanly with one yield, (b) tmpdir removed, (c) external dir + file + content survive, (d) zero cleanup warnings.
- Adjacent suites: zero regressions across programmatic-api (370), env-vars (96), wfdir (28) → 494/494 in ~57s. Full tmpdir.test.ts run: 429/429 in ~65s.

### ADR-0004 §7.4 (mismatched-directory cleanup-rule-5 surface-parity) — RESOLVED

SPEC §7.4 cleanup-safety dispatch case 5: "Path is a directory whose identity does not match: leave in place with a stderr warning. loopx does not recursively remove a directory it did not create." The implementation in `cleanupTmpdir` (`packages/loop-extender/src/tmpdir.ts` lines 240-247) already conforms — when `lstat` returns a directory whose `dev`/`ino` (read with `bigint:true`) do not match the recorded identity from creation time, `emitCleanupWarning` fires with payload `cleanup of <path> skipped: identity mismatch` and the function returns without `rmSync`. Per-run cleanup-warning cardinality (SPEC §7.2) is exactly one because `CleanupState.warned` deduplicates. The warning does not affect the surfaced terminal outcome (CLI exit 0 / promise resolves / generator settles cleanly) per SPEC §7.4. T-TMP-36 / 36a / 36b pin this contract across all three execution surfaces — a buggy implementation that wired surface-specific dispatchers (e.g., a CLI-only mismatch-leave-in-place path and a programmatic-driver path that incorrectly `rmSync({ recursive: true, force: true })`'d the mismatched directory — silently destroying any same-user replacement contents that happened to be at the path) would pass T-TMP-36 yet fail T-TMP-36a / 36b.

The fixture uses a rename-aside pattern (`mv "$LOOPX_TMPDIR" "$LOOPX_TMPDIR-original-aside" && mkdir "$LOOPX_TMPDIR"`) rather than a naive `rm -rf … && mkdir …` to guarantee inode-distinctness. On POSIX filesystems where inode allocation does not strictly avoid recently-freed values, a rm/mkdir sequence could let the kernel coincidentally reuse the original inode for the freshly-created directory, making the new directory's identity fingerprint match loopx's captured one — the test would observe rule-4 success rather than rule-5 mismatch, an unrelated kernel-implementation accident. Keeping the original alive at a different path occupies its inode for the lifetime of the script, guaranteeing the freshly-created directory at $LOOPX_TMPDIR is allocated a distinct inode. As an incidental defense-in-depth side-effect, this fixture also asserts the renamed-aside copy survives loopx (already covered by T-TMP-33 "renamed-away tmpdirs are not chased").

Now-passing tests (this iteration):
- **tmpdir.test.ts: 423/423 PASS** — added 6 tests (3 IDs × 2 runtimes):
  - **T-TMP-36**: CLI mismatched-directory replacement. Fixture observes LOOPX_TMPDIR, renames it aside, mkdir + touch `mismatched-marker` at the original path, emits stop:true. Asserts: (a) exit 0, (b) tmpdir path still exists as a directory (`statSync().isDirectory()`), (c) `mismatched-marker` file inside still exists (rule-5 leave-in-place — loopx did not recursively remove the directory's contents), (d) renamed-aside copy survives, (e) exactly one `LOOPX_TEST_CLEANUP_WARNING\t…` line on stderr. Sets `NODE_ENV=test` to enable the structured marker line. Cleans up both leftover paths post-test.
  - **T-TMP-36a**: `runPromise()` counterpart. Same fixture, driven via `runAPIDriver` driver code that captures rejection state, observed-path existence/dir-status, marker-file existence, and renamed-aside existence into a JSON envelope. Asserts: (a) promise resolves with one Output with stop:true, (b) tmpdir path still exists as a directory, (c) `mismatched-marker` intact, (d) renamed-aside survives, (e) exactly one cleanup warning.
  - **T-TMP-36b**: `run()` generator counterpart. Same fixture, drained via `for await`. Asserts: (a) generator settles cleanly with one yield (lastStop:true), (b) tmpdir path still exists as a directory, (c) `mismatched-marker` intact, (d) renamed-aside survives, (e) exactly one cleanup warning.
- Adjacent suites: zero regressions across programmatic-api (370), env-vars (96), wfdir (28). Full tmpdir.test.ts run: 423/423 in ~64s.

### ADR-0004 §7.4 (stale-tmpdir non-reaping + renamed-away ENOENT silence) — RESOLVED

SPEC §7.4 specifies that loopx does not reap stale `loopx-*` entries during CLI startup, CLI `loopx run` setup, or any per-run setup performed for `run()` / `runPromise()`. SPEC §7.4 also specifies that a script that renames its tmpdir defeats automatic cleanup (loopx does not chase renamed tmpdirs) and that the resulting ENOENT at cleanup time is a silent no-op (cleanup-safety rule 1).

The existing implementation already conformed:
- `createTmpdir` (`packages/loop-extender/src/tmpdir.ts`) only invokes `mkdtempSync(join(parent, "loopx-"))` — no parent-scan, no validation, no removal of pre-existing entries.
- `cleanupTmpdir` rule 1 (lines 196-199) returns silently on ENOENT without emitting any warning.
- `bin.ts` dispatches to help / version / unknown-command paths via `process.exit()` before any tmpdir-related code runs, so non-`run` CLI startup never creates or scans tmpdir.

Now-passing tests (this iteration):
- **tmpdir.test.ts: 405/405 PASS** — added 16 tests (7 sub-tests × 2 runtimes for T-TMP-32 series + 1 × 2 for T-TMP-33):
  - **T-TMP-32**: CLI `loopx run` setup leaves pre-existing `loopx-stale-xyz/` intact + cleans up its own tmpdir after run (only stale entry remains under parent).
  - **T-TMP-32a**: Same contract on `runPromise()` (eager-snapshot path per SPEC §9.2).
  - **T-TMP-32b**: Same contract on `run()` (lazy-snapshot path per SPEC §9.1).
  - **T-TMP-32c**: 4 sub-cases over non-`run` CLI startup — `loopx -h` (exit 0), `loopx version` (exit 0), `loopx` (no args, exit 0), `loopx --unknown` (parser error, exit 1). All assert: stale entry survives, no new `loopx-*` materialized under parent, expected exit code.
  - **T-TMP-33**: Fixture renames `$LOOPX_TMPDIR` to `$LOOPX_TMPDIR-renamed` mid-run. Asserts: original path absent, renamed path present with marker intact, **zero** `LOOPX_TEST_CLEANUP_WARNING\t…` lines on stderr (ENOENT-at-cleanup is silent per SPEC §7.4 cleanup-rule-1, completing the warning-cardinality characterization across the cleanup-dispatch tree alongside T-TMP-35/T-TMP-36 which assert exactly one warning for non-ENOENT mismatched-identity / regular-file replacements).
- Adjacent suites: zero regressions. Full tmpdir.test.ts run: 405/405 in ~61s.

### ADR-0004 §7.4 (cleanup-fault-warning-does-not-mask script-error terminal surface-parity) — RESOLVED

SPEC §7.4 final paragraph: "warnings do not affect the CLI exit code, the generator outcome, or the promise rejection reason." T-TMP-40/41/42 + T-TMP-40a/40b/41a/41b/42d/42e pin this rule on the SUCCESS terminal across all three cleanup-fault seams (lstat-fail / symlink-unlink-fail / recursive-remove-fail) × all three execution surfaces. T-TMP-35c/35d/35e pin the rule on the SCRIPT-ERROR terminal × the two natural cleanup-safety dispatch branches (rule 3 regular-file replacement, rule 5 mismatched-directory replacement). T-TMP-42a closes the matrix: the SCRIPT-ERROR terminal × all three cleanup-fault seams × all three surfaces.

The implementation in `runLoop` (`packages/loop-extender/src/loop.ts:120-217`) already conformed: the iteration body wraps in `try/finally` so `cleanupTmpdir(tmpdirResource, cleanupState)` (line 216) runs before the script-failure `throw new Error('Script <wf>:<scr> exited with code <n>')` (line 133-135) propagates out of the generator. The fault seam fires inside `cleanupTmpdir` (top-of-`cleanupTmpdir` for `lstat-fail`, rule-2 unlinkSync for `symlink-unlink-fail`, rule-4 rmSync for `recursive-remove-fail`) and emits via `emitCleanupWarning` which writes to stderr but never rewrites the in-flight throw value.

The CLI tests carry an observably-disjoint-lines assertion: a distinctive `SCRIPT-FAILURE-MARKER-T-TMP-42A` line printed to stderr by the script before its tampering must reach the user's stderr on a separate line from the `LOOPX_TEST_CLEANUP_WARNING\t…` marker. Since both paths produce CLI exit 1, the disjoint-lines assertion is what catches a buggy implementation that wrapped or replaced the script's stderr with a cleanup-classifier wrapper. The API tests carry an error-message-shape probe: the rejection reason (runPromise) / throw value (run) must match the loop.ts contract (regex `/exited with code/`) and must NOT contain "cleanup" anywhere in the message.

Per-fault tampering required to make the seam fire on the failure path:
- **lstat-fail**: seam fires at the top-level lstat in cleanupTmpdir; no path manipulation needed.
- **symlink-unlink-fail**: seam fires only when dispatch reaches rule 2 (path is a symlink), so the script must `rm -rf` the tmpdir and replace it with `ln -s /tmp` before exit 1.
- **recursive-remove-fail**: seam fires only when dispatch reaches rule 4 (identity-matched directory); the original loopx-created directory satisfies that. Populating the directory matches the success-terminal T-TMP-42 fixture.

Now-passing tests (this iteration):
- **tmpdir.test.ts: 483/483 PASS** — added 18 tests (3 fault seams × 3 surfaces × 2 runtimes):
  - **T-TMP-42a (lstat-fail / symlink-unlink-fail / recursive-remove-fail) [CLI]**: `runCLI(['run', '-n', '1', 'ralph'])` with `LOOPX_TEST_CLEANUP_FAULT=<seam>` and `NODE_ENV=test`. Asserts: (a) exit 1 (script failure preserved), (b) exactly one `SCRIPT-FAILURE-MARKER-T-TMP-42A` line on stderr, (c) exactly one `LOOPX_TEST_CLEANUP_WARNING\t…` line, (d) marker and warning lines are observably disjoint, (e) path persistence per fault seam (lstat-fail: original directory exists; symlink-unlink-fail: symlink exists; recursive-remove-fail: directory exists).
  - **T-TMP-42a (lstat-fail / symlink-unlink-fail / recursive-remove-fail) [runPromise]**: driver code awaits `runPromise("ralph", { maxIterations: 1 })`, captures rejection state, error message, observed-path file/symlink type. Asserts: (a) promise rejected, (b) errMsg matches `/exited with code/` (script-failure shape) and does NOT contain "cleanup", (c) exactly one cleanup warning, (d) path persistence per fault seam.
  - **T-TMP-42a (lstat-fail / symlink-unlink-fail / recursive-remove-fail) [run]**: driver code drives `run("ralph", { maxIterations: 1 })` via `for await`, captures throw state and error message. Asserts: (a) generator threw, (b) errMsg matches `/exited with code/` and does NOT contain "cleanup", (c) exactly one cleanup warning, (d) path persistence per fault seam.
- Adjacent suites: zero regressions across programmatic-api + env-vars + wfdir → 494/494. Full tmpdir.test.ts run: 483/483 in ~70s.

### ADR-0004 §7.2 / §7.4 (LOOPX_TEST_TERMINAL_TRIGGER_PAUSE seam — cleanup-start window + first-trigger-wins) — RESOLVED

SPEC §7.2: "the first terminal trigger observed by loopx determines the surfaced outcome among genuinely racing triggers." TEST-SPEC §1.4 specifies a `LOOPX_TEST_TERMINAL_TRIGGER_PAUSE` seam (gated on `NODE_ENV=test`) whose value names a window inside the run lifecycle at which the implementation pauses for a bounded interval (≥2s ≤10s) AFTER writing a parent-observable JSON marker to the path named by `LOOPX_TEST_TERMINAL_TRIGGER_PAUSE_MARKER`, so a polling harness can deterministically know when to deliver a racing second terminal trigger. This iteration implements the seam at the `cleanup-start` window value and pins the SPEC §7.2 contract for the racing-SIGINT→SIGTERM case on the rule-3 and rule-5 cleanup-warning branches.

Implementation (`packages/loop-extender/src/tmpdir.ts`): the seam fires INSIDE `cleanupTmpdir` after the `state.attempted` idempotence check, so a second cleanup call on the same state is still a no-op (no second pause). Marker write: `openSync` / `writeSync({"window":"cleanup-start"})` / `fsyncSync` / `closeSync` BEFORE the bounded delay begins (per TEST-SPEC §1.4 ordering — marker visibility implies pause is about to start). Sync sleep: `Atomics.wait(view, 0, 0, 3000)` on a tiny SharedArrayBuffer — within the spec-required 2-10s range, no spawn dependency, no event-loop entanglement during the wait. Seam is gated on `NODE_ENV=test` AND the env-var equaling `cleanup-start`; all other values (or unset) are no-ops. Marker write is best-effort (if marker path is unwritable, the pause still happens).

SPEC §7.2 first-trigger-wins fix (`packages/loop-extender/src/bin.ts`): the previous CLI signal handler unconditionally executed `receivedSignal = sig; ac.abort(sig);`, which meant a SIGTERM observed during cleanup-of-prior-SIGINT would overwrite the first observation and the surfaced exit code would shift from 130 to 143. The fix: only set `receivedSignal` if currently `null`; the second `ac.abort()` still propagates (no-op since already aborted) but `receivedSignal` stays anchored at the first observation. This is a real implementation correctness fix for SPEC §7.2, not just a test-fixture concern — any production scenario with two close-together signals exercised the same overwrite bug.

Now-passing tests (this iteration):
- **tmpdir.test.ts: 503/503 PASS** — added 4 tests (2 IDs × 2 runtimes):
  - **T-TMP-38**: CLI cleanup idempotence under racing SIGINT→SIGTERM on the SPEC §7.4 rule-3 (regular-file replacement) cleanup-warning branch. Driven via `runCLIWithSignal`; the harness polls for the `LOOPX_TEST_TERMINAL_TRIGGER_PAUSE_MARKER` path written by the seam (existence implies cleanup paused at the `cleanup-start` window), then delivers the racing SIGTERM. Asserts: (a) exit code 130 (SIGINT survives the SIGTERM-during-pause race per SPEC §7.2 first-trigger-wins), (b) exactly one `LOOPX_TEST_CLEANUP_WARNING\t…` line on stderr (per-run cleanup-warning cardinality holds across racing triggers — `CleanupState.warned` deduplicates), (c) regular-file at the recorded tmpdir path with content `regular-file-replacement` survives (rule-3 leave-with-warning preserved). Carries `{ timeout: 60_000, retry: 2 }` per the racing-trigger flakiness convention.
  - **T-TMP-39**: same race configuration as T-TMP-38 but on the SPEC §7.4 rule-5 (mismatched-directory replacement via rename-aside pattern) cleanup-warning branch. Asserts: (a) exit code 130, (b) exactly one cleanup warning, (c) mismatched-directory replacement with `mismatched-marker` file inside survives, (d) renamed-aside copy at `<loopx-tmpdir-name>-aside` also survives.
- Adjacent suites: zero regressions across programmatic-api + env-vars + wfdir (494/494), signals (9/9), loop-state + execution + cli-basics (449/449), unit + harness (158/158).

### ADR-0004 §7.4 (cleanup-fault-warning-does-not-mask CLI signal terminal surface) — RESOLVED

SPEC §7.4 final paragraph: "warnings do not affect the CLI exit code, the generator outcome, or the promise rejection reason." The contract holds for both the cleanup-safety warning branch and the cleanup-failure warning branch. T-TMP-35f covers the cleanup-safety side of the signal terminal (rule 3 / rule 5 × SIGINT/SIGTERM × CLI). T-TMP-40 / T-TMP-41 / T-TMP-42 cover the cleanup-failure side on the success terminal across all three surfaces. T-TMP-42a covers cleanup-failure × script-error across all three surfaces. T-TMP-42b covers cleanup-failure × abort across the two programmatic surfaces. T-TMP-42c closes the remaining diagonal: the cleanup-failure warning branch × CLI signal terminal — the only diagonal not previously pinned in the cleanup-warning-does-not-affect-outcome matrix.

A buggy implementation that wired the signal-terminal `128 + signal-number` exit-code path correctly for rule-3 / rule-5 cleanup-safety warnings (passing T-TMP-35f) yet routed cleanup-failure warnings (lstat-fail / symlink-unlink-fail / recursive-remove-fail) through a separate stream that promoted the warning to a cleanup-failure-class exit code under signal — exit 1 or some implementation-specific cleanup-failure code instead of the signal code — would pass T-TMP-35f and T-TMP-40 / T-TMP-41 / T-TMP-42 / T-TMP-42a / T-TMP-42b yet fail this test.

Implementation in `runLoop` (`packages/loop-extender/src/loop.ts`) and the CLI signal forwarder (`packages/loop-extender/src/bin.ts`) already conformed: the iteration body wraps in `try/finally` so `cleanupTmpdir(...)` runs before any signal-driven abort error propagates out of the generator, and the CLI's signal handler observes the first signal as the surfaced terminal trigger. The cleanup-fault seam (`LOOPX_TEST_CLEANUP_FAULT={lstat-fail, symlink-unlink-fail, recursive-remove-fail}`) fires inside `cleanupTmpdir` and emits via `emitCleanupWarning` which writes to stderr but never rewrites the in-flight throw value or shifts the CLI exit code.

Now-passing tests (this iteration):
- **tmpdir.test.ts: 515/515 PASS** — added 12 tests (3 cleanup-fault seams × 2 signals × 2 runtimes):
  - **T-TMP-42c (lstat-fail × SIGINT, lstat-fail × SIGTERM, symlink-unlink-fail × SIGINT, symlink-unlink-fail × SIGTERM, recursive-remove-fail × SIGINT, recursive-remove-fail × SIGTERM)**: `runCLIWithSignal(['run', '-n', '1', 'ralph'])` with `LOOPX_TEST_CLEANUP_FAULT=<seam>` and `NODE_ENV=test`. Fixture observes LOOPX_TMPDIR into an external marker (path external to the tmpdir so it survives cleanup), performs the seam-specific path manipulation when needed (for `symlink-unlink-fail`: `rm -rf "$LOOPX_TMPDIR" && ln -s /tmp "$LOOPX_TMPDIR"` so cleanup dispatch reaches rule 2; for `recursive-remove-fail`: writes a few files inside the tmpdir so the dispatch reaches rule 4 on a non-empty identity-matched directory; for `lstat-fail`: no path manipulation needed, the seam fires on the top-level `lstat`), writes `"ready"` to stderr, then blocks indefinitely. Harness waits for `"ready"` then sends the variant-specific signal. Asserts: (a) loopx exits with `130` (SIGINT) or `143` (SIGTERM) — the cleanup-failure warning did not mask, replace, or override the signal exit code (load-bearing), (b) exactly one `LOOPX_TEST_CLEANUP_WARNING\t…` line on stderr (per-run cleanup-warning cardinality holds across the signal terminal), (c) path persistence per fault seam (lstat-fail: identity-matched directory remains; symlink-unlink-fail: symlink remains; recursive-remove-fail: directory remains).

### ADR-0004 §7.2 / §7.4 (T-TMP-38f cleanup idempotence under racing SIGTERM → SIGINT — inverted-order parity) — RESOLVED

SPEC §7.2's first-observed-trigger-wins rule and SPEC §7.4's at-most-one-cleanup-attempt / at-most-one-cleanup-warning rules apply symmetrically across SIGINT and SIGTERM — neither signal is privileged. T-TMP-38 covered the SIGINT-first × SIGTERM-second-during-cleanup race on the rule-3 regular-file warning branch; T-TMP-39 covered the same SIGINT-first race on the rule-5 mismatched-directory branch; T-TERM-03 (still pending) covers the same SIGINT-first race on the surfaced-exit-code axis. None of those exercises the inverted observation order. T-TMP-38f closes that gap: a buggy implementation that special-cased SIGINT-first cleanup-race handling (e.g., a SIGINT-handler path that correctly gated cleanup-idempotence and exit-code precedence, but a SIGTERM-handler path that re-entered cleanup or surfaced the second signal's exit code) would pass T-TMP-38 / T-TMP-39 / T-TERM-03 yet fail T-TMP-38f.

The implementation in `bin.ts` (`signalHandler` at lines 652-657) already conformed: `receivedSignal` is set only when currently `null`, so the first observed signal pins the surfaced exit code regardless of which signal arrives first. The `cleanup-start` seam in `tmpdir.ts` (`maybePauseAtCleanupStart` at lines 105-137) is signal-agnostic — it pauses on cleanup entry and writes the parent-observable marker without inspecting which signal initiated the cleanup. `CleanupState.attempted` deduplicates the cleanup attempt so the racing post-pause SIGINT does not re-enter `cleanupTmpdir`.

Now-passing tests (this iteration):
- **tmpdir.test.ts: 517/517 PASS** — added 2 tests (1 ID × 2 runtimes):
  - **T-TMP-38f**: Same fixture and seam configuration as T-TMP-38 (rule-3 regular-file replacement, `LOOPX_TEST_TERMINAL_TRIGGER_PAUSE=cleanup-start`). Driven via `runCLIWithSignal`; the harness waits for the script's `ready` marker on stderr, sends **SIGTERM** (the first-observed signal in the inverted order), polls for the `LOOPX_TEST_TERMINAL_TRIGGER_PAUSE_MARKER` path written by the seam (existence implies cleanup paused at the `cleanup-start` window), then delivers the racing **SIGINT** during the bounded pause. Asserts (a) exit code 143 (SIGTERM survives the SIGINT-during-cleanup race per SPEC §7.2 first-trigger-wins applied symmetrically across signals — load-bearing: a buggy SIGTERM-handler that re-pinned `receivedSignal` to the second SIGINT would shift the exit code to 130), (b) exactly one `LOOPX_TEST_CLEANUP_WARNING\t…` line on stderr (per-run cleanup-warning cardinality holds across racing triggers regardless of signal-order), (c) regular-file at the recorded tmpdir path with content `regular-file-replacement` survives (rule-3 leave-with-warning preserved). Carries `{ timeout: 60_000, retry: 2 }` per the racing-trigger flakiness convention.
- Adjacent suites: zero regressions across signals + programmatic-api + env-vars + wfdir.

### ADR-0004 §7.4 (cleanup-warning-does-not-mask signal/abort terminal surface-parity) — RESOLVED

SPEC §7.4: "cleanup warnings do not affect the CLI exit code, the generator outcome, or the promise rejection reason." T-TMP-35 / 35a / 35b (rule-3 success terminal) and T-TMP-36 / 36a / 36b (rule-5 success terminal) pinned the contract on `stop: true` script termination. T-TMP-35c / 35d / 35e extended the contract to the SCRIPT-ERROR terminal × both warning-emitting cleanup-safety branches (rule 3 regular-file replacement, rule 5 mismatched-directory replacement). T-TMP-35f / 35g / 35h close the matrix on the remaining terminals: SIGNAL (CLI SIGINT/SIGTERM) and ABORT (programmatic API), again × both warning-emitting cleanup-safety branches × all three execution surfaces.

The implementation in `runLoop` (`packages/loop-extender/src/loop.ts:120-217`) already conformed: the iteration body wraps in `try/finally` so `cleanupTmpdir(tmpdirResource, cleanupState)` (line 216) runs before any abort error propagates out of the generator. The user signal → internal AbortController propagation (`packages/loop-extender/src/run.ts:279-303` per SPEC §9.5) wires the abort terminal correctly so a CLI SIGINT/SIGTERM or programmatic abort reaches the in-flight iteration. The active child process group is terminated per SPEC §9.1; T-TMP-35g and T-TMP-35h verify this explicitly via pid-marker probing (assert the script's pid is no longer alive after the rejection / throw is observed).

Fixture: a shared `buildSignalAbortCleanupFixture` helper in tmpdir.test.ts. The fixture tampers with `$LOOPX_TMPDIR` per cleanup-safety branch (rule 3: `rm -rf "$LOOPX_TMPDIR"` followed by writing a regular file at the path; rule 5: `mv "$LOOPX_TMPDIR" "$LOOPX_TMPDIR-original-aside" && mkdir "$LOOPX_TMPDIR" && touch "$LOOPX_TMPDIR/mismatched-marker"`), writes the original tmpdir path to a `tmpdirObservation` marker file AFTER tampering completes (existence-of-marker implies tampering complete — important for API drivers that poll for the marker before triggering abort), writes the script's pid to a `pidMarker` for child-termination probing, prints `ready` to stderr (consumed by CLI signal coordinator via `runCLIWithSignal`'s `waitForStderr`), then blocks forever (so the run cannot terminate by any means other than the signal/abort under test).
