### ADR-0004 §7.4 (cleanup-warning-does-not-mask script-error terminal surface-parity) — RESOLVED

SPEC §7.4: "cleanup warnings do not affect the CLI exit code, the generator outcome, or the promise rejection reason." T-TMP-35 / 35a / 35b (rule-3 success terminal) and T-TMP-36 / 36a / 36b (rule-5 success terminal) pin this against `stop: true` script termination. T-TMP-35c / 35d / 35e pin the contract on the script-error terminal — when a script triggers a cleanup-safety rule (rule 3 regular-file replacement or rule 5 mismatched-directory replacement) AND exits non-zero, the surfaced terminal must remain the SCRIPT failure (CLI exit 1 with the script's stderr passed through; runPromise rejects with the script-failure error; run() throws the script-failure error), not a cleanup-failure-class outcome. The implementation in `runLoop` (`packages/loop-extender/src/loop.ts:120-217`) already conformed: the iteration body wraps in `try/finally` so `cleanupTmpdir(tmpdirResource, cleanupState)` (line 216) runs before the script-failure `throw new Error('Script <wf>:<scr> exited with code <n>')` (line 133-135) propagates out of the generator. Cleanup `emitCleanupWarning` writes to stderr but never rewrites the in-flight throw value.

The CLI test (T-TMP-35c) carries an observably-disjoint-lines assertion: a distinctive `SCRIPT-FAILURE-MARKER-T-TMP-35C` line printed to stderr by the script before its tampering must reach the user's stderr on a separate line from the `LOOPX_TEST_CLEANUP_WARNING\t…` marker. Since both the script-failure path and a hypothetical cleanup-promoted-to-failure path produce CLI exit 1, exit-code alone cannot distinguish — the disjoint-lines assertion is what catches a buggy implementation that wrapped or replaced the script's stderr with a cleanup-classifier wrapper.

The API tests (T-TMP-35d / 35e) carry an error-message-shape probe: the rejection reason (runPromise) / throw value (run) must match the loop.ts contract `Script '<wf>:<scr>' exited with code <n>` (regex `/exited with code/`) and must NOT contain "cleanup" anywhere in the message. A buggy implementation that wrapped the script-failure error in a cleanup-failure error would fail this assertion.

- **tmpdir.test.ts: 465/465 PASS** — added 12 tests (3 IDs × 2 cleanup-safety variants × 2 runtimes):
  - **T-TMP-35c (regular-file-replacement, mismatched-directory-replacement) [CLI]**: `runCLI(['run', '-n', '1', 'ralph'])`. Asserts: (a) exit 1 (from script), (b) exactly one `SCRIPT-FAILURE-MARKER-T-TMP-35C` line on stderr, (c) exactly one `LOOPX_TEST_CLEANUP_WARNING\t…` line, (d) marker line and warning line are disjoint, (e) path persistence per cleanup-safety branch (rule 3: regular file with content `regular-file-replacement` survives; rule 5: directory with `mismatched-marker` and the renamed-aside copy survive).
  - **T-TMP-35d (regular-file-replacement, mismatched-directory-replacement) [runPromise]**: driver code awaits `runPromise("ralph", { maxIterations: 1 })`, captures rejection state, error message, and post-run path observations. Asserts: (a) promise rejected, (b) errMsg matches `/exited with code/` (script-failure shape) and does NOT contain "cleanup", (c) exactly one cleanup warning, (d) path persistence per branch.
  - **T-TMP-35e (regular-file-replacement, mismatched-directory-replacement) [run]**: driver code drives `run("ralph", { maxIterations: 1 })` via `for await`, captures throw state and error message. Asserts: (a) generator threw, (b) errMsg matches `/exited with code/` and does NOT contain "cleanup", (c) exactly one cleanup warning, (d) path persistence per branch.
- Adjacent suites: zero regressions across programmatic-api (370), env-vars (96), wfdir (28) → 494/494. Full tmpdir.test.ts run: 465/465 in ~70s.

### ADR-0004 §7.2 / §7.4 (T-TMP-38a — first-observed-wins for racing abort → .return() during cleanup-start, run() surface) — RESOLVED

The SPEC §7.2 contract: "the first terminal trigger observed by loopx determines the surfaced outcome among genuinely racing triggers" applies symmetrically across all terminal-trigger pairs. T-TMP-38 / T-TMP-38f / T-TMP-39 pinned the rule for signal-vs-signal races on the CLI surface. T-TMP-38a closes one of the diagonals on the run() programmatic surface: abort observed first, .return() racing during the cleanup-start pause.

Implementation gaps that this iteration closed:
- **Async seam pause (`packages/loop-extender/src/tmpdir.ts`):** the `cleanup-start` seam previously used `Atomics.wait` on a SharedArrayBuffer (sync sleep blocking the JS thread for 3 sec). For CLI tests, sync vs async pause was indistinguishable — the test process and loopx CLI subprocess are separate processes. For a same-process driver (programmatic API tests), the sync sleep blocked the driver's event loop, preventing it from polling for the parent-observable cleanup-start marker and calling `gen.return()` / `ac.abort()` mid-pause. Replaced `syncSleep` with `asyncSleep` (`setTimeout`-based Promise). Made `maybePauseAtCleanupStart` async, `cleanupTmpdir` async, and `createTmpdir` async (since its error path may invoke `cleanupTmpdir`). `runLoop`'s finally now `await`s `cleanupTmpdir(...)`. T-TMP-38 / T-TMP-39 / T-TMP-38f all still pass with the async pause (signal handler runs during the async wait instead of after the sync wait — observably equivalent for cross-process coordination).
- **Wrapper first-observed-wins (`packages/loop-extender/src/run.ts`):** the wrapper's `.return()` / `.throw()` / `[Symbol.asyncDispose]` previously pinned `returnCalled = true` unconditionally. The wrapper's `.next()` catch then silenced the abort error from a pending in-flight iteration when `returnCalled` was true (the SPEC §9.1 silent-clean-completion contract). For an abort-first-then-.return() race, this incorrectly inverted the surfaced outcome — silent completion instead of abort error. Fixed: each consumer-cancellation method now reads `internalAc.signal.aborted` at entry; only pins `returnCalled` if abort was NOT first-observed. The inner generator's `.return()` is still driven so the runLoop `finally` (`cleanupTmpdir`) runs and the inner gen settles. SPEC §9.3 post-final-yield-abort carve-out preserved (existing path unchanged for that case).

Now-passing tests (this iteration):
- **tmpdir.test.ts: 519/519 PASS** — added 2 tests (1 ID × 2 runtimes):
  - **T-TMP-38a**: bash fixture observes nothing (rule-3 replacement is sufficient — fixture `rm -rf "$LOOPX_TMPDIR" && printf '%s' "regular-file-replacement" > "$LOOPX_TMPDIR" && touch "$FIXTURE_READY_PATH" && while true; do sleep 1; done`). Driver code (run via `runAPIDriver`) creates an `AbortController`, kicks off `for await (const _ of run("ralph", { signal: ac.signal }))` in an async IIFE that captures any thrown error into `errName` / `errMessage`, polls for the fixture-ready file, calls `ac.abort()`, polls for the parent-observable cleanup-start marker (existence implies cleanup paused at the seam), then calls `await gen.return()` (during the seam pause), then awaits the IIFE. Writes a JSON envelope `{ errName, errMessage }` to stdout. Asserts: (a) `envelope.errName === "AbortError"` (load-bearing — a buggy wrapper that pinned `returnCalled` unconditionally would silence the abort error and produce `errName === ""`), (b) exactly one `LOOPX_TEST_CLEANUP_WARNING\t…` line on stderr, (c) regular-file at the recorded tmpdir path with content `regular-file-replacement` survives.
- Adjacent suites: zero regressions across programmatic-api (370), signals (9), env-vars (96), wfdir (28), loop-state (96), execution (45), unit (143), harness (15).

### ADR-0004 §7.2 / §7.4 (T-TMP-38b / T-TMP-38b-run — first-observed-wins for racing non-zero-script-exit → abort during cleanup-start, runPromise() and run() surfaces) — RESOLVED

The SPEC §7.2 contract: "the first terminal trigger observed by loopx determines the surfaced outcome among genuinely racing triggers" applies symmetrically across all terminal-trigger pairs. T-TMP-38a / T-TMP-38a2 covered the abort-vs-consumer-cancellation diagonal on the run() surface. T-TMP-38b / T-TMP-38b-run cover the non-zero-script-exit-vs-abort diagonal on the runPromise() and run() surfaces. Together the family pins SPEC §7.2 first-observed-wins symmetrically across multiple trigger pairs at the cleanup-start window.

The implementation in `runLoop` (`packages/loop-extender/src/loop.ts`) and the `run.ts` wrapper ALREADY conformed: when the script exits non-zero, runLoop throws `Error('Script <wf>:<scr> exited with code <n>')` from the iteration body. The throw enters the try/finally which awaits `cleanupTmpdir`. cleanupTmpdir pauses at the `cleanup-start` seam (`maybePauseAtCleanupStart` in tmpdir.ts) for ~3s after writing the parent-observable marker. During the pause, the driver code (running in parallel via the iterPromise IIFE for run(), or directly under runPromise's for-await loop) calls `ac.abort()`. This sets `internalAc.signal.aborted = true` but the in-flight throw is unaffected. cleanup completes (rule-3 emits exactly one warning), the throw propagates out, and wrapper.next() catches with `returnCalled === false` → throws err. The script-failure error reaches the consumer (runPromise rejects; for-await re-throws to the iterPromise's catch).

Now-passing tests (this iteration):
- **tmpdir.test.ts: 525/525 PASS** — added 4 tests (2 IDs × 2 runtimes):
  - **T-TMP-38b**: bash fixture (rule-3 regular-file replacement, identical structure to T-TMP-38a's fixture but exits 1 instead of blocking — `rm -rf "$LOOPX_TMPDIR" && printf '%s' "regular-file-replacement" > "$LOOPX_TMPDIR" && touch "$FIXTURE_READY_PATH" && exit 1`). Driver code (run via `runAPIDriver`) creates an `AbortController`, kicks off `runPromise("ralph", { signal: ac.signal, maxIterations: 1 })`, polls for the fixture-ready file, polls for the parent-observable cleanup-start marker (existence implies cleanup paused at the seam), then calls `ac.abort()` during the bounded pause. Awaits the promise inside try/catch capturing `errName` / `errMessage`. Writes a JSON envelope `{ errName, errMessage }` to stdout. Asserts: (a) `envelope.errMessage` matches `/exited with code/` AND `envelope.errName !== "AbortError"` AND `envelope.errMessage` does NOT match `/abort/i` (script-failure preserved — first-observed-wins; load-bearing — a buggy implementation that wrapped the script-failure error in an abort-class wrapper would fail), (b) exactly one `LOOPX_TEST_CLEANUP_WARNING\t…` line on stderr (no second cleanup attempt), (c) regular-file at the recorded tmpdir path with content `regular-file-replacement` survives.
  - **T-TMP-38b-run**: bash fixture (same as T-TMP-38b). Driver code creates an `AbortController`, drives `for await (const _ of run("ralph", { signal: ac.signal, maxIterations: 1 }))` in an async IIFE that captures any thrown error into `errName` / `errMessage`, polls for fixture-ready, polls for cleanup-start marker, calls `ac.abort()` during the pause, then awaits the IIFE. Writes the same JSON envelope. Asserts: same shape as T-TMP-38b — verifies that a buggy implementation that wired idempotence correctly on `runPromise` rejection but routed `run()` settlement through a different cleanup-dispatcher would fail this counterpart.
- Adjacent suites: zero regressions across programmatic-api + env-vars + wfdir + loop-state (590), signals (9). Full tmpdir.test.ts run: 525/525 in ~118s.

### ADR-0004 §7.2 / §7.4 (T-TMP-38a2 — first-observed-wins for racing .return() → abort during cleanup-start, run() surface, inverted-order parity) — RESOLVED

Inverted-order parity counterpart to T-TMP-38a: where T-TMP-38a covered abort-first × .return()-second on the run() programmatic surface, T-TMP-38a2 covers .return()-first × abort-second on the same run() surface. Together the pair pins SPEC §7.2 first-observed-wins symmetrically across the consumer-cancellation-vs-abort diagonal at the cleanup-start window.

The implementation in `packages/loop-extender/src/run.ts` ALREADY conformed: when `.return()` is the first observed terminal trigger (`internalAc.signal.aborted === false` at .return() entry), the wrapper sets `returnCalled = true`. The post-pause abort (during the cleanup-start seam) then propagates through the runLoop body, but the wrapper.next() catch silences the abort error per the consumer-cancellation contract. CleanupState.attempted gates the single cleanup attempt across both observation orders. No implementation change was required this iteration — only the test was authored.

Now-passing tests (this iteration):
- **tmpdir.test.ts: 521/521 PASS** — added 2 tests (1 ID × 2 runtimes):
  - **T-TMP-38a2**: bash fixture (rule-3 regular-file replacement, identical to T-TMP-38a's fixture). Driver code (run via `runAPIDriver`) creates an `AbortController`, drives `for await (const _ of run("ralph", { signal: ac.signal }))` in an async IIFE that captures any thrown error into `errName` / `errMessage`, polls for the fixture-ready file, calls `gen.return(undefined)` first (first observed terminal trigger), polls for the parent-observable cleanup-start marker (existence implies cleanup paused at the seam), then calls `ac.abort()` during the bounded pause, then awaits the `returnPromise` and the `iterPromise` (IIFE). Writes a JSON envelope `{ returnDone, returnValue, errName, errMessage }` to stdout. Asserts: (a) `envelope.returnDone === true` AND `envelope.returnValue === null` AND `envelope.errName === ""` (clean settlement, no abort surfaced — first-observed-wins applied symmetrically: .return() was first, so the abort error is silenced by the consumer-cancellation contract), (b) exactly one `LOOPX_TEST_CLEANUP_WARNING\t…` line on stderr (no second cleanup attempt), (c) regular-file at the recorded tmpdir path with content `regular-file-replacement` survives.
- Adjacent suites: zero regressions across programmatic-api (370), env-vars (96), wfdir (28) → 494/494. signals (9). loop-state (96), execution (45). tmpdir.test.ts: 521/521 (was 519, +2).

### ADR-0004 §7.2 / §7.4 (T-TMP-38c — first-observed-wins for racing abort → .throw() during cleanup-start, run() surface) — RESOLVED

The .throw()-axis companion to T-TMP-38a (which covered the .return() axis on the same surface, same observation order). Together with T-TMP-38a/T-TMP-38a2 (.return() axis, both observation orders) and T-TMP-38b/T-TMP-38b-run (non-zero-exit axis, both surfaces), this closes SPEC §7.2's "abort concurrent with consumer .return() / .throw()" enumeration on the cleanup-idempotence axis at the cleanup-start window for the abort-first half of the matrix on the run() programmatic surface. The .throw()-first × abort-second inverted-order counterpart is T-TMP-38c2 (now also RESOLVED — see next subsection).

The implementation in `packages/loop-extender/src/run.ts` (`wrapper.throw` lines 419-449) ALREADY conformed: the wrapper.throw() body is symmetric to wrapper.return() — it reads `internalAc.signal.aborted` at entry, only pins `returnCalled` when abort was NOT first-observed, then drives `gen.return(undefined)` so the inner runLoop's try/finally executes cleanupTmpdir. When abort was first-observed, returnCalled stays false, leaving the in-flight wrapper.next() (queued behind the inner gen's finally) free to surface the abort error to the for-await consumer once cleanup completes. CleanupState.attempted gates the single cleanup attempt; the queued gen.return() from the racing .throw() resolves on the now-completed gen with done:true. No implementation change required this iteration — only the test was authored.

Now-passing tests (this iteration):
- **tmpdir.test.ts: 527/527 PASS** — added 2 tests (1 ID × 2 runtimes):
  - **T-TMP-38c**: bash fixture (rule-3 regular-file replacement, identical to T-TMP-38a's fixture). Driver code (run via `runAPIDriver`) creates an `AbortController`, drives `for await (const _ of run("ralph", { signal: ac.signal }))` in an async IIFE that captures any thrown error into `errName` / `errMessage`, polls for the fixture-ready file, calls `ac.abort()` (first observed terminal trigger), polls for the parent-observable cleanup-start marker (existence implies cleanup paused at the seam), then calls `await gen.throw(new Error("test-throw"))` during the bounded pause, then awaits the `iterPromise`. Writes a JSON envelope `{ errName, errMessage }` to stdout. Asserts: (a) `envelope.errName === "AbortError"` AND `envelope.errMessage` does NOT match `/test-throw/` (first-observed abort wins; consumer error silently absorbed per SPEC §9.1 silent-clean-completion contract — load-bearing: a buggy wrapper that surfaced the consumer-thrown error or wrapped it around the abort would shift errName), (b) exactly one `LOOPX_TEST_CLEANUP_WARNING\t…` line on stderr (no second cleanup attempt — load-bearing: a buggy wrapper that re-entered cleanup on the racing .throw() would emit a second warning), (c) regular-file at the recorded tmpdir path with content `regular-file-replacement` survives.
- Adjacent suites: zero regressions across programmatic-api + env-vars + wfdir + loop-state (590), signals (9). tmpdir.test.ts: 527/527 (was 525, +2).

### ADR-0004 §7.2 / §7.4 / §9.1 / §9.3 (T-TMP-38d3 — first-observed-wins for racing post-final-yield .return() → abort during consumer-return-observed, run() surface) — RESOLVED

`.return()`-axis post-final-yield counterpart on the run() programmatic surface — `.return()` observed FIRST after final yield (post first-`next()`); loopx records the .return() as the first-observed terminal trigger and pauses at the new TEST-SPEC §1.4 `consumer-return-observed` window seam BEFORE dispatching settlement; harness polls the parent-observable pause marker, then calls `ac.abort()` during the bounded pause. Per SPEC §9.3 second paragraph + §9.1 silent-clean-completion-when-no-child rule, the .return() observed earlier wins as the surfaced outcome — clean `{ done: true, value: undefined }` settlement; the racing post-pause abort does NOT displace it. Per SPEC §7.4 idempotence + at-most-one-warning, the racing abort must NOT initiate a second cleanup attempt. Symmetric counterpart to T-TMP-38d2 (the `.throw()`-axis variant on the same observation order, still pending). Together with T-TMP-38d (abort-first × `.throw()`-second post-final-yield) and T-TMP-38d4 (abort-first × `.return()`-second post-final-yield, still pending), this closes one quadrant of the post-final-yield consumer-cancellation × abort matrix on the warning-cardinality axis.

Implementation changes (this iteration introduced new SPEC infrastructure on top of the test):

1. **`packages/loop-extender/src/run.ts` (wrapper.return)** — adds `await maybePauseAtTerminalTriggerWindow("consumer-return-observed")` AFTER the `returnCalled = true` pin (preserving first-observed status recording per the seam's spec'd ordering) and BEFORE `internalAc.abort() / gen.return()` dispatch. The seam call is gated INSIDE the `if (!abortObservedFirst)` branch, so it only fires when .return() is the first-observed terminal trigger — preserves T-TMP-38a's abort-first × .return()-second contract by skipping the seam entirely when abort was observed first (the `surfacePostFinalYieldAbort` branch above also bypasses the seam for the abort-first × post-final-yield case). The seam fires uniformly on any post-first-`next()` `.return()` — both mid-loop and post-final-yield — so the same wiring covers both contexts described by the §1.4 `consumer-return-observed` contract.

Now-passing tests (this iteration):
- **tmpdir.test.ts: 533/533 PASS** — added 4 tests (1 ID × 2 variants × 2 runtimes):
  - **T-TMP-38d3 (stop)**: bash fixture (rule-3 regular-file replacement; `printf '%s' '{"stop":true}'`) with `maxIterations: 5`. Driver code (run via `runAPIDriver`) creates an `AbortController`, calls `await gen.next()` to receive the final yield (verifies `first.value.stop === true`), then calls `gen.return(undefined)` (captures the returned promise into `returnPromise`), polls for the parent-observable consumer-return-observed marker (existence implies wrapper.return paused at the seam), then calls `ac.abort()` during the bounded pause, awaits `returnPromise` (capturing `settled.done` and `settled.value`). Writes JSON envelope `{ errName, errMessage, returnDone, returnValue, firstStop, firstDone }`.
  - **T-TMP-38d3 (maxIterations)**: same fixture structure but `printf '%s' '{}'` (raw fallback `{ result: "{}" }`) with `maxIterations: 1` (loopx-driven iteration-count-limit final yield). Verifies `first.done === false` to confirm the harness entered the post-final-yield window.
  - Asserts (both variants): (a) `envelope.returnDone === true` AND `envelope.returnValue === null` AND `envelope.errName === ""` AND `errMessage` does NOT match `/abort/i` (clean settlement, no abort surfaced — first-observed .return() silently absorbs the racing abort per SPEC §9.1 consumer-cancellation contract; load-bearing: a buggy wrapper that surfaced the abort error would shift returnDone / errName), (b) exactly one `LOOPX_TEST_CLEANUP_WARNING\t…` line on stderr (per-run cardinality holds across racing triggers — `CleanupState.attempted` deduplicates; load-bearing: a buggy implementation that started a second cleanup attempt on the racing abort would emit a second warning), (c) rule-3 regular-file replacement at the recorded path survives (cleanup completed once and left the file in place per SPEC 7.4 rule-3; load-bearing: a buggy implementation that re-touched the rule-3 entry on the second attempt would corrupt or remove the file).
- Adjacent suites: zero regressions across programmatic-api + signals + loop-state + execution (544/544), unit + harness (158/158).

### ADR-0004 §7.2 / §7.4 (T-TMP-38c2 — first-observed-wins for racing .throw() → abort during consumer-throw-observed, run() surface, inverted-order parity) — RESOLVED

Inverted-order parity counterpart to T-TMP-38c on the run() programmatic surface — .throw() observed FIRST mid-loop (post first-next()); loopx records the .throw() as the first-observed terminal trigger and pauses at the new TEST-SPEC §1.4 `consumer-throw-observed` window seam BEFORE dispatching the resulting silent settlement; harness polls the parent-observable pause marker, then calls `ac.abort()` during the bounded pause. Per SPEC §7.2 first-observed-wins, the .throw() observed earlier wins as the surfaced outcome — the racing abort must NOT displace the silent-clean-completion settlement (SPEC §9.1) and must NOT initiate a second cleanup attempt (SPEC §7.4 idempotence + at-most-one-warning).

Implementation changes (this iteration introduced new SPEC infrastructure — not just test authoring):

1. **`packages/loop-extender/src/test-seams.ts` (new)** — extracts the marker-write + bounded-sleep mechanic into a shared `maybePauseAtTerminalTriggerWindow(expectedWindow: string)` helper. When `NODE_ENV=test` and `LOOPX_TEST_TERMINAL_TRIGGER_PAUSE` equals `expectedWindow`, writes a UTF-8 JSON marker file (when `LOOPX_TEST_TERMINAL_TRIGGER_PAUSE_MARKER` is set) using `openSync` / `writeSync` / `fsyncSync` / `closeSync` BEFORE the bounded delay begins (per TEST-SPEC §1.4 ordering — marker visibility implies pause is about to start). Bounded delay: 3 seconds (within the spec-required [2s, 10s] range). All other `LOOPX_TEST_TERMINAL_TRIGGER_PAUSE` window values not yet wired in implementation are no-ops at non-matching callsites (e.g., setting it to `abort-listener` will still be a no-op since the abort-listener callsite doesn't yet invoke this helper).
2. **`packages/loop-extender/src/tmpdir.ts` (refactored)** — removed local `maybePauseAtCleanupStart` and `asyncSleep`; `cleanupTmpdir` now invokes `await maybePauseAtTerminalTriggerWindow("cleanup-start")` from the shared helper. Same delay, same marker contract, same NODE_ENV gating — pure refactor with no behavior change. Verified: full tmpdir.test.ts 529/529 pass (existing T-TMP-38/38a/38a2/38b/38b-run/38c/38f/39 cleanup-start window tests all still pass — proves the refactor is behavior-preserving).
3. **`packages/loop-extender/src/run.ts` (wrapper.throw)** — adds `await maybePauseAtTerminalTriggerWindow("consumer-throw-observed")` AFTER the `returnCalled = true` pin (preserving first-observed status recording per the seam's spec'd ordering) and BEFORE `internalAc.abort() / gen.return()` dispatch. The seam call is gated INSIDE the `if (!abortObservedFirst)` branch, so it only fires when .throw() is the first-observed terminal trigger. This preserves T-TMP-38c's abort-first × .throw()-second contract: when abort was observed first, the `!abortObservedFirst` branch is skipped entirely (returnCalled stays false, no pause, dispatch proceeds immediately) — the existing wrapper.throw flow is unchanged for the abort-first half of the matrix.

### ADR-0004 §7.2 / §7.4 / §9.1 / §9.3 (T-TMP-38d2 — first-observed-wins for racing post-final-yield .throw() → abort during consumer-throw-observed, run() surface) — RESOLVED

`.throw()`-axis post-final-yield counterpart on the run() programmatic surface — `.throw()` observed FIRST after final yield (post first-`next()`); loopx records the .throw() as the first-observed terminal trigger and pauses at the TEST-SPEC §1.4 `consumer-throw-observed` window seam BEFORE dispatching settlement; harness polls the parent-observable pause marker, then calls `ac.abort()` during the bounded pause. Per SPEC §9.3 second paragraph + §9.1 silent-clean-completion-when-no-child rule, the .throw() observed earlier wins as the surfaced outcome — clean `{ done: true, value: undefined }` settlement; the consumer-supplied error is silently absorbed AND the racing post-pause abort does NOT displace the settlement. Per SPEC §7.4 idempotence + at-most-one-warning, the racing abort must NOT initiate a second cleanup attempt. Symmetric counterpart to T-TMP-38d3 (the `.return()`-axis variant on the same observation order). Together with T-TMP-38d (abort-first × `.throw()`-second post-final-yield, still pending) and T-TMP-38d4 (abort-first × `.return()`-second post-final-yield, still pending), this closes one quadrant of the post-final-yield consumer-cancellation × abort matrix on the warning-cardinality axis.

Implementation status: NO implementation changes required this iteration — only the test was authored. The wrapper.throw seam wiring landed in the T-TMP-38c2 iteration: at `packages/loop-extender/src/run.ts` line 461, `await maybePauseAtTerminalTriggerWindow("consumer-throw-observed")` is called inside the `if (!abortObservedFirst)` branch AFTER pinning `returnCalled = true`. Critically, the seam call is positioned to fire on **any** post-first-`next()` `.throw()` — both mid-loop AND post-final-yield — uniformly: when post-final-yield is true and abort is NOT yet observed, the wrapper.throw flow goes:
1. `if (settled)` → false (settled=false)
2. `if (postFinalYield && internalAc.signal.aborted && !returnCalled)` → false (abort not observed) → skip surfacePostFinalYieldAbort branch
3. `abortObservedFirst = false`; `if (!abortObservedFirst)` → true → returnCalled=true; seam fires
4. During seam pause: `ac.abort()` arrives → user signal listener fires `internalAc.abort()` (just sets the flag)
5. Seam ends (3s)
6. `internalAc.abort()` (no-op, already aborted); `gen.return(undefined)` drives inner gen settlement
7. Inner gen's try/finally runs cleanupTmpdir ONCE (CleanupState.attempted gates idempotence)
8. wrapper.throw returns `{ done: true, value: undefined }` — clean silent settlement
9. The consumer-supplied "test-throw" error is absorbed (per SPEC §9.1 consumer-cancellation contract); the racing abort error is also absorbed (per SPEC §9.3 second paragraph + §7.2 first-observed-wins residual rule)

So the existing seam wiring naturally satisfies T-TMP-38d2 — fix_plan.md's earlier note "the wrapper.throw post-final-yield path goes through surfacePostFinalYieldAbort, not the abort-observation pinning logic" was outdated (it predated the post-final-yield × abort-NOT-observed branch's natural fall-through to the seam).

Now-passing tests (this iteration):
- **tmpdir.test.ts: 537/537 PASS** — added 4 tests (1 ID × 2 variants × 2 runtimes):
  - **T-TMP-38d2 (stop)**: bash fixture (rule-3 regular-file replacement; `printf '%s' '{"stop":true}'`) with `maxIterations: 5`. Driver code (run via `runAPIDriver`) creates an `AbortController`, calls `await gen.next()` to receive the final yield (verifies `first.value.stop === true`), then calls `gen.throw(new Error("test-throw"))` (captures the returned promise into `throwPromise`), polls for the parent-observable consumer-throw-observed marker (existence implies wrapper.throw paused at the seam), then calls `ac.abort()` during the bounded pause, awaits `throwPromise` (capturing `settled.done` and `settled.value`). Writes JSON envelope `{ errName, errMessage, throwDone, throwValue, firstStop, firstDone }`.
  - **T-TMP-38d2 (maxIterations)**: same fixture structure but `printf '%s' '{}'` (raw fallback `{ result: "{}" }`) with `maxIterations: 1` (loopx-driven iteration-count-limit final yield). Verifies `first.done === false` to confirm the harness entered the post-final-yield window.
  - Asserts (both variants): (a) `envelope.throwDone === true` AND `envelope.throwValue === null` AND `envelope.errName === ""` AND `errMessage` does NOT match `/abort/i` AND `errMessage` does NOT match `/test-throw/` (clean settlement, no abort or consumer-thrown error surfaced — first-observed .throw() silently absorbs both itself and the racing abort per SPEC §9.1 consumer-cancellation contract; load-bearing: a buggy wrapper that surfaced either error would shift these), (b) exactly one `LOOPX_TEST_CLEANUP_WARNING\t…` line on stderr (per-run cardinality holds across racing triggers — `CleanupState.attempted` deduplicates; load-bearing: a buggy implementation that started a second cleanup attempt on the racing abort would emit a second warning), (c) rule-3 regular-file replacement at the recorded path survives (cleanup completed once and left the file in place per SPEC 7.4 rule-3; load-bearing: a buggy implementation that re-touched the rule-3 entry on the second attempt would corrupt or remove the file).

### ADR-0004 §7.2 / §7.4 (T-TMP-38b2 / T-TMP-38b2-run — abort-listener seam wiring + first-observed-wins under racing abort → non-zero-exit during abort-listener) — RESOLVED

Inverted-order parity counterpart to T-TMP-38b / T-TMP-38b-run on the runPromise() and run() programmatic surfaces. Where T-TMP-38b/-run covered iteration-error first × abort second (`cleanup-start` window), T-TMP-38b2/-run cover the abort first × non-zero-script-exit second race at the new TEST-SPEC §1.4 `abort-listener` window. The seam fires AFTER abort is recorded as first-observed (the user-signal listener's flag pin) but BEFORE loopx dispatches the abort outcome (i.e., before kicking off child termination, abortPromise rejection, or abort-error surfacing). This keeps the active child alive during the bounded ~3s pause (TEST-SPEC §1.4 form (a)), so the harness can race a child-driven non-zero exit (SIGUSR1 → bash trap → `exit 1`) against the still-paused abort dispatch on the still-alive process group.

This iteration introduces fundamentally new SPEC §7.2 infrastructure that decouples first-observed-trigger determination from `internalAc.signal.aborted` (which the new seam delays). Without this decoupling, the wrapper's first-observed checks would see `internalAc.signal.aborted === false` during the seam-paused dispatch and incorrectly classify the racing trigger as first-observed. The implementation:

1. **`packages/loop-extender/src/loop.ts`** — added `FirstObservedTrigger` type alias (`"abort" | "iteration" | "consumer" | null`) and `FirstObservedRef` interface holding a single `trigger` slot, both exported. Added `firstObservedRef?: FirstObservedRef` to `LoopOptions`. Added a `pinIterationFirstObserved()` helper that conditionally sets `firstObservedRef.trigger = "iteration"` (only if currently null). Each iteration-level throw now calls the helper before throwing: the script-failure branch (`if (result.exitCode !== 0)`), the parse-goto branch (`if (!goto.ok)`), the bare-goto unknown-script branch, the workflow-qualified-goto unknown-workflow branch, and the workflow-qualified-goto unknown-script branch.

2. **`packages/loop-extender/src/run.ts`** — added a `firstObservedRef = { trigger: null }` slot per run() call, threaded through to `runInternal` → `runLoop` via the new field. The user-signal listener (`onUserSignalAbort`) now: (a) pins `firstObservedRef.trigger = "abort"` if currently null AT ENTRY (before any pause); (b) dispatches `internalAc.abort()` synchronously when not in test mode OR when `LOOPX_TEST_TERMINAL_TRIGGER_PAUSE !== "abort-listener"`; (c) when the abort-listener seam is active, schedules an async IIFE that awaits `maybePauseAtTerminalTriggerWindow("abort-listener")` and only THEN calls `internalAc.abort()`. The eager-aborted-at-call-time branch (`if (snap.signal.aborted)` at the top of run()'s signal wiring) ALSO pins `firstObservedRef.trigger = "abort"` since the listener never fires there.

3. **`packages/loop-extender/src/run.ts` (wrapper)** — every previous `internalAc.signal.aborted` first-observed check now consults `firstObservedRef.trigger === "abort"` instead. Touched callsites: `wrapper.next()` post-final-yield abort branch (line ~398), `wrapper.return()` post-final-yield abort branch and mid-loop `abortObservedFirst` check (lines ~451/466), `wrapper.throw()` mirror branches (lines ~519/534), and `[Symbol.asyncDispose]` (line ~573). When consumer cancellation acts as first-observed (the `!abortObservedFirst` branch in .return() / .throw() / asyncDispose), the wrapper now ALSO pins `firstObservedRef.trigger = "consumer"` if currently null, so a subsequent abort-listener firing sees the slot occupied and does not displace the consumer-cancellation outcome.

4. **`packages/loop-extender/src/run.ts` (wrapper.next() catch)** — added a NEW first-observed-wins gate AFTER the existing `if (returnCalled) return done:true` clause: when an iteration-level error reaches the wrapper.next() catch BUT abort had already been pinned as first-observed by the listener, the wrapper now throws `makeAbortError(snap.signal ?? internalAc.signal)` instead of the iteration error. This is the load-bearing change that produces the abort-error surfacing under T-TMP-38b2 / T-TMP-38b2-run when the SIGUSR1-driven script-failure reached runLoop first. The pre-existing path (no abort first-observed) still surfaces the original `err` unchanged, preserving T-TMP-38b / T-TMP-38b-run semantics (where iteration-error was actually observed first via runLoop's `pinIterationFirstObserved` call BEFORE the racing abort-during-cleanup-start).

Now-passing tests (this iteration):
- **tmpdir.test.ts: 541/541 PASS** — added 4 tests (1 ID × 2 surfaces × 2 runtimes):
  - **T-TMP-38b2** (runPromise surface): bash fixture installs `trap 'exit 1' USR1`, writes its own PID via `printf '%s' "$$" > "$PID_MARKER_PATH"`, replaces the tmpdir with the rule-3 regular-file replacement, then `sleep 30 & wait`s. Driver code (run via `runAPIDriver`) creates an `AbortController`, kicks off `runPromise("ralph", { signal: ac.signal, maxIterations: 1 })`, polls for the fixture-ready file, calls `ac.abort()` (FIRST observed terminal trigger — the listener pins `firstObservedRef.trigger = "abort"` AT ENTRY and schedules the abort-listener pause), polls for the parent-observable abort-listener marker (existence implies the seam paused at entry to the dispatch path), reads the script's PID from the PID marker, sends `SIGUSR1` to the script's process group (`process.kill(-pid, "SIGUSR1")`) so the racing iteration error fires while loopx is still paused. Awaits the promise inside try/catch capturing `errName` / `errMessage`. Writes JSON envelope `{ errName, errMessage }`. Asserts: (a) `envelope.errName === "AbortError"` AND `envelope.errMessage` does NOT match `/exited with code/` (load-bearing — a buggy wrapper.next() catch that surfaced the iteration error directly without consulting `firstObservedRef` would shift this), (b) exactly one `LOOPX_TEST_CLEANUP_WARNING\t…` line on stderr (per-run cardinality holds across racing triggers — `CleanupState.attempted` deduplicates; load-bearing: a buggy implementation that started a second cleanup attempt on the racing iteration error would emit a second warning), (c) regular-file at the recorded tmpdir path with content `regular-file-replacement` survives.
  - **T-TMP-38b2-run** (run surface): same fixture, driver code drives `for await (const _ of run("ralph", { signal: ac.signal, maxIterations: 1 }))` in an async IIFE that captures any thrown error into `errName` / `errMessage`, otherwise mirrors the runPromise variant (poll fixture-ready, abort, poll pause marker, send SIGUSR1, await iterPromise). Asserts: same shape as T-TMP-38b2 — verifies that a buggy implementation that wired the abort-listener seam correctly on `runPromise` rejection but routed `run()` settlement through a different first-observed dispatcher would fail this counterpart.

### ADR-0004 §7.4 (T-TMP-42b — cleanup-fault warning does not mask abort terminal × programmatic surfaces) — RESOLVED

SPEC §7.4 final paragraph: "warnings do not affect the CLI exit code, the generator outcome, or the promise rejection reason." The cleanup-warning-does-not-affect-outcome contract holds for both the cleanup-safety warning branch and the cleanup-failure warning branch on every terminal type. Coverage matrix entries previously pinned: T-TMP-35g/35h (cleanup-safety × abort × programmatic surfaces), T-TMP-40/41/42 + 40a/40b/41a/41b/42d/42e (cleanup-failure × success × all three surfaces), T-TMP-42a (cleanup-failure × script-error × all three surfaces), T-TMP-42c (cleanup-failure × CLI signal terminal). T-TMP-42b closes the remaining missing diagonal: cleanup-failure warning × abort terminal × programmatic surfaces (abort is programmatic-only). A buggy implementation that promoted the cleanup-failure warning to a cleanup-failure-class rejection in place of the abort error — an implementation-defect mode that would still pass the cleanup-SAFETY counterpart (T-TMP-35g/35h) — would fail T-TMP-42b's first assertion.

The implementation in `runLoop` (`packages/loop-extender/src/loop.ts:120-217`) and the `run.ts` wrapper / signal-listener wiring (`packages/loop-extender/src/run.ts:307-348`) already conformed: the iteration body wraps in `try/finally` so `cleanupTmpdir(tmpdirResource, cleanupState)` runs before any abort error propagates out of the generator. The cleanup-fault seam (`LOOPX_TEST_CLEANUP_FAULT={lstat-fail, symlink-unlink-fail, recursive-remove-fail}` in `tmpdir.ts:184-279`) fires inside `cleanupTmpdir` and emits via `emitCleanupWarning` which writes to stderr but never rewrites the in-flight throw value.

Now-passing tests (this iteration):
- **tmpdir.test.ts: 553/553 PASS** — added 12 tests (3 cleanup-fault seams × 2 programmatic surfaces × 2 runtimes):
  - **T-TMP-42b (lstat-fail / symlink-unlink-fail / recursive-remove-fail) [runPromise]**: bash fixture observes `LOOPX_TMPDIR` into an external marker, performs the seam-specific path manipulation if needed (for `symlink-unlink-fail`: `rm -rf "$LOOPX_TMPDIR" && ln -s /tmp "$LOOPX_TMPDIR"` so dispatch reaches rule 2; for `recursive-remove-fail`: writes a few files inside the tmpdir so dispatch reaches rule 4 on a non-empty identity-matched directory; for `lstat-fail`: no path manipulation, the seam fires on the top-level `lstat`), writes its PID to a separate marker, then blocks indefinitely. Driver code (run via `runAPIDriver`) creates an `AbortController`, kicks off `runPromise("ralph", { signal: c.signal })`, polls for both markers, calls `c.abort()` from the harness, awaits the rejection capturing `errName` / `errMessage`, then waits up to 10s for the script's PID to exit (probed via `process.kill(pid, 0)` returning ESRCH). Asserts: (a) promise rejected with abort error (`errName === "AbortError"` or `/abort/i.test(errMsg)`) and message does NOT contain "cleanup" — load-bearing — a buggy implementation that promoted the cleanup-failure warning to a cleanup-failure-class rejection in place of the abort error would shift `errName` and add "cleanup" to the message, (b) exactly one `LOOPX_TEST_CLEANUP_WARNING\t…` line on stderr (per-run cleanup-warning cardinality holds under the abort terminal × cleanup-failure branch), (c) child PG terminated per SPEC §9.1 / §9.5 — abort-driven process-group termination still applies under the cleanup-failure branch, (d) path persistence per fault seam (lstat-fail: identity-matched directory remains; symlink-unlink-fail: symlink remains; recursive-remove-fail: directory remains).
  - **T-TMP-42b (lstat-fail / symlink-unlink-fail / recursive-remove-fail) [run]**: same fixture, driver code creates an `AbortController` and drives `const gen = run("ralph", { signal: c.signal }); const nextP = gen.next();` (`nextP.catch(() => {})` to avoid unhandled rejection) then polls for both markers, calls `c.abort()`, awaits `nextP` capturing `thrown` / `errName` / `errMessage`. Same assertion shape as runPromise variant. Verifies a buggy implementation that wired the cleanup-failure-warning-does-not-affect-outcome contract correctly on `runPromise` rejection but routed `run()` settlement through a different cleanup-dispatcher would fail this counterpart.
- Adjacent suites: zero regressions across programmatic-api + env-vars + wfdir + loop-state + execution (635/635), signals (9/9), unit + harness (158/158). Full tmpdir.test.ts run: 553/553 in ~157s.

### ADR-0004 §7.2 / §7.4 / §9.3 (T-TMP-38d / T-TMP-38d4 — first-observed-wins for racing post-final-yield abort → .throw() / .return() during abort-listener) — RESOLVED

Closing two of the four post-final-yield consumer-cancellation × abort race quadrants on the warning-cardinality axis. T-TMP-38d (the `.throw()` axis) and T-TMP-38d4 (the `.return()` axis) cover the abort-FIRST observation order; T-TMP-38d2 (`.throw()`-first × abort-second) and T-TMP-38d3 (`.return()`-first × abort-second) cover the inverted order. Together the four IDs close the full {`.return()` / `.throw()`} × {abort-first / consumer-first} 2×2 matrix on the post-final-yield surface.

Per SPEC §9.3's abort-after-final-yield rule, when abort is observed first after the final yield (before generator settlement), the abort outcome displaces normal completion regardless of which consumer cancellation later races against it. Equivalent contract to T-API-66b / T-API-66e (abort-first × `.return()` / `.throw()` post-final-yield outcome-axis tests), but driven through the `abort-listener` pause race rather than direct interaction sequencing — pinning the warning-cardinality axis on the same race.

The implementation in `packages/loop-extender/src/run.ts` ALREADY conformed: when `firstObservedRef.trigger === "abort"` is set (which the user-signal listener pins at entry, BEFORE the abort-listener seam pause begins), the wrapper's `.return()` / `.throw()` post-final-yield branch (lines 397-404 / 450-458 / 518-526) jumps to `surfacePostFinalYieldAbort` synchronously, drives the inner gen's finally (cleanup runs once with rule-3 warning), and throws AbortError. The abort-listener seam itself was wired in the T-TMP-38b2 iteration; this iteration verifies that the post-final-yield code paths participate correctly.

The `abort-listener` seam (rather than `cleanup-start` or `consumer-throw-observed`) is essential here per TEST-SPEC §1.4: SPEC §7.4 does NOT forbid an opportunistic implementation from running cleanup after the final yield but before settlement, so a `cleanup-start` pause cannot reliably coordinate this race. The `abort-listener` seam fires deterministically when `c.abort()` is delivered, regardless of whether the implementation had also opportunistically begun cleanup before the abort arrived.

Now-passing tests (this iteration):
- **tmpdir.test.ts: 561/561 PASS** — added 8 tests (2 IDs × 2 variants × 2 runtimes):
  - **T-TMP-38d (stop) / T-TMP-38d (maxIterations)**: bash fixture (rule-3 regular-file replacement) emits final yield then exits 0. Variant (stop) emits `{"stop":true}` + `maxIterations: 5`; variant (maxIterations) emits raw `{}` (parses as `{ result: "{}" }` per SPEC §2.3 raw-fallback) + `maxIterations: 1`. Driver code (run via `runAPIDriver`) creates an `AbortController`, calls `await gen.next()` to consume the final yield (asserts `first.value.stop === true` for stop variant or `first.done === false` for maxIterations variant), calls `ac.abort()` FIRST (pins `firstObservedRef.trigger = "abort"` + schedules abort-listener seam pause), polls the parent-observable abort-listener marker, then calls `gen.throw(new Error("test-throw"))` during the bounded pause, awaits the throwPromise (captures rejection in try/catch). Asserts: (a) `envelope.errName === "AbortError"` AND `envelope.errMessage` does NOT match `/test-throw/` AND `envelope.throwDone === false` (load-bearing: a buggy wrapper that surfaced the consumer-thrown error or a clean settlement would shift these); (b) exactly one `LOOPX_TEST_CLEANUP_WARNING\t…` line on stderr; (c) rule-3 regular-file replacement at the recorded path survives.
  - **T-TMP-38d4 (stop) / T-TMP-38d4 (maxIterations)**: same fixture, same observation order. Driver code calls `gen.return(undefined)` instead of `gen.throw(...)` during the abort-listener pause, awaits the returnPromise. Asserts: (a) `envelope.errName === "AbortError"` AND `envelope.returnDone === false` (load-bearing: a buggy wrapper that surfaced a clean `.return()` settlement would shift these); (b) exactly one cleanup warning; (c) rule-3 file persists.
- Adjacent suites: zero regressions across programmatic-api + env-vars + wfdir + loop-state + execution (635/635), signals (9/9), unit + harness + typecheck (172/172). Full tmpdir.test.ts run: 561/561 in ~182s.

### ADR-0004 §7.2 / §7.4 (T-TMP-38e / T-TMP-38e-run — child-spawn-failure × abort cleanup idempotence on programmatic surfaces) — RESOLVED

Closing the child-spawn-failure × abort race quadrants on the cleanup-idempotence + warning-cardinality axes. Two race configurations are exercised: variant (a) the spawn failure is observed FIRST (script-failure shape iteration outcome wins, racing abort does not displace), variant (b) the abort is observed FIRST (abort outcome wins, racing post-abort spawn failure does not displace). Both variants are run on both programmatic surfaces (`runPromise()` and `run()`) on both runtimes (node, bun) — 2 IDs × 2 variants × 2 runtimes = 8 tests.

Implementation iteration. Two new TEST-SPEC §1.4 seam windows wired in `packages/loop-extender/src/execution.ts`:
- **`child-spawn-attempt`**: pause window placed BEFORE the `spawn()` call. Used by variant (b) — the harness aborts during this pause window, BEFORE any spawn syscall has executed, so the abort can be pinned as first-observed.
- **`child-spawn-failure`**: pause window placed AFTER catching the synchronous spawn rejection (NUL-byte-in-env triggers a synchronous throw from `child_process.spawn` because Node validates env-pair byte content before invoking the syscall) AND alongside the async `'error'` event handler for spawn failures discovered after fork. Used by variant (a) — `firstObservedRef.trigger` is pinned to `"iteration"` BEFORE entering the seam pause so a racing abort delivered during the pause cannot displace the spawn-failure outcome.

Two new fields threaded through `ExecOptions`: `firstObservedRef?: FirstObservedRef` (the same shared trigger-tracking slot already used by `runLoop` and `run.ts`'s wrapper), so `executeScript` can pin `trigger = "iteration"` when null at spawn-failure observation. Both the synchronous spawn throw (NUL-in-env path) and the async `'error'` event handler pin first-observed BEFORE the seam pause runs, so any racing abort delivered during the bounded pause cannot retroactively claim first-observed.

A new gate added to `runLoop`'s `abortPromise` in `loop.ts`: when `firstObservedRef.trigger === "iteration"`, the abort listener does NOT reject the abortPromise that participates in the per-iteration `Promise.race`. This is load-bearing — without the gate, a racing abort observed AFTER the spawn-failure was pinned as iteration-first would still reject the abortPromise, and the race in `runLoop` would resolve to the abort-error rejection rather than letting the iteration error propagate as the surfaced terminal outcome. The gate preserves the spawn-failure-first contract by ensuring the iteration error is what reaches the wrapper's catch.

A synthetic `onAbort` dispatch is performed at child-listener-attach time when `signal.aborted` is already true: this ensures variant (b) — where the abort fired during the `child-spawn-attempt` pause BEFORE the spawn() call — still terminates the active child if `spawn()` succeeded after the pause resumed. Without the synthetic dispatch, the abort listener attached AFTER spawn would never fire, leaving the just-spawned child unkilled.

Cleanup-warning is induced via `LOOPX_TEST_CLEANUP_FAULT=recursive-remove-fail` so rule-4 cleanup (the empty tmpdir loopx created) emits the SPEC §7.4 warning. Without this fault, cleanup of the empty tmpdir succeeds warning-free, and the cardinality assertion (`exactly one cleanup warning`) cannot distinguish a single-attempt from a double-attempt code path. The cleanup-fault seam reliably emits one warning per `cleanupTmpdir` invocation, so `count === 1` proves cleanup ran exactly once across the racing trigger pair (single-attempt code path) while `count === 2+` would catch a regression where each trigger independently invoked cleanup.

Now-passing tests (this iteration):
- **tmpdir.test.ts: 569/569 PASS** — added 8 tests (2 IDs × 2 variants × 2 runtimes):
  - **T-TMP-38e (variant a, variant b) [runPromise]**: variant (a) sets `LOOPX_TEST_TERMINAL_TRIGGER_PAUSE=child-spawn-failure` + a NUL-in-env value, awaits `runPromise(...)` with a signal whose `c.abort()` is delivered during the pause; asserts the rejection has script-failure shape (NOT AbortError) and exactly one cleanup warning, tmpdir cleaned once. Variant (b) sets `LOOPX_TEST_TERMINAL_TRIGGER_PAUSE=child-spawn-attempt`, calls `c.abort()` during the spawn-attempt pause BEFORE spawn fires; asserts AbortError rejection and exactly one cleanup warning.
  - **T-TMP-38e-run (variant a, variant b) [run]**: same race configurations driven through the `run()` generator surface, with `gen.next().catch(() => {})` to defer rejection observation, polling for the parent-observable pause marker, then `c.abort()`. Same assertion shape per variant.
- Adjacent suites: zero regressions across programmatic-api + env-vars + wfdir + loop-state + execution (635/635 e2e), signals (9/9), unit + harness (158/158).

### ADR-0004 §9.3 / §9.1 (T-API-66/66a/66b/66c/66d/66e — abort-after-final-yield outcome-axis on the API surface) — RESOLVED

SPEC §9.3 second paragraph: "Abort observed after the final yield but before the generator settles produces the abort error on the next generator interaction — `g.next()`, `.return()`, or `.throw()`." The "final yield" is triggered by either `maxIterations`-reached OR a script-emitted `stop: true`; the rule applies symmetrically across both triggers and across all three settle-triggering interactions. For `.throw()`, the abort error displaces the consumer-supplied error per SPEC §9.3 (signal wins).

The cleanup-ORDERING-axis tests (T-TMP-23/24a/24c/24d/24e/24f/24g in tmpdir.test.ts) already pin the contract that tmpdir is removed BEFORE the abort error surfaces. The OUTCOME axis (the abort error is the surfaced rejection at all — vs silent `{ done: true }` settlement, and the abort error displaces a concurrent consumer-supplied error in `.throw()`) was unpinned on the API surface until this iteration. A buggy implementation that ran cleanup correctly but then resolved silently `{ done: true }` on the post-final-yield interaction (or that allowed `.throw()`'s consumer-error to surface in place of the abort error) would pass the T-TMP series yet fail T-API-66/66a/66b/66c/66d/66e. The two families are complementary — neither subsumes the other.

The implementation in `packages/loop-extender/src/run.ts` already conformed: each of `wrapper.next()` (line 398-403), `wrapper.return()` (line 451-457), and `wrapper.throw()` (line 519-525) carries a `if (postFinalYield && firstObservedRef.trigger === "abort" && ...) await surfacePostFinalYieldAbort();` branch that drives `gen.return(undefined)` to run the inner runLoop's try/finally (cleanup) before throwing `makeAbortError(...)`. The `firstObservedRef.trigger === "abort"` check (introduced for T-TMP-38b2 to decouple first-observed determination from `internalAc.signal.aborted`) is pinned by the user-signal listener at entry, so a `c.abort()` call before the second interaction sets it synchronously. Test-only iteration; no implementation changes required.

Now-passing tests (this iteration):
- **programmatic-api.test.ts: 370/370 PASS** — added 12 tests (6 IDs × 2 runtimes) under a new `SPEC: Abort After Final Yield` describe block:
  - **T-API-66 (`.next()`, maxIterations: 1)**: bash fixture emits `{"result":"ok"}`. Driver: `await gen.next()` (final yield), `c.abort()`, `await gen.next()` → expect rejection. Asserts (a) `firstDone === false`, (b) `firstHasValue === true`, (c) result is rejection with `name === "AbortError" || /abort/i.test(msg)` (load-bearing — silent `{ done: true }` would shift `result.kind` to `"resolved"`).
  - **T-API-66a (`.return()`, maxIterations: 1)**: same fixture; driver swaps `gen.return(undefined)` for the second interaction. Asserts rejection with abort-error shape (load-bearing — pre-§9.3 wrapper would have settled `{ done: true, value: undefined }` silently per the consumer-cancellation contract).
  - **T-API-66b (`.throw()`, maxIterations: 1)**: same fixture; driver swaps `gen.throw(new Error("consumer-err"))`. Asserts rejection with abort-error shape AND `msg !== "consumer-err"` (load-bearing — abort displaces consumer-supplied error per SPEC §9.3 final paragraph).
  - **T-API-66c (`.next()`, stop:true / maxIterations: 5)**: bash fixture emits `{"stop":true}`. Driver verifies `first.value.stop === true` then aborts and calls `.next()`. Asserts rejection with abort-error shape (load-bearing — a buggy implementation that recognized "final yield" only via `maxIterations`-reached and treated `stop:true` as a separate "settle silently" path that bypassed abort-precedence would silently resolve `{ done: true }` and fail).
  - **T-API-66d (`.return()`, stop:true / maxIterations: 5)**: same fixture; `.return()` axis. Asserts rejection.
  - **T-API-66e (`.throw()`, stop:true / maxIterations: 5)**: same fixture; `.throw()` axis with consumer-supplied error. Asserts rejection AND `msg !== "consumer-err"`.
- Adjacent suites: zero regressions across tmpdir (561), env-vars (96), wfdir (40), signals (9), loop-state (96), execution (45), unit (143), harness (15), typecheck OK. Full programmatic-api.test.ts run: 370/370 in ~47s.

### ADR-0004 §9.5 / §9.1 / §9.2 (T-API-53/53a/53b/53c/53d/53e/53f/53g + T-API-54/54a/54b/54c/54d/54e/54f/54g/54h + T-API-55 — RunOptions.env invalid-shape matrix on both API surfaces) — RESOLVED

SPEC §9.5 contract: `RunOptions.env` must be a non-null, non-array, non-function object whose own enumerable string-keyed entries all have string values. Any of: invalid object types, non-string entry values, snapshot-time throws — surface as option-snapshot errors via the standard pre-iteration error path: throwing on the first generator `next()` under `run()`, or rejecting the returned promise under `runPromise()`. The T-API-53/54/55 series pin the contract on both API surfaces across the full SPEC §9.5 invalid-`env` enumeration.

The implementation in `packages/loop-extender/src/run.ts` (`snapshotEnv` at lines 72-103, called from `snapshotOptions` at line 202) ALREADY conformed: rejects null / arrays / functions / non-objects (covering string, number, boolean, symbol, bigint via the `typeof !== "object"` arm); enumerates own-enumerable string-keyed entries via `Object.keys`; reads each value once via `[[Get]]` semantics; rejects any non-string value (covering number, undefined, null, object, function, boolean, symbol, bigint) with `TypeError("RunOptions.env[…] must be a string, got <type>")`. Captured errors surface via the standard pre-iteration error path (`snap.error` populates and is thrown lazily on first `next()` for `run()` or rejects the promise under `runPromise`). Test-only iteration; no implementation changes required.

Now-passing tests (this iteration):
- **programmatic-api.test.ts: 482/482 PASS** (was 418, +64) — added 64 tests under a new `SPEC: RunOptions.env Invalid Shape` describe block (32 IDs × 2 runtimes; the run/runPromise pairs live as separate IDs):
  - **T-API-53 / 53a / 53b / 53c / 53d / 53e / 53f / 53g (run() — whole-env primitives)**: 8 IDs × 2 runtimes = 16 tests. Parameterized variants for env: null / array / function / string / number / boolean / Symbol / bigint. Each asserts (a) `gen.next()` throws, (b) error message matches `/env|RunOptions/i`, (c) no spawn occurred (marker file absent). The boolean / symbol / bigint arms (53e/53f/53g) catch a buggy implementation that gated whole-env rejection on a partial primitive enumeration that omitted `typeof !== "object"`.
  - **T-API-54 / 54a / 54b / 54c / 54f / 54g / 54h (run() — entry-value primitives)**: 7 IDs × 2 runtimes = 14 tests. Parameterized variants for non-string entry value: number / undefined / null / object / boolean / symbol / bigint. Each asserts (a) throw, (b) error matches `/env|MYVAR|string/i`, (c) no spawn. The boolean / symbol / bigint arms (54f/54g/54h) catch a buggy implementation that gated entry-value rejection on `typeof !== "number"` instead of `typeof !== "string"`.
  - **T-API-54d (run() — accessor returning non-string)**: 1 ID × 2 runtimes = 2 tests. Constructs env via `Object.defineProperty(env, "KEY", { enumerable: true, get() { return 42; } })` — never via object spread (which would invoke the getter in the test harness before run() is called). Asserts the [[Get]]-semantics value-read identifies the non-string return value and throws an option-snapshot error. Catches a buggy implementation using descriptor-based extraction (`descriptor.value` is undefined on accessor properties) that would either capture undefined or skip validation entirely.
  - **T-API-54e (runPromise() — accessor returning non-string)**: 1 ID × 2 runtimes = 2 tests. Same accessor construction as T-API-54d on the runPromise() surface; asserts the promise rejects.
  - **T-API-55 (runPromise() — full invalid-shape matrix)**: 15 variants × 2 runtimes = 30 tests. Parameterized across all 8 whole-env primitive variants AND all 7 entry-value primitive variants. Each asserts (a) promise rejects, (b) error matches `/env|MYVAR|RunOptions|string/i`, (c) no spawn. Closes the runPromise() surface counterpart for both invalid-shape branches.
- Adjacent suites: zero regressions across env-vars (96) + wfdir (40) → 136/136. Typecheck OK. Full programmatic-api.test.ts run: 482/482 in ~61s.

### ADR-0004 §9.5 / §8.3 (T-API-50/50a/50b/50c/50d/50e/50h — RunOptions.env basic injection across iteration / goto / loop-reset / value-shape contract) — RESOLVED

SPEC §9.5 / §8.3 contract: `RunOptions.env` entries are injected into every spawned script's environment, applying uniformly to the starting target, intra- and cross-workflow `goto` destinations, and loop resets. Entries merge in tier 2 of §8.3's precedence chain (after global env file, after local env file, after inherited `process.env`; before protocol-tier `LOOPX_*` vars). The contract has been load-bearing for the §9.5 RunOptions.env-tier-2-env-merging implementation (now in `run.ts` + `types.ts`) since that landed; T-API-50 series pins the externally-observable end-to-end contract on the API surface that the implementation actually reaches every spawn point and propagates the value byte-for-byte.

The implementation in `packages/loop-extender/src/run.ts` (`snapshotEnv` + `runInternal` env merging) and `packages/loop-extender/src/execution.ts` (env injection at spawn time) ALREADY conformed: `mergeEnv(globalEnv, localEnv)` overlaid with `snap.env` then protocol vars at execution time produces the spec'd precedence; the merged env is computed once per call (eager-snapshot under `runPromise`, lazy under `run`) and passed to every `executeScript` invocation regardless of which workflow / script the iteration targets. Test-only iteration; no implementation changes required.

Now-passing tests (this iteration):
- **programmatic-api.test.ts: 384/384 PASS** — added 14 tests (7 IDs × 2 runtimes) under a new `SPEC: RunOptions.env Basic Injection` describe block:
  - **T-API-50 (runPromise)**: bash fixture writes `present\\t<value>` or `absent` to a marker depending on whether `MYVAR` is set (using `${MYVAR+x}` parameter expansion to distinguish set-but-empty from unset). Driver `runPromise("ralph", { env: { MYVAR: "hello" }, maxIterations: 1 })`. Asserts (a) one Output, (b) marker = `present\\thello` (load-bearing — `absent` would catch a regression where the env never propagated; `present\\t<wrong>` would catch a regression where the value was mangled).
  - **T-API-50a (run, multi-iteration)**: bash fixture increments a counter, writes `iter<N>.txt` with `MYVAR` value, stops after 2 iterations. Driver drives `for await` with `maxIterations: 3` (final stop:true caps actual iterations at 2). Asserts both iter1 and iter2 markers contain "shared" — load-bearing for "applies to every iteration" rule.
  - **T-API-50b (run, intra-workflow goto)**: `ralph:index` writes `index.txt` with MYVAR then gotos `ralph:check`; `ralph:check` writes `check.txt` and emits stop:true. Asserts both markers contain "intra" — load-bearing for "applies across goto destinations" within a single workflow.
  - **T-API-50c (run, cross-workflow goto)**: `alpha:index` writes `alpha.txt` with MYVAR then gotos `beta:step`; `beta:step` writes `beta.txt` and emits stop:true. Asserts both markers contain "cross" — load-bearing for "applies across cross-workflow goto" — a buggy implementation that re-resolved env from a per-workflow context would fail this.
  - **T-API-50d (run, loop reset)**: `ralph:index` increments a counter, writes `run<N>.txt`, returns plain output (no goto, no stop) on iteration 1 — triggering loop reset back to `ralph:index` for iteration 2 (counter = 2 → emits stop:true). Asserts both markers contain "reset" — load-bearing for "applies across loop reset" — a buggy implementation that bound env to the initial spawn rather than the call-time snapshot might fail to propagate after reset.
  - **T-API-50e (runPromise, empty-string value)**: same `${MYVAR+x}` set-vs-empty distinction fixture, driver passes `env: { MYVAR: "" }`. Asserts marker = `present\\t` (set, empty) — load-bearing — a buggy implementation that filtered empty-string values as "unset" would produce `absent`.
  - **T-API-50h (runPromise + run, tricky non-NUL values)**: bash fixture iterates over 11 keys (V_SPACES, V_EQ, V_HASH, V_DQ, V_SQ, V_BS, V_UTF, V_LF, V_CRLF, V_TAB, V_WSONLY) using bash indirect expansion `${!key}` and writes each value to `<key>.txt`. Driver passes a payload covering whitespace (leading/trailing/only), embedded `=`, comment-prefix `#`, double quotes, single quotes, backslashes, UTF-8 + emoji, LF, CRLF, TAB, whitespace-only. Asserts each marker matches the original payload byte-for-byte across BOTH `runPromise()` and `run()` surfaces — load-bearing for "RunOptions.env is NOT subject to env-file parser normalization" — a buggy implementation that ran the values through the §8.1 `parseEnvFile` normalization (stripping leading whitespace, treating `#` as comment, treating `=` as separator) would fail many of these.

### ADR-0004 §9.5 / §9.1 / §9.2 (T-API-52/52a/52b/52c/52d/52e/52e2/52f — RunOptions.env snapshot semantics) — RESOLVED

SPEC §9.5 second paragraph (Lifetime): "Entries are captured synchronously at call time as a shallow copy — loopx reads the supplied object's own enumerable string-keyed properties once. The capture runs at the `run()` / `runPromise()` call site …". The contract has multiple structurally-distinct branches that need pinning down independently:
- **Outer-property mutation axis**: post-call value mutation × post-call key-set mutation × both API surfaces. Buggy implementations that held a live reference to the supplied object instead of a snapshot would observably surface post-call mutations to spawned scripts.
- **Per-entry getter axis**: accessor-property values read via `[[Get]]` semantics exactly once at call time, not lazily at first `next()` and not re-invoked per spawn. T-API-52/52a/52b cover plain-object snapshots only — they do not catch a regression where an implementation deferred entry-getter reads to first `next()` (or re-invoked them per spawn) on accessor-defined keys.
- **Proxy trap axis**: `ownKeys` and `get` traps invoked exactly the spec'd number of times at call time. T-API-52c/52d cover the per-entry-getter axis but not the proxy enumeration axis. T-API-62f/62f3 cover the throwing-trap failure path, but a successful proxy must also be enumerated and value-read exactly once.

The implementation in `packages/loop-extender/src/run.ts` (`snapshotEnv` at lines 72-103, called synchronously inside `snapshotOptions` at lines 192-207, called synchronously at the head of `runWithInternal` at line 267) ALREADY conforms: `Object.keys(envRaw)` enumerates own-enumerable string-keyed properties exactly once (which invokes the proxy `ownKeys` trap once and the `getOwnPropertyDescriptor` trap an implementation-defined number of times per SPEC §9.5); `(envRaw)[key]` invokes `[[Get]]` semantics once per included key (proxy `get` trap or accessor getter); the result `out: Record<string, string>` is a freshly-allocated shallow copy detached from the original object. `runPromise` (lines 732-783) calls `runWithInternal` synchronously before its `await Promise.resolve()` microtask boundary, preserving eager-snapshot semantics on the eager surface. Test-only iteration; no implementation changes required.

Now-passing tests (this iteration):
- **programmatic-api.test.ts: 418/418 PASS** (was 398, +20) — added 20 tests (10 IDs × 2 runtimes) under a new `SPEC: RunOptions.env Snapshot Semantics` describe block:
  - **T-API-52 (runPromise — value mutation post-call)**: bash fixture observes MYVAR. Driver: `const e = { MYVAR: "initial" }; const p = runPromise("ralph", { env: e, maxIterations: 1 }); e.MYVAR = "mutated"; await p;` Asserts marker = `"initial"` — load-bearing — a buggy implementation that held a live reference would surface `"mutated"`.
  - **T-API-52a (run — added key post-call)**: bash fixture observes both MYVAR (`${MYVAR+x}` set-vs-empty) and NEWVAR. Driver: `const e = { MYVAR: "initial" }; const gen = run("ralph", { env: e, maxIterations: 1 }); e.NEWVAR = "added"; for await (const o of gen) {}` Asserts MYVAR marker = `"present\tinitial"` and NEWVAR marker = `"absent"` — the shallow snapshot captured initial keys; post-call key addition is not observed.
  - **T-API-52b (run — value mutation between call and first next())**: same single-key fixture. Driver: `const e = { MYVAR: "A" }; const gen = run("ralph", { env: e, maxIterations: 1 }); e.MYVAR = "B"; for await (const o of gen) {}` Asserts marker = `"A"` — proves snapshot is taken at `run()` call site, NOT at first `next()` (would surface `"B"` on lazy-snapshot implementation).
  - **T-API-52c (run — accessor getter call-time eager + no per-spawn re-read)**: `Object.defineProperty(env, "MYVAR", { enumerable: true, configurable: true, get() { count += 1; return backing; } });` Driver captures `count` at three points: after `run()` returns (before any `next()`), after backing-state mutation (`backing = "mutated"`), after `for await` settlement. Asserts countAfterRun=1 (proves eager call-time snapshot), countAfterMutate=1 (frozen — backing-state mutation does not re-invoke), countAfterSettle=1 (no per-spawn re-read), marker = `"initial"`.
  - **T-API-52d (runPromise — accessor getter call-time eager + reused across iterations)**: same accessor; multi-iteration fixture (3 iterations, per-iteration markers). Driver captures `count` at runPromise() call point, after backing mutation, after promise resolution. Asserts countAfterCall=1 (eager call-time), countAfterMutate=1 (frozen), countAfterResolve=1 (no per-spawn re-read across 3 iterations), all three iter markers = `"initial"`.
  - **T-API-52e (run + runPromise — proxy ownKeys+get traps call-time + no per-spawn re-read)**: proxy with custom `ownKeys`, default `getOwnPropertyDescriptor`, custom `get`. Two-key target `{ MYVAR, OTHERVAR }`. 3-iteration fixture. Driver captures trap counts at call site and after settlement. Asserts on each surface: ownKeysAfterCall=1 (call-time enumeration once); ownKeysAfterDone=ownKeysAfterCall (no re-enumeration per spawn); getAfterCall=2 (one [[Get]] per included string key); per-key valueGetSnapshot=1 each; getAfterDone=getAfterCall + per-key counts unchanged (no per-spawn value-re-read); 3 outputs, all 6 markers (3 iter × 2 vars) record snapshot values.
  - **T-API-52e2 (runPromise — descriptor-only proxy)**: only `getOwnPropertyDescriptor` is custom-trapped. SPEC §9.5 leaves descriptor-call cardinality implementation-defined; asserts only descAfterDone === descAfterCall (no per-spawn re-invocation), 3 iter markers all record snapshot values.
  - **T-API-52e2 (runPromise — get-only proxy)**: only `get` is custom-trapped. Asserts getAfterCall=2 (one [[Get]] per included key per SPEC §9.5 normative contract), per-key valueGetSnapshot=1, getAfterDone=getAfterCall (no per-spawn re-read), per-key counts unchanged, 3 iter markers record snapshot values.
  - **T-API-52f (runPromise — added key post-call)**: same two-marker fixture as T-API-52a but on the eager surface. Driver: `const e = { MYVAR: "initial" }; const p = runPromise("ralph", { env: e, maxIterations: 1 }); e.NEWVAR = "added"; await p;` Asserts MYVAR marker = `"present\tinitial"`, NEWVAR marker = `"absent"` — closes the post-call-key-addition axis on the runPromise() surface (T-API-52d/52e cover call-time enumeration cardinality but not post-call additions).
- Adjacent suites: zero regressions across tmpdir (569/569), env-vars + wfdir + loop-state (232/232), signals (9/9), unit + harness (158/158), typecheck OK. Full programmatic-api.test.ts run: 418/418 in ~54s.

### ADR-0004 §9.5 / §8.3 / §13 / §7.4 (T-API-51a/51a2/51b/51c/51d/51e/51f — RunOptions.env precedence chain) — RESOLVED

SPEC §8.3 precedence chain (highest wins): (1) protocol vars `LOOPX_*` (applied at execution time), (2) `RunOptions.env`, (3) local env file (`-e` / `RunOptions.envFile`), (4) global loopx env (`$XDG_CONFIG_HOME/loopx/env`), (5) inherited `process.env`. SPEC §9.5: `RunOptions.env` entries override same-named values from `-e`, the global env file, and inherited `process.env`, and are overridden by protocol variables. SPEC §13: protocol variables silently override user-supplied values (no warning / notice on stderr). The T-API-51 series pins each precedence boundary on the API surface: tier-2 vs tier-1 (51a / 51a2), tier-2 vs tier-3 (51b), tier-2 vs tier-4 (51c), tier-2 vs tier-5 (51d), and the full chain (51e for runPromise, 51f for run).

The implementation in `packages/loop-extender/src/run.ts` (`runInternal` env merging at line 661-664: `{ ...mergeEnv(globalEnv, localEnv, inheritedEnv), ...(snap.env ?? {}) }`) and `packages/loop-extender/src/execution.ts` (protocol-var overlay at line 179-185: `{ ...env, LOOPX_BIN, LOOPX_PROJECT_ROOT, LOOPX_WORKFLOW, LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR, LOOPX_TMPDIR }`) ALREADY conformed: `mergeEnv` produces tiers 5→4→3, `snap.env` overlays tier 2, protocol vars overlay tier 1 last per the documented comment block at run.ts:652-660. The silent-override contract holds because no override-warning code exists for any LOOPX_* name. Test-only iteration; no implementation changes required.

Now-passing tests (this iteration):
- **programmatic-api.test.ts: 398/398 PASS** (was 384, +14) — added 14 tests (7 IDs × 2 runtimes) under a new `SPEC: RunOptions.env Precedence` describe block:
  - **T-API-51a (runPromise) / T-API-51a2 (run)**: bash fixture observes all five script-protocol-protected names (`LOOPX_BIN`, `LOOPX_PROJECT_ROOT`, `LOOPX_WORKFLOW`, `LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR`, `LOOPX_TMPDIR`) into per-name marker files, AND performs an in-script `[ -d "$LOOPX_TMPDIR" ]` stat (during execution — SPEC §7.4 cleanup runs after the script, so a post-run stat would observe absence) writing `is-dir` / `not-dir` to a stat marker. Driver passes `env: { LOOPX_WORKFLOW: "fake", LOOPX_PROJECT_ROOT: "/tmp/fake", LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR: "/tmp/fake-dir", LOOPX_TMPDIR: "/tmp/fake-tmp", LOOPX_BIN: "/tmp/fake-bin" }`. Asserts: (a) each marker records the real protocol value, NOT the user-supplied `/tmp/fake-*` value (load-bearing — a buggy implementation that spread `RunOptions.env` AFTER protocol vars instead of BEFORE would propagate the fake values); LOOPX_BIN marker is a real existing file; LOOPX_PROJECT_ROOT marker equals `realpathSync(project.dir)`; LOOPX_WORKFLOW marker equals `"ralph"`; LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR marker equals `join(realpathSync(project.dir), ".loopx", "ralph")`; LOOPX_TMPDIR marker matches `/\/loopx-[^/]+$/` (real loopx-created tmpdir per SPEC §7.4 mkdtemp naming convention `loopx-XXX`). (b) During-run stat marker records `"is-dir"` (load-bearing — proves LOOPX_TMPDIR points to a real loopx-created directory, not merely a substituted string; T-TMP-30 / T-TMP-31 rigor). (c) Stderr matches NO regex `<name>.*(override|overrid|ignored|warning|notice)` for any of the five names (load-bearing — a buggy implementation that emitted a "user-supplied LOOPX_* was overridden" diagnostic to flag the silent-override behavior would fail this even though (a) and (b) would pass).
  - **T-API-51b (runPromise — tier 2 vs tier 3)**: local `.env` at `<project>/.env` contains `MYVAR=from-file`; driver passes `envFile: ".env", env: { MYVAR: "from-options" }`. Asserts marker == `"from-options"` — load-bearing — a buggy implementation that merged `snap.env` BEFORE local-env-file overlay would surface `"from-file"`.
  - **T-API-51c (runPromise — tier 2 vs tier 4)**: temp `XDG_CONFIG_HOME` directory with `<xdg>/loopx/env` containing `MYVAR=from-global`; driver sets `process.env.XDG_CONFIG_HOME = <xdg>` then calls `runPromise("ralph", { env: { MYVAR: "from-options" } })`. Asserts marker == `"from-options"`. try/finally cleans up the temp xdg dir.
  - **T-API-51d (runPromise — tier 2 vs tier 5)**: driver sets `process.env.MYVAR = "inherited"` then calls `runPromise` with `env: { MYVAR: "from-options" }`. Asserts marker == `"from-options"`.
  - **T-API-51e (runPromise — full chain)**: configures all four lower tiers — `process.env.MYVAR = "1"` (tier 5), `process.env.XDG_CONFIG_HOME = <xdg>` with `MYVAR=2` (tier 4), local `.env` with `MYVAR=3` (tier 3), `RunOptions.env: { MYVAR: "4" }` (tier 2). MYVAR is not a protocol name so tier 1 doesn't apply. Asserts marker == `"4"` — load-bearing — any inverted overlay order would surface a different lower-tier value. try/finally cleans up the temp xdg dir.
  - **T-API-51f (run — full chain)**: same fixture as T-API-51e, driver consumes via `for await`. Verifies the run() generator surface routes the same merged env to every executeScript invocation (a buggy implementation that wired correct precedence on `runPromise` but routed `run()` through a different env-resolution path would fail this counterpart).
